Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in Salah is Wajib
Establishes Hanafi ruling that Fatihah is wajib, not fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting al-Fatihah in prayer, explain the distinction between fard and wajib, and apply the ruling to determine whether sujud al-sahw is required.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatihah is wajib — omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sujud al-sahw.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every obligation carries the same weight. Reciting Surah al-Fatihah in prayer is required, but it is classified as wajib, not fard. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind this ruling, clarifying the practical consequence: the prayer remains valid without it, but sujud al-sahw becomes necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard. Note that fard is established by definitive evidence, wajib by probable evidence.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the first set of evidences
The author presents proofs from Quran (73:20) and hadith that show reciting any Quran is fard, not specifically al-Fatihah. This supports the view that al-Fatihah is not a pillar.
These evidences show general obligation of qira'ah.
3
Analyze the specific proofs for wujub
The hadith 'la salata liman lam yaqra' bi Fatihah al-kitab' is cited. Understand the Hanafi interpretation: the negation indicates deficiency, not invalidity, thus wujub.
The same hadith is used by Shafi'is to argue for fard.
4
Understand the Hanafi usul principle
Apply the rule that 'la salata' can mean 'no perfect prayer' (nafy al-kamal) based on other evidences. This yields wujub, not fard.
This is a key example of how usul principles affect fiqh rulings.
5
Apply the consequence
If al-Fatihah is omitted, the prayer is valid but deficient; sujud al-sahw is wajib to compensate. Identify scenarios where sujud al-sahw is required.
Sujud al-sahw is performed before salam.

Source Text

فصل في واجبات الصلوة (۳۹۰) قرائة الفاتحة ( ۳۹۱) وضم السورة او ثلاث آيات فى ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض و جمه : (۳۹۰) [۱] سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا۔ تشریح : نماز میں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا ہمارے یہاں فرض نہیں ہے بلکہ واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) کہیں سے بھی قرآن پڑھنے کی فرضیت کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فاقرنوا ما تیسر من القرآن (آیت ۲۰ ،سورة المزمل ۷۳) (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن سعید قال امرنا ان نقرء بفاتحة الكتاب وما تيسر ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من ترك القراءة (الفاتحة) فی صلوته بفاتحۃ الکتاب، ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۸۱۸ / نسائی شریف ، باب ایجاب قراءة فاتحة الكتاب في الصلوۃ ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۱۹۱۲ ) (۳) بخاری شریف میں ہے آپ نے اس دیہاتی سے فرمایا جس نے جلدی جلدی نماز پڑھی ثم اقرء ما تيسر معک من القرآن (بخاری شریف، باب وجوب القرآ ةلا مام والمهاموم في الصلوة كلها ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۷۵۷ رمسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قرائۃ الفاتحۃ فی کل رکعتۃ ص ۱۷۰ نمبر ۸۸۵/۳۹۷) اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ قرآن میں سے جو آسان ہو اس کا پڑھنا فرض ہے۔ چاہے سورہ فاتحہ کے علاوہ ہو۔ (۴) حدثنی ابو هريرة قال : قال لى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اخرج فناد في المدينة أنه لا صلوة الا بقرآن و لو بفاتحة الكتاب فما زاد ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب من ترک القرآة في صلونة بفاتحة الكتاب ،ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۸۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ ہو یا کوئی اور آیت ہو اس سے نماز ہو جائے گی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فاتحہ پڑھنا فرض نہیں ہے، البتہ واجب ہم بھی کہتے ہیں۔ صلى الله سورة فاتحه واجب ھونے کی دليل: (۱) عن عبادة بن الصامت ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب - ( بخارى شريف، باب وجوب القراءة للامام والماموم في الصلوة كلها ص ۱۰۴ نمبر ۷۵۶ مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعته ،ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۷۴/۳۹۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ نہیں پڑھیں گے تو کمی رہ جائے گی ۔ حدیث میں ہے (۲) عن ابي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى صلوة صلى الله لم يقرأ فيها بام القرآن فهى خداج ثلاثا غير تمام مسلم شریف، باب وجوب قراءة الفاتحة في كل ركعة ، ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۷۸۷۸/۳۹۵ بو داؤد شریف، باب من ترک القراءة في صلوته، ص ۱۲۵، نمبر ۸۲۱) فهى خداج کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فاتحہ چھوڑنے سے نماز میں کمی رہ جائے گی اور اس کا اتمام سجدہ سہو سے کرنا پڑے گا۔ اسی لئے حنفیہ کے یہاں سورہ فاتحہ پڑھنا واجب ہے ، اور چھوڑنے سے نماز ہو جائے گی لیکن سجدہ سہو کرنا ہوگا۔
Chapter on Wajibat of Salah. (390) Recitation of al-Fatihah. (391) And adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of witr and nafl. [Summary: (390) [1] Reciting Surah al-Fatihah. Explanation: In our view, reciting Surah al-Fatihah in prayer is not fard but wajib. Evidence: (1) The proof for the obligation of reciting any part of the Quran is the verse: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' (Quran 73:20) (2) In a hadith: Ibn Sa'id said we were commanded to recite the Fatihah and what is easy. (Abu Dawud, Bab man taraka al-qira'ah bi Fatihah al-kitab fi salatihi, p.125, no.818; Nasa'i, Bab Ijab Qira'at Fatihah al-kitab fi al-salah, p.105, no.1912) (3) In Bukhari: The Prophet said to the bedouin who prayed hastily, 'Then recite what is easy from the Quran.' (Bukhari, Bab Wujub al-qira'ah li al-imam wa al-ma'mum fi al-salah kulliha, p.105, no.757; Muslim, Bab Wujub Qira'at al-Fatihah fi kulli rak'ah, p.170, no.885/397) This means that reciting what is easy from the Quran is fard, even if it is other than al-Fatihah. (4) Abu Hurairah narrated: The Prophet said, 'Proclaim in Madinah that there is no prayer except with Quran, even if with the Fatihah or more.' (Abu Dawud, Bab man taraka al-qira'ah fi salatihi bi fatihah al-kitab, p.126, no.819) This hadith shows that if one recites al-Fatihah or any other verse, the prayer is valid, indicating that reciting al-Fatihah is not fard, though we say it is wajib. Proof that al-Fatihah is wajib: (1) From Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet said, 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite the Fatihah.' (Bukhari, p.104, no.756; Muslim, p.169, no.874/394) This indicates reciting al-Fatihah is wajib; if omitted, deficiency remains. (2) From Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said, 'Whoever prays a prayer and does not recite Umm al-Quran in it, it is deficient (khidaj) – three times – not complete.' (Muslim, p.169, no.17878/395; Abu Dawud, p.125, no.821) 'Khidaj' means that leaving the Fatihah leaves a deficiency in the prayer, which must be remedied by sujud al-sahw. Therefore, in the Hanafi school, reciting al-Fatihah is wajib; if one leaves it, the prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is required.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof concerning the status of reciting Surah al-Fatihah in prayer according to the Hanafi school. The author clarifies at the outset that in the Hanafi school, reciting al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard. He then presents two sets of evidences: first, proofs that reciting any Quran is fard and that al-Fatihah is not exclusively required for validity; second, proofs that al-Fatihah specifically is wajib. The key distinction is that fard is established by definitive evidence (qati'), while wajib is established by probable evidence (zanni). The hadith 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite the Fatihah' is interpreted by the Hanafis as showing wujub, not fard, because the negative form can indicate either. The passage concludes that omitting al-Fatihah does not invalidate the prayer but necessitates sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): In this passage, wajib refers to an obligation that is established by zanni evidence; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation (sujud al-sahw).
فرض (fard): In this passage, fard refers to an obligation established by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir sunnah); omission invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person intentionally omits reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs of Fajr prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is required.
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The prayer is invalid if omitted intentionally, but valid if omitted unintentionally.

Key Takeaway
Reciting al-Fatihah is wajib (not fard) in Hanafi prayer; omission requires sujud al-sahw but does not invalidate.

The Wajib of Adding a Surah after Fatihah: Ruling, Context, and Evidence
Establishes that adding a surah after Fatihah is wajib in specific contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a surah after al-Fatihah, identify the contexts in which it is wajib, and explain the evidence and the inter-madhhab difference regarding its obligation.

Core Idea
Adding a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of witr and nafl; omitting it requires sujud al-sahw.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah clarifies the Hanafi ruling on qira'ah in prayer beyond al-Fatihah. It specifies where a surah (or equivalent) is wajib and distinguishes the Hanafi position from that of Imam Malik. The evidence relies on a key hadith and the interpretation of the negation 'la salata'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Adding a surah after al-Fatihah. The ruling: wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of witr and nafl.
Wajib means omission requires sujud al-sahw but prayer remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Abu Sa'id with 'la salata', and the practice of the Prophet in Zuhr and Asr. Also a qawl sahabi for the minimum of three verses.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith yield wujub? The phrase 'la salata' is interpreted as negation of perfection (nafy al-kamal), not validity, leading to wujub not fard.
This interpretation is based on Hanafi usul that la nafiyata al-jins when used in certain contexts indicates deficiency.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik interprets the same hadith as fard. The difference stems from the interpretation of 'la salata'. The practical consequence: Hanafi prayer is valid with omission (requires sujud al-sahw), Maliki prayer would be invalid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul principles.
5
Apply the ruling to all contexts
Note that in fard, it's only the first two rak'ahs; in witr and nafl, all rak'ahs because witr is like nafl and nafl has each shaf' as a separate unit.
Each shaf' (pair of rak'ahs) in nafl is considered an independent prayer.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۳۹۱) [۲] فرض کی دورکعتوں میں سورت ملائے یا کم از کم تین آیتیں ملائے [۲] اور وتر کی (۳) اور نفل کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملائے ۔ تشریح : [1] فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں یا دوسری دورکعتوں میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے، یا کم سے کم تین چھوٹی آیتیں، یا ایک بڑی آیت ملائے ،[۲] اور وتر نفل کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملائے [۳] اور نفل کی ہر دور کعتیں ایک شفعہ اور ہرشفعہ الگ الگ نماز ہے اس لئے ہر شفعہ میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے، یعنی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله ... ولا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد و سورة في فريضة او غيرها - ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تحریم الصلوة وتحلیلها ص ۵۵، نمبر ۲۳۸ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب القرأة خلف الامام، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۸۳۹) اس حدیث میں وسورۃ فی فریضہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ کی طرح سورۃ ملانا بھی فرض ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں حضور نے سورت ملائی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورت ملانا بھی فرض ہے ۔ حدیث یہ ہے عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن أبيه ، قال : كان رسول الله الا الله يقرأ في الركعتين الاوليين من صلوة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين يطول فى الاولى ويقصر في الثانية و يسمع الآية احيانا ، و كان يقرأ في العصر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين و كان يطول في الاولى ، و كان يطول في الركعة الاولى من صلوة الصبح ، و يقصر فى الثانية (بخارى شريف، باب القرآة في الظهر ، ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۷۵۹ مسلم شریف ، باب القرآة في الظهر والعصر بص ١٩٠، نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت بھی ملاتے تھے، اس سے امام مالک ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ سورت ملانا بھی فرض ہے ۔ حنفیہ اسی حدیث سے سورت ملانا واجب قرار دیتے ہیں۔ (۳) اور کم سے کم تین آیتیں ہوں اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ قال لی ابن شبرمة نظرت كم يكفي الرجل من القرآن فلم اجد سورة اقل من ثلاث آيات فقلت لا ينبغي لاحد ان يقرأ اقل من ثلاث آيات ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب فی کم یقرأ القرآن ؟ ص ۱۹۰۴ نمبر ۵۰۵)
Translation: (391) [2] In the two rak'ahs of fard, add a surah or at least three verses. [2] And in witr, (3) and in all rak'ahs of nafl, add a surah. Explanation: [1] In the first two rak'ahs of fard (or in the second two), adding a surah is wajib, or at least three short verses, or one long verse. [2] Witr is of the status of nafl, so in all its rak'ahs, adding a surah is wajib. [3] In nafl, each two rak'ahs constitute a shaf' (pair), and each shaf' is a separate prayer, so in every shaf', adding a surah is wajib, meaning in all rak'ahs it is wajib. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Abu Sa'id: The Prophet said, 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in a fard or other prayer.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi tahrim al-salah wa tahliliha, p.55, no.238; Ibn Majah, Bab al-qira'ah khalfa al-imam, p.19, no.839) This shows that adding a surah is fard just like al-Fatihah. (2) Another hadith: The Prophet recited in every rak'ah a surah after al-Fatihah. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada: 'The Prophet used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr with al-Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening in the first and shortening in the second, and sometimes making audible an ayah. And he recited in Asr with al-Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening in the first. And he lengthened the first rak'ah of Fajr and shortened the second.' (Bukhari, Bab al-qira'ah fi al-zuhr, p.133, no.759; Muslim, Bab al-qira'ah fi al-zuhr wa al-asr, p.190, no.1012/451) Imam Malik deduces from this that adding a surah is fard. The Hanafis use this same hadith to declare it wajib. (3) For the minimum of three verses, the saying of the Companion Ibn Shubrumah: 'I considered how much Quran suffices a man, and I found no surah shorter than three verses, so I said no one should recite less than three verses.' (Bukhari, Bab fi kam yuqra' al-Quran? p.1904, no.505)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of adding a surah (or its equivalent) after al-Fatihah in prayer. The author states clearly the applications: it is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard (if one recites in the second two, that also fulfills the wajib), and in all rak'ahs of witr and nafl. The evidence presented includes a hadith with the phrase 'la salata' again, which the Hanafis interpret to indicate wujub, not fard. There is an explicit mention that Imam Malik considers it fard, while the Hanafis consider it wajib, highlighting an inter-madhhab difference. The minimum amount is established by the Companion's statement as three verses.

Key Terms
سورة (surah): A chapter of the Quran; in this context, it means a complete surah of at least three short verses or one long verse.
شفعة (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in nafl prayer; each shaf' is considered an independent unit of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the minimum recitation required after al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs of Fard?
A) A complete surah of any length.
B) At least three short verses or one long verse equivalent to three short verses.
C) At least one verse of any length.
D) No additional recitation after al-Fatihah is required.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, adding a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard; its omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sujud al-sahw.

Reciting a Surah in Witr and Nafl and Specifying Recitation in First Two Rak'ahs
Explaining rulings on surah recitation in witr/nafl and specification of recitation in first two rak'ahs with order of Fatihah before surah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting a surah after al-Fatihah in witr, nafl, and the first two rak'ahs of fard, and explain the evidence and the difference with Imam Malik's view.

Core Idea
Reciting a surah after al-Fatihah is wajib in every rak'ah of witr and nafl, and in the first two rak'ahs of fard, with al-Fatihah before the surah.

In this lesson, we examine three key rulings on surah recitation in prayer from the Hanafi school. The passage clarifies when a surah is required after al-Fatihah, the obligation to recite it in specific rak'ahs of fard, and the mandatory order of recitation. These rulings are derived from hadith and the practice of the Companions, and are distinguished from the view of Imam Malik, who considers surah recitation fard in all rak'ahs. Understanding these distinctions helps you properly apply the wajib category in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage covers: (1) reciting a surah in witr and nafl is wajib in every rak'ah; (2) in fard, reciting a surah is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; (3) al-Fatihah must be recited before the surah. Note that the surah must be at least three verses.
These rulings apply to both the imam and the individual praying alone.
2
State the Hanafi position for each
For witr: it is treated like nafl, so a surah is wajib in every rak'ah. For nafl: each pair of rak'ahs is a separate unit, so a surah is wajib in every rak'ah. For fard: reciting in two rak'ahs is fard overall, but it is wajib to recite the surah in the first two rak'ahs. The order of al-Fatihah before the surah is also wajib.
The hukm of wajib means omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
3
Locate the primary dalil
The main proof is the hadith of Abu Sa'id: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory or other prayer.' The Hanafis interpret the imperative 'wa surah' as requiring a surah, but since the hadith is ahad, the obligation is at the level of wajib, not fard.
The hadith is recorded in Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah. Its chain is zanni al-thubut.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik
Imam Malik uses the same hadith and the practice of the Prophet (reciting a surah in every rak'ah) to argue that surah recitation is fard in all rak'ahs of fard. The Hanafis respond by pointing to other evidence that the Prophet sometimes shortened in the last rak'ahs, indicating that the full recitation (with surah) is only required in the first two.
The practical difference: Hanafis do not require repeating a prayer if a surah is omitted in the last two rak'ahs; Maliki would require repetition.
5
Analyze the additional proofs
The passage cites the practice of Sa'd, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ali to confirm that in the last two rak'ahs only al-Fatihah (or even tasbih) is recited. This supports the Hanafi position that the surah is specific to the first two rak'ahs.
These are qawl sahabi, which in Hanafi usul is hujja if not contradicted.

فصل في واجبات الصلوة
في جميع ركعات الوتر والنفل (۳۹۲) وتعيين القراءة فى الاوليين وتقديم الفاتحة على بڑی آیت ملائے ،[۲] اور وتر نفل کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے وتر کی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملائے [۳] اور نفل کی ہر دور کعتیں ایک شفعہ اور ہرشفعہ الگ الگ نماز ہے اس لئے ہر شفعہ میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے، یعنی تمام رکعتوں میں سورت ملانا واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله ... ولا صلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد و سورة في فريضة او غيرها - ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تحریم الصلوة وتحلیلها ص ۵۵، نمبر ۲۳۸ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب القرأة خلف الامام، ص ۱۹، نمبر ۸۳۹) اس حدیث میں وسورۃ فی فریضہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ کی طرح سورۃ ملانا بھی فرض ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں حضور نے سورت ملائی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورت ملانا بھی فرض ہے ۔ حدیث یہ ہے عن عبد الله بن ابی قتادة عن أبيه ، قال : كان رسول الله الا الله يقرأ في الركعتين الاوليين من صلوة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين يطول فى الاولى ويقصر في الثانية و يسمع الآية احيانا ، و كان يقرأ في العصر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين و كان يطول في الاولى ، و كان يطول في الركعة الاولى من صلوة الصبح ، و يقصر فى الثانية (بخارى شريف، باب القرآة في الظهر ، ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۷۵۹ مسلم شریف ، باب القرآة في الظهر والعصر بص ١٩٠، نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت بھی ملاتے تھے، اس سے امام مالک ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ سورت ملانا بھی فرض ہے ۔ حنفیہ اسی حدیث سے سورت ملانا واجب قرار دیتے ہیں۔ (۳) اور کم سے کم تین آیتیں ہوں اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ قال لی ابن شبرمة نظرت كم يكفي الرجل من القرآن فلم اجد سورة اقل من ثلاث آيات فقلت لا ينبغي لاحد ان يقرأ اقل من ثلاث آيات ۔ ( بخاری شریف ، باب فی کم یقرأ القرآن ؟ ص ۱۹۰۴ نمبر ۵۰۵) ترجمه : (۳۹۲) (۳) پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کا معین کرنا۔ [۴] فاتحہ کا سورت پر مقدم کرنا۔ تشریح : چار رکعت فرض ہو تو دور کعتوں میں قرآت کرنا فرض ہے، پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت کرے تب بھی ادا ہو جائے گا ، اور دوسری دورکعتوں میں قرآت کرے تب بھی ادا ہو جائے گا لیکن پہلی دو رکعت میں قرآت کرنا واجب ہے، اور دوسرا مسئلہ یہ بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ قرآت کرتے وقت سورۃ فاتحہ کو پہلے پڑھے اور دوسری سورت کو اس کے بعد پڑھے یہ بھی واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں اس کی وضاحت ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابي قتادة عن أبيه ، قال : كان رسول الله الله صلى الله يقرأ في الركعتين الاوليين من صلوة الظهر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين يطول في الاولى و يقصر في الثانية و يسمع الآية احيانا ، و كان يقرأ في العصر بفاتحة الكتاب و سورتين و كان يطوّل في الاولى ، و كان يطول في الركعة الأولى من صلوة الصبح ، و يقصر في الثانية (بخارى شريف، باب القرآة في الظهر ، ص ۱۲۳، نمبر ۷۵۹ مسلم شریف، باب القرأة في الظهر العصر ، ص۱۹۰، نمبر ۱۰۱۲/۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ فرض کی پہلی دورکعتوں میں قرآت کی اور یہ بھی ہے کہ پہلے سورہ فاتحہ پڑھی بعد میں سورت ملائی۔ (۲) جابر بن سمرة قال قال عمر لسعد لقد شکوک فی کل شيء حتى الصلوة قال اما انا فامد في الاوليين واحذف في الآخرين ولا آلو ما اقتديت به من صلوة رسول الله قال صدقت ذاک الظن بک ۔ (بخاری شریف ، باب يطول في الاوليين و يحذف في الاخر بین ، ص ۱۰۶ نمبر ۷۷ مسلم شریف ، باب القرآة في الظهر والعصر ، ص ۱۸۶، نمبر ۱۰۱۸/۴۵۳) دوسری دو رکعتوں میں حذف کرتے تھے یعنی صرف سورہ فاتحہ پڑھتے تھے۔ (۳) عن ابن سیرین قال نبئت ان ابن مسعود كان يقرأ في الظهر والعصر في الركعتين الأوليين بفاتحة الكتاب و ما تيسر و في الاخريين بفاتحة الكتاب - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يقر أفي الاولين بفاتحہ الكتاب وسورة وفي الاخر بين بفاتحۃ الکتاب ، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۵، نمبر ۳۷۲۲) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ تیسری اور چوتھی رکعتوں میں صرف سورہ فاتحہ پڑھے ۔ (۴) عن علی و عبد الله انهما قالا اقرأ في الاوليين و سبح في الاخريين (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من كان يقول يسج في الاخر بین ولا یقر ، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۷، نمبر ۳۷۴۲) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ تیسری اور چوتھی رکعتوں میں صرف تسبیح پڑھے۔
Chapter on the obligatory acts of prayer. Regarding reciting a surah in all rak'ahs of witr and nafl (392) and specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs and presenting al-Fatihah before the surah. [2] And witr is of the category of nafl, therefore in all rak'ahs of witr a surah is recited. [3] And nafl: every two rak'ahs are a shaf' (pair), and each shaf' is a separate prayer, therefore in each shaf' reciting a surah is wajib. That is, reciting a surah in all rak'ahs is wajib. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: from Abu Sa'id, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: '...No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory or other prayer.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) From this hadith, it is understood that reciting a surah, like al-Fatihah, is fard. (2) In a hadith, the Prophet recited a surah in every rak'ah, indicating that reciting a surah is fard. The hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of zuhr al-Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first and shortening the second, and sometimes making us hear a verse; and in asr he recited al-Fatihah and two surahs, lengthening the first; and he lengthened the first rak'ah of fajr and shortened the second. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, he recited a surah with al-Fatihah in every rak'ah. From this, Imam Malik proves that reciting a surah is fard. The Hanafis consider it wajib from the same hadith. (3) And the minimum is three verses. For this, there is a saying of a Companion: Ibn Shubruma said to me: I looked at how much Quran suffices a man, and I did not find a surah less than three verses, so I said: It is not proper for anyone to recite less than three verses. (Bukhari) Translation: (392) (3) Specifying recitation in the first two rak'ahs. [4] Presenting al-Fatihah before the surah. Explanation: In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, reciting in two rak'ahs is fard. If one recites in the first two rak'ahs, it is performed; if in the last two, it is also performed. But reciting in the first two is wajib. And the second issue: when reciting, one should recite al-Fatihah first and then the surah after it; this is also wajib. Evidence: (1) This hadith clarifies: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of zuhr al-Fatihah and two surahs... (as above) In this hadith, he recited in the first two rak'ahs of fard, and he recited al-Fatihah first then the surah. (2) Jabir ibn Samurah said: Umar said to Sa'd: They have complained about you in everything, even prayer. He said: As for me, I lengthen in the first two and shorten in the last two, and I do not fall short of what I followed from the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. He said: You have spoken the truth; that is what we thought of you. (Bukhari, Muslim) He used to shorten in the last two, i.e., recite only al-Fatihah. (3) From Ibn Sirin, he said: I was informed that Ibn Mas'ud used to recite in zuhr and asr in the first two rak'ahs al-Fatihah and whatever was easy, and in the last two al-Fatihah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) This saying of the Companion indicates that in the third and fourth rak'ahs only al-Fatihah is recited. (4) From Ali and Abdullah, they said: Recite in the first two and glorify in the last two. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) This saying of the Companion indicates that in the third and fourth rak'ahs only tasbih is recited.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage opens the section on the obligatory acts (wajibat) of prayer. It addresses three rulings: reciting a surah in witr and nafl, specifying recitation in the first two rak'ahs of fard, and the order of al-Fatihah before the surah. The author first explains that witr is treated like nafl, so a surah is wajib in every rak'ah. Similarly, each pair of rak'ahs in nafl forms a separate unit, requiring a surah in each rak'ah. For fard, the only obligation is to recite in two rak'ahs, but it is wajib to do so in the first two. Presenting al-Fatihah before the surah is also wajib. The proofs include a hadith from Abu Sa'id stating that a prayer without al-Hamd and a surah is invalid, which the Hanafis interpret as requiring a surah but at the level of wajib, not fard, because the chain is ahad. The hadith of Abu Qatada shows the Prophet's practice of reciting a surah in every rak'ah, which Imam Malik takes as fard, but the Hanafis see it as emphatic sunnah or wajib due to other evidence. The minimum length of the surah is three verses, based on Ibn Shubruma's ijtihad. Further proofs from the practice of the Companions, like Sa'd shortening to only al-Fatihah in the last rak'ahs, and reports from Ibn Mas'ud and Ali about reciting only al-Fatihah or tasbih in the last two, confirm that the full recitation (with surah) is confined to the first two rak'ahs. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is consistent: surah recitation is wajib in witr and nafl in all rak'ahs, and in fard only in the first two rak'ahs, with al-Fatihah always preceding.

Key Terms
واجب (wājib): An obligatory act that is proven by a zanni (probable) dalil; omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
سورة (sūrah): A chapter of the Quran, or a passage of at least three verses recited after al-Fatihah in prayer.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer that is recommended but not obligatory.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in nafl prayer; each pair is considered a separate unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, in which rak'ahs is reciting a surah after al-Fatihah wajib according to the Hanafi school?
A) All four rak'ahs
B) First two rak'ahs
C) Last two rak'ahs
D) Only the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Reciting a surah after al-Fatihah is a wajib act in witr, nafl, and the first two rak'ahs of fard; its omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

The Wajib of the Nose in Sujud
Stating the ruling that placing the nose in sujud is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing the nose in sujud and explain why it is wajib, not fard.

Core Idea
Placing the nose on the ground in sujud is wajib; omission requires sajdah sahw.

In the Hanafi school, sujud is a pillar of prayer requiring the forehead to touch the ground. But what about the nose? This lesson examines the proofs that establish the nose as a wajib requirement, clarifying the distinction between fard and wajib in prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that placing the nose with the forehead in sujud is wajib. The forehead is the original (foundation), and the nose is an additional obligation.
Wajib in Hanafi: required but proven by zanni evidence; omission does not invalidate the act but requires compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
Three hadith are cited: Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi (Tirmidhi), Ibn Abbas (Bukhari/Muslim), and Ibn Abbas (Darqutni). All indicate the importance of the nose in sujud.
These are ahad hadith, hence the ruling is at the level of wajib, not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The first hadith says the Prophet 'placed his nose and forehead firmly'. The second lists nose among seven bones. The third states 'no prayer for one who does not place his nose on the ground'.
The strongest evidence is the clear command in the third hadith, but it is ahad.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhahib may consider the nose sunnah or recommended. The Hanafi position is based on these proofs and the distinction between fard and wajib.
Cross-madhhab disagreement exists but is legitimate.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the nose is wajib; if omitted, the prayer is valid but sajdah sahw is required.
The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that a missing wajib is compensated.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۳۹۳) [۵] سجدہ میں پیشانی کے ساتھ ناک ملانا۔ تشریح : سجدہ میں زمین پر پیشانی رکھنا اصل ہے، لیکن اس کے ساتھ ناک کو بھی زمین پر رکھنا واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) ناک زمین پر رکھنا واجب اس کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ عن ابی حمید الساعدي : أن النبي الله كان اذا سجد أمكن أنفه و جبهته من الارض و نحى يديه عن جنبيه ، ووضع كفيه حذو منكبيه ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فى السجود على الجمعة والانف ہیں، ۷۴ ، نمبر، ۲۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ناک اور پیشانی پر سجدہ کرے۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس قال قال النبي علم امرت ان اسجد على سبعة اعظم على الجبهة واشار بيده على انفه واليدين والركبتين واطراف القدمين ( بخاری شریف ، باب السجود علی الانف ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۸۱۲ر مسلم شریف، باب اعضاء السجو دو النھی عن كف الشعر ص ۲۰۳، نمبر ۱۰۹۹٫۴۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ناک اور پیشانی پر سجدہ کرے۔ (۳) عن ابن عباس ، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : لا صلوة لمن لم يضع أنفه على الارض . (دار قطنی ، باب وجوب وضع الجبهة والانف ، ج اول ص ۱۳۴۱، نمبر ۱۳۰۳ رمستدرک للحاکم ، کتاب الصلوۃ ، ج اول ،ص ۴۰۴ نمبر ۹۹۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب تک ناک زمین پر نہ لگائے نماز نہیں ہوگی۔
Translation: (393) [5] Placing the nose with the forehead in sujud. Explanation: Placing the forehead on the ground in sujud is the foundation, but placing the nose on the ground along with it is wajib. Evidence: (1) The evidence that placing the nose on the ground is wajib is the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: The Prophet, when he prostrated, placed his nose and forehead firmly on the ground, moved his hands away from his sides, and placed his palms level with his shoulders. (Tirmidhi, chapter on sujud on the forehead and nose, no. 27) This hadith indicates prostrating on the nose and forehead. (2) From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Prophet said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead, and he pointed with his hand to his nose, and [also on] the hands, knees, and toes. (Bukhari, chapter on sujud on the nose, no. 812; Muslim, chapter on limbs of sujud) This hadith indicates prostrating on the nose and forehead. (3) From Ibn Abbas, from the Prophet, he said: There is no prayer for the one who does not place his nose on the ground. (Darqutni, chapter on obligation of placing the forehead and nose, no. 1303; Mustadrak al-Hakim) This hadith indicates that until the nose touches the ground, the prayer will not be valid.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof that placing the nose on the ground in sujud is wajib, in addition to the forehead. The primary pillar (rukn) of sujud is placing the forehead, but the nose is an additional requirement. The author provides three hadith proofs: the first shows the Prophet's consistent practice of placing both nose and forehead; the second explicitly lists the nose as one of the seven bones of sujud; the third directly states that prayer is invalid without placing the nose. The Hanafi position is that if one sujuds only on the forehead without the nose, the sujud is valid but the prayer is deficient and requires sajdah sahw, because the nose is wajib, not rukn. The hadiths are ahad, so the obligation is at the level of wajib, not fard. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi distinction between fard (forehead) and wajib (nose).

Key Terms
سجود (sujūd): Prostration, a pillar of prayer in which the forehead and nose touch the ground.
وجوب (wujūb): Obligation at the level of wajib, proven by zanni evidence; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate the act's essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on placing the nose on the ground during sujud?
A) It is sunnah and its omission is allowed
B) It is wajib and its omission requires sajdah sahw
C) It is fard and the prayer is invalid without it
D) It is makruh to touch the nose

Key Takeaway
Placing the nose on the ground in sujud is wajib; its omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah sahw.

The Second Sajdah is Wajib, Not Fard
Distinguishing the second sajdah as wajib with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the second sajdah, explain why it is wajib, and identify the consequence of its omission.

Core Idea
The second sajdah is wajib; omission requires sajdah sahw, but the prayer remains valid.

In the Hanafi school, not every prostration in prayer carries the same weight. While the first sajdah in each rak'ah is a fundamental pillar (fard), the second sajdah is classified as wajib. This lesson examines that distinction, the ruling that it must be performed before moving to the next action, and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing the second sajdah in each rak'ah. The Hanafi ruling is that it is wajib, not fard.
Wajib means it is required; if omitted unintentionally, sajdah sahw compensates.
2
Distinguish between first and second sajdah
The first sajdah is a rukn (fard) – the prayer is invalid without it. The second sajdah is wajib – the prayer remains valid but compensation is needed if omitted.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Note the timing condition
The second sajdah must be performed before moving to the next action, such as standing for the next rak'ah or sitting for tashahhud.
Deliberate delay or omission changes the ruling.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
If the second sajdah is omitted unintentionally, sajdah sahw is required. If omitted intentionally, the prayer is still valid but the person is sinful.
This follows the general rule for wajib acts in prayer.
5
Examine the proof
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet taught a man to repeat his prayer because he did not perform the sajdahs properly. This indicates the wajib nature of the second sajdah.
The hadith is from Abu Huraira, though the text is truncated here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۹۴) [1] ہر رکعت میں دوسرے افعال کی طرف منتقل ہونے سے پہلے دوسرا سجدہ کرنا ۔ تشریح: پہلا سجدہ فرض ہے اور دوسرا سجدہ واجب ہے اس لئے اگلی رکعت میں یا تشہد میں جانے سے پہلے دوسرا سجدہ کرنا واجب ہے صلى الله وجه : عن ابي هريرة عن النبي علي دخل المسجد فدخل رجل فصلى ثم جاء فسلم على النبي
Translation: (394) [1] Performing the second sajdah in each rak'ah before moving to other actions. Explanation: The first sajdah is fard, and the second sajdah is wajib. Therefore, it is wajib to perform the second sajdah before going to the next rak'ah or to tashahhud. Evidence: From Abu Huraira, from the Prophet: 'A man entered the mosque, prayed, then came and greeted the Prophet...'
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about the second sajdah in each rak'ah. The first sajdah is a pillar (fard) of the prayer; the second sajdah is wajib. The obligation is to perform it before any action that moves to the next part of the prayer, such as rising for the next rak'ah or sitting for tashahhud. If one intentionally omits the second sajdah, the prayer is still valid but a sajdah sahw is required. The proof cited is from a hadith of Abu Huraira, though the text cuts off. This is likely the well-known hadith of the man who prayed and the Prophet taught him to repeat his prayer because he did not perform the sajdahs properly. The Hanafi school uses this to establish the wajib status of the second sajdah.

Key Terms
سجدہ (sajdah): Prostration; first sajdah is a rukn, second sajdah is wajib in each rak'ah.
تشہد (tashahhud): Sitting for recitation of the testimony of faith in the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of the second sajdah in each rak'ah?
A) It is fard and the prayer is invalid without it
B) It is wajib and its omission requires sajdah sahw
C) It is sunnah and its omission is allowed
D) It is not required

Key Takeaway
The second sajdah in each rak'ah is wajib according to the Hanafi school; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah sahw.

Placing the Nose with the Forehead in Sujood is Wajib
Obligation of placing nose on ground during prostration with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that placing the nose alongside the forehead in sujood is wajib according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the three hadith cited.

Core Idea
Placing the nose on the ground in sujood is wajib, not merely sunnah.

In the Hanafi school, the act of prostration has specific requirements. While the forehead is the primary part that must touch the ground, the nose is also obligatory. This lesson examines the textual evidence that establishes this ruling and clarifies the difference between fard and wajib in this context. We will walk through three key hadith and understand why the Hanafi school treats this act as wajib rather than sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which act is being ruled upon and its legal classification. The passage states: 'Placing the nose along with the forehead in sujood is wajib.'
The act is placing the nose on the ground in prostration.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the three hadith cited as evidence. They are: (1) Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi on the Prophet's practice, (2) Ibn Abbas on the command to prostrate on seven bones including the nose, and (3) Ibn Abbas on the negation 'no prayer for one who does not place his nose on the ground.'
All three are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each hadith proves wujub. The first shows the Prophet's consistent action. The second includes a gesture indicating the nose. The third uses a severe negation which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub when combined with other evidence.
The negation 'no prayer' is interpreted as emphasizing wujub, not fard, because the act is not a rukn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that other schools, especially the Shafi'i, consider placing the nose as sunnah, not wajib. Their proof is that the forehead alone is the primary part, and the nose is included by gesture but not an obligatory element.
The Hanafi response relies on the explicit negation in the third hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that placing the nose is wajib. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the standard fatwa.
Intra-Hanafi disagreement is minimal; the three imams agree.

In the Hanafi school, omitting the nose intentionally invalidates the prayer; if forgotten, sajdah al-sahw is required.

Performing the Second Sajdah in Each Rakah
Obligation of second prostration with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the second sajdah (wajib) and apply the fard/wajib distinction to determine the consequence of omission.

Core Idea
Second sajdah is wajib; omitting it intentionally requires repetition, forgetting requires sajdah al-sahw.

The second prostration in each rakah is often misunderstood. This lesson clarifies its precise ruling in the Hanafi school: not a fard (integral) but a wajib (obligatory) whose omission does not undo the prayer but demands compensation. We will examine the prophetic proof and the legal reasoning behind this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling.
Locate the act being discussed — the second sajdah in each rakah. Note that the text explicitly states it is wajib, contrasting with the first sajdah which is fard.
The passage uses the Urdu terms 'farz' and 'wajib'.
2
Locate the dalil.
The author cites the hadith of the man who prayed improperly. Identify the specific instruction: the Prophet ordered him to prostrate a second time after sitting between the two prostrations.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah.
How does the hadith prove the obligation? The imperative 'then prostrate' after the sitting indicates a separate commanded act. In Hanafi usul, a single command conveys obligation (wujub), but the requirement of tranquility (itmi'nan) suggests it is not at the level of fard.
The distinction: fard is proven by qat'i evidence, wajib by zanni evidence.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference.
Contrast the Hanafi view (wajib) with the Shafi'i position (fard). Understand that the difference stems from different evaluations of the strength of the dalil.
Thamarah al-khilaf: if forgotten, Hanafi requires sajdah al-sahw; Shafi'i requires repeating the sajdah.
5
Evaluate the consequence of omission.
Apply the ruling: if the second sajdah is omitted intentionally, the prayer is still valid but sinful (makruh tahrimi) and must be repeated. If forgotten, sajdah al-sahw suffices.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Explanation: The first sajdah is fard and the second sajdah is wajib. Therefore, it is wajib to perform the second sajdah before going to the next rakah or to tashahhud. Tranquility in the Pillars of Prayer (Tadil al-Arkan)
Obligation of tranquility and composure in all postures of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadil al-arkan and explain the proof from the hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Badri.

Core Idea
Tranquility in prayer is a wajib element — its omission intentionally invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of tranquility (iṭmi'nān) in each posture of prayer, known as tadil al-arkan. The Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, not fard, meaning that if omitted unintentionally, it can be compensated by sajdah al-sahw. We will explore the primary dalil from the hadith and understand how the Hanafi usul derives this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, understand what tadil al-arkan means: pausing in each posture (ruku, sujud, standing, sitting) until all limbs are still. The passage states it is wajib.
Wajib in Hanafi means obligatory but based on a zanni dalil, unlike fard which is based on qati dalil.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: the hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet ordered the man to repeat his prayer, and the explicit hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Badri.
The key hadith is: 'لا تجزىء صلاة الرجل حتى يقيم ظهره في الركوع والسجود' (The prayer of a man is not complete until he straightens his back in bowing and prostration).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze the negation 'لا تجزىء' (does not suffice). In Hanafi usul, such negation for a specific element within prayer indicates that element is wajib. If omitted, the prayer is invalid unless compensated by sajdah al-sahw when forgotten.
This derivation shows how ahad hadith yield a wajib ruling, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider tadil al-arkan as fard. Understand the practical consequence: in Hanafi, unintentional omission requires sajdah al-sahw; in other schools, the prayer must be repeated if omitted intentionally or unintentionally.
This difference stems from the classification of the dalil's certainty (zanni vs qati) and the application of usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and derived from the explicit hadith combined with the principle that ahad hadith indicate wujub. The ruling is consistent with the majority of Hanafi scholars.
No major intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists on this point; the position is well-established.

In this hadith is that whoever does not perform tadil al-arkan, his prayer is not valid, therefore tadil al-arkan is wajib.

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation (wujub) of tranquility (iṭmi'nān) in all pillars of prayer, a concept known as tadil al-arkan. This means pausing in each posture long enough for the joints to settle. The proof is from two hadith: first, the previously mentioned hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet ordered him to repeat his prayer because he did not pause in bowing and prostration; second, the explicit hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Badri that the prayer is not complete until the back is straight in ruku and sujood. First Sitting and Tashahhud: Wajib Acts in Prayer
Obligation of first sitting and tashahhud in both sittings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the first sitting and tashahhud in both sittings, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Buhainah demonstrating wujub.

Core Idea
The first sitting and tashahhud in both sittings are wajib, proven by the Prophet's sajdah al-sahw for omitting them.

In the Hanafi school, certain acts in prayer are classified as wajib—obligatory but not at the level of fard. Among these are the first sitting after two rak'ahs and the recitation of tashahhud in both the first and final sittings. This lesson unpacks these three interrelated rulings and the hadith evidence that establishes their wajib status, while also addressing the differing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and list the three distinct rulings: (1) sitting in the first qa'dah is wajib, (2) reciting tashahhud in the first qa'dah is wajib, (3) reciting tashahhud in the final qa'dah is wajib.
2
Examine the primary proof (Ibn Buhainah)
Analyze the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhainah. The Prophet stood up after two rak'ahs without sitting, then performed sajdah al-sahw before the taslim. Since sajdah al-sahw compensates for an omitted wajib act, this proves the first sitting is wajib.
Sajdah al-sahw is only required for omitting a wajib, not a sunnah.
3
Understand the second proof (al-Mughira)
Review the hadith of al-Mughira: if the imam stands after two rak'ahs and remembers before straightening, he should sit; if he is already straight, he completes the prayer and performs sajdah al-sahw. This rule reinforces wujub.
4
Assess the proof for tashahhud
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud narrates that the Prophet taught the tashahhud to be recited in prayer. The continuous practice of the Companions and the Prophet indicates its obligatory nature in both sittings.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i considers the first sitting as sunnah, not wajib, and the final tashahhud as fard. The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith of Ibn Buhainah overrides general practice, and the sajdah al-sahw is decisive evidence for wujub.

ترجمه : (۳۹۲) [۸] پہلا تعدہ - (۹) پہلے قعدہ میں تشہد پڑھنا صحیح روایت میں ۔ [۱۰] اخیر قعدہ میں تشہد پڑھنا۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں [1] چار رکعت والی فرض نماز میں پہلے قعدہ میں بیٹھنا واجب ہے [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے قعدہ میں تشہد پڑھنا بھی واجب ہے۔ [۳] تیسر امسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے۔
وجه : (1) عن عبد الله بن بحينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله الله ركعتين ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلاته و انتظرنا التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتين و هو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب من قام من شفتین ولم تشهد ، ص ۱۵۷ نمبر ۱۰۳۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قعدہ اولی واجب ہے جسکے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو کیا۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن المغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم (( اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل أن يستوى قائما فليجلس ، فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس ويسجد سجدتي السهو )) ۔(ابوداود شریف، باب من نسى أن يتشهد وهو جالس ، ص ۱۵۷، نمبر ۱۰۳۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قاعدہ اولی بھول جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے، کیونکہ قعدہ اولی واجب ہے۔(۳) قعدہ اولی اور قعدہ ثانیہ میں تشہد پڑھنا واجب ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قــال عبد الله بن مسعـود كـنـا اذا صلينا خلف النبي عل الله فقال ان الله هو السلام فاذا صلى احدكم فليقل التحيات لله ، ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب التشهد في الآخرة ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۸۳۱ مسلم شریف ، باب التشهد فی الصلاۃ ص ۱۷۱ نمبر
(396) And the first sitting and recitation of tashahhud in it. Translation: (392) [8] First sitting - (9) Reciting tashahhud in the first sitting according to the correct narration - [10] Reciting tashahhud in the last sitting. Explanation: Here are three issues: [1] In a four-rakah obligatory prayer, sitting in the first qa'dah is wajib. [2] The second issue: reciting tashahhud in the first qa'dah is also wajib. [3] The third issue: reciting tashahhud in the final qa'dah is wajib. Evidence: (1) From Abdullah ibn Buhainah that the Prophet led us in two rakahs, then stood without sitting, and the people stood with him. When he completed his prayer, and we awaited the taslim, he said takbir and performed two sajdahs while sitting before taslim, then said salam. This hadith indicates that the first qa'dah is wajib because he performed sajdah al-sahw for omitting it. (2) From al-Mughira ibn Shu'bah that the Prophet said: When the imam stands after two rakahs, if he remembers before straightening up fully, let him sit; if he straightens up fully, let him not sit and perform sajdah al-sahw. This hadith shows that the first qa'dah is wajib. (3) Reciting tashahhud in the first and second qa'dah is wajib; for this, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: When we prayed behind the Prophet, he said: Indeed Allah is Peace, so when one of you prays, let him say 'al-tahiyyatu lillah'...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage discusses three related rulings about sitting in prayer. First, sitting after two rakahs (qa'dah ula) in a four-rakah fard prayer is wajib. Second, reciting tashahhud in that first sitting is also wajib. Third, reciting tashahhud in the final sitting is wajib. The proofs are three hadith. The first from Abdullah ibn Buhainah shows that the Prophet performed sajdah al-sahw when he accidentally stood up without sitting after two rakahs, proving that the first sitting is wajib (since sajdah al-sahw is only required for omitting a wajib, not a sunnah). The second hadith from al-Mughira provides a rule: if a person stands up after two rakahs but has not yet straightened, he should sit down; if he has straightened, he should not sit but perform sajdah al-sahw. This again confirms wujub. The third hadith from Ibn Mas'ud narrates the tashahhud and implies its recitation is wajib because it was taught by the Prophet as part of the prayer. In the Hanafi school, the first sitting is wajib, and reciting tashahhud in both sittings is also wajib. Deliberate omission invalidates the prayer; if forgotten, sajdah al-sahw is required.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rakah in prayers of three or four rakahs
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation beginning 'al-tahiyyatu lillah' in both sittings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in a four-rakah fard prayer?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The first sitting and the recitation of tashahhud in both sittings are wajib acts in the Hanafi school, requiring sajdah al-sahw if omitted forgetfully.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Tranquility in All Pillars is Wajib
States the obligation of tranquility in all prayer pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tranquility in prayer pillars and explain the dalil that establishes wajib.

Core Idea
Tranquility in every prayer pillar is wajib — without it, the prayer is invalid.

The Hanafi school holds that tranquility (tuma'ninah) is an obligatory element (wajib) of each prayer pillar. This lesson examines the key hadith proofs and the reasoning that leads to this ruling. You will learn how the Prophet's command to the bedouin and the negation of validity in another hadith establish that tranquility is a condition for a valid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly that the Hanafi position is: tranquility in every pillar of prayer (ruku', sujud, standing after ruku', sitting between prostrations) is wajib. The term used is ta'dil al-arkan.
Wajib means obligatory, but not a pillar (rukn). Omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw) or, if deliberate, the prayer is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
Two primary hadith are cited: (1) The hadith of the bedouin whom the Prophet commanded to repeat his prayer, explicitly instructing him to perform tranquility in each posture. (2) The hadith of Abu Mas'ud al-Badri: 'The prayer of a man is not complete until he straightens his back in bowing and prostration.'
Both are ahad hadith, providing zanni evidence, but sufficient for wajib.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'ارجع فصل' (go back and pray) and the explicit instruction 'حتى تطمئن' (until you are at ease) indicate wujub (obligation) per the Hanafi principle that a command implies obligation. The negation 'لا تجزىء' (does not suffice) in the second hadith shows that without tranquility, the prayer is not valid, which is a stronger indication of wujub.
The repetition of the command for each posture reinforces that tranquility is required in all pillars.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'i scholars consider tranquility to be sunnah, not wajib, arguing that the command indicates recommendation, not obligation. The Hanafi school responds with the negation of validity, which raises it to the level of wajib.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa. The combination of the command and the negation provides strong evidence. Moreover, the hadith is transmitted in major sources (Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi), and the practice of the Companions and early scholars supports wajib.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

Chapter on the Obligatory Acts of Prayer: Transition to other than it (395) and tranquility in the pillars (396) and the first sitting and reciting the tashahhud in it. ... The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed... Then bow until you are at ease bowing, then rise until you are standing straight, then prostrate until you are at ease prostrating, then rise until you are at ease sitting, then prostrate until you are at ease prostrating, then do that in all your prayer.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud)... Explanation: Performing all pillars with tranquility is called ta'dil al-arkan; it is wajib. Evidence: (1) The above hadith. (2) Also this hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Badri: 'The prayer of a man is not complete until he straightens his back in bowing and prostrating.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi)... Therefore ta'dil al-arkan is wajib.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that tranquility (tuma'ninah) in each pillar of prayer is wajib (obligatory). The author first presents the famous hadith of the bedouin whom the Prophet commanded to repeat his prayer because he did not perform tranquility. Then he cites another hadith from Abu Mas'ud al-Badri stating that the prayer is not valid without straightening the back in ruku' and sujud. The term 'ta'dil al-arkan' is introduced as a synonym for performing pillars with tranquility. The Hanafi position is that tranquility is wajib, not merely sunnah. This is derived from the explicit command ('amr) in the first hadith and the negation of validity in the second. The ruling applies to all pillars: standing, bowing, prostration, and sitting.

Key Terms
الاطمئنان (al-ṭuma'nīnah): Being at ease and still in a pillar for a moment, with all limbs settled.
تعديل الأركان (ta'dīl al-arkān): Performing each pillar with tranquility and proper posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tranquility in each prayer pillar is wajib; without it, the prayer is invalid or requires compensation.

First Sitting and Tashahhud are Wajib
Establishes the obligation of first sitting and tashahhud recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three wajibat related to the first sitting and tashahhud, and explain the Hanafi proofs that establish each as wajib.

Core Idea
First sitting and tashahhud are wajib, not sunnah; forgetting them requires sajdah sahw.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the first sitting (qu'ud ula) and reciting tashahhud in both the first and final sittings are wajib. The text presents six pieces of evidence from hadith, Quran, and the practice of the Companions to establish this obligation. Understanding these proofs will strengthen your grasp of Hanafi prayer obligations and the methodology of deriving rulings from dalil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three wajibat
Read the passage carefully and list the three specific actions declared wajib: sitting in the first sitting (for 4-rak'ah prayers), reciting tashahhud in that sitting, and reciting tashahhud in the last sitting.
These are not the only wajibat of prayer; the passage focuses on these three.
2
Locate the dalil for each
Match each ruling to its primary evidence. For the first sitting, the hadith of Ibn Buhaynah and Mughirah involve sajdah sahw. For tashahhud, the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud with the imperative 'falyqul', the hadith that completion depends on it, the Quranic verse, and Umar's athar are used.
Some dalil apply to multiple rulings.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each dalil indicates wujub. For example, performing sajdah sahw for forgetting the first sitting proves it is wajib (since sajdah sahw compensates for a wajib omitted). The imperative 'falyqul' in Hanafi usul indicates obligation. The negation 'la tajuz' indicates a condition or integral.
This step connects usul al-fiqh principles to the proofs.
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Identify that the Shafi'i school considers the first sitting to be sunnah, not wajib. Thus they do not require sajdah sahw for forgetting it. This practical difference is the thamarah al-khilaf.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Translation: (392) [8] The first sitting - (9) Reciting tashahhud in the first sitting according to the correct narration. [10] Reciting tashahhud in the last sitting. Explanation: Here are three issues: [1] Sitting in the first sitting in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer is wajib. [2] The second issue is that reciting tashahhud in the first sitting is also wajib. [3] The third issue is that reciting tashahhud in the last sitting is wajib. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Ibn Buhaynah... (2) Hadith from Mughirah... (3) Hadith from Ibn Mas'ud commanding tashahhud... (4) Hadith: 'When you say this, you have completed your prayer'... (5) Verse of the Quran (33:56)... (6) Athar from Umar: 'Prayer is not valid without tashahhud'...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering three wajibat: (a) sitting in the first sitting (qad'ah ula) in a four-rak'ah prayer, (b) reciting tashahhud in that sitting, and (c) reciting tashahhud in the final sitting. The author provides six pieces of evidence. First, the hadith of Ibn Buhaynah shows that the Prophet performed sajdah sahw when he forgot the first sitting, indicating it is wajib. Second, Mughirah's hadith commands sitting if one remembers before standing straight, otherwise perform sajdah sahw. Third, Ibn Mas'ud's hadith uses the imperative 'falyqul' (let him say) which indicates wujub. Fourth, the hadith that completion of prayer depends on saying tashahhud. Fifth, a Quranic verse (33:56) containing 'sallimu taslima' which alludes to tashahhud because it includes salutation upon the Prophet. Sixth, the athar of Umar stating prayer is not valid without tashahhud. All these prove tashahhud is wajib.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ūd al-awwal): The first sitting in a prayer of three or more rak'ahs, after completing two rak'ahs.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'Attahiyyatu lillahi...' and the salutation upon the Prophet and the righteous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers the first sitting and tashahhud in both sittings as wajib, supported by multiple hadiths, a Quranic verse, and a Companion's statement, with sajdah sahw as the consequence for omission.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Standing for Third Rak'ah Without Delay After Tashahhud
Explains the wajib of standing promptly after first tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what to recite in the first sitting of a four-rak'ah prayer, explain the hadith evidence, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Standing immediately after tashahhud is wajib; reciting salawat in the first sitting is not allowed in the Hanafi school.

In this lesson, we analyze the ruling on the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer. The Hanafi school holds that after reciting tashahhud, one must stand up promptly for the third rak'ah without reciting anything extra. This ruling is supported by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Ibn Mas'ud. We will also see how the Shafi'i school differs on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing from the first sitting to the third rak'ah. The ruling is that it is wajib to do so immediately without extra recitation.
The text explicitly states: 'this is also wajib.'
2
Examine the source evidence
Two hadith from Ibn Mas'ud are cited: the Prophet rose immediately after tashahhud (Musnad Ahmad) and was as quick as if on hot stones (Nasa'i, Abu Dawud).
These hadith demonstrate the Prophet's practice.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's consistent fi'l in worship indicates wujub unless evidence shows otherwise. Here, the fi'l of rising immediately indicates obligation.
This is a key Hanafi principle.
4
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that reciting salawat in the first tashahhud is sunnah, based on a general command and analogy with the last sitting.
This leads to a practical difference in prayer performance.

آخر، ان ترك التشهد الاول ، و الصلوة على النبي عله في التشهد الاول ساهيا ، لا اعادة عليه ، و عليه
Translation (397) [11] Standing up for the third rak'ah without delay after tashahhud. Explanation: In a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, in the first sitting one should only recite tashahhud, not salawat or du'a. Therefore, after reciting tashahhud, one should stand up for the third rak'ah without reciting anything else; this is also wajib. Evidence: (1) Hadith from Ibn Mas'ud: 'The Prophet taught me tashahhud in the middle and end of prayer... then if it is the middle of prayer, he would rise when he finished his tashahhud' (Musnad Ahmad). (2) Hadith from Ibn Mas'ud: 'The Prophet in the two rak'ahs was as if on hot stones' (Nasa'i, Abu Dawud). This indicates he did not recite more than tashahhud in the first sitting. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, one should recite salawat after tashahhud in the first sitting.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that standing for the third rak'ah immediately after the first tashahhud, without reciting anything extra, is wajib. The author explains that in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, one should only recite tashahhud in the first sitting, not salawat or du'a. Two hadith from Ibn Mas'ud support this: first, the Prophet rose immediately after tashahhud in the middle of prayer; second, he was quick to stand as if on hot stones. The fa'idah (benefit) notes the Shafi'i position that one should recite salawat in the first tashahhud, which contrasts with the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
القيام إلى الثالثة (al-qiyām ilā al-thālithah): Standing up from the first sitting to perform the third rak'ah.

B) Tashahhud and salawat
C) Tashahhud, salawat, and a du'a
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, standing immediately after tashahhud without extra recitation is a wajib act in prayers with multiple rak'ahs.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Standing Immediately After Tashahhud in the First Sitting: Wajib
Ruling on standing immediately after tashahhud in first sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing after tashahhud in the first sitting and identify the hadith proofs that establish its wujub.

Core Idea
Standing immediately for the third rak'ah after tashahhud in the first sitting is wajib.

In a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, after completing the tashahhud in the first sitting, one must stand up without delay. This act is considered wajib in the Hanafi school. Many mistakenly add durad or du'a, but the Prophet's practice shows immediate standing. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing up for the third rak'ah immediately after completing tashahhud in the first sitting (qada'ah ula). The Hanafi ruling is that this standing is wajib.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (sajda sahw), not repetition of the entire prayer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet taught that in the middle of prayer one stands when finishing tashahhud, and only in the last sitting does one supplicate. This shows immediate standing is part of the sunna.
The hadith is in Musnad Ahmad and other collections.
3
Analyze the secondary dalil
Another hadith describes the Prophet standing so quickly from the first sitting that he seemed to be on hot stones. This reinforces that he did not delay with additional recitations.
Hadith from Nasa'i and Abu Dawud.
4
Understand the wujub classification
These ahadith are zanni al-thubut (single transmission), so the ruling is wajib not fard. If one forgetfully omits the immediate standing (e.g., by reciting durad), sajda sahw is required.
Fard requires qat'i evidence; wajib is based on strong but not certain proof.

نوٹ : [1] بعض ائمہ کی اور عوام کی عام عادت یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اولی میں بھی تشہد کے بعد درود شریف پڑھ لیتے ہیں، اس لئے یہ عموم بلوی ہے، (٢) اور تشہد کے بعد درودشریف کی حدیث بھی موجود ہے اور امام شافعی کا مسلک بھی [٣] صرف نور الایضاح کی عبارت سے مترشح ہوتا ہے کہ فورا اٹھنا واجب ہے، لیکن سجدہ سہو لازم ہونے کی تشریح یہاں بھی نہیں ہے، اور نہ اس کے لئے کوئی حدیث ہے اس لئے بھول سے پڑھنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم کرنا مناسب معلوم نہیں ہوتا۔
Chapter on the obligatory acts of prayer. The correct recitation in the last sitting (397) and standing for the third without delay after tashahhud. (Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, p.147, no.968) In this hadith, the word 'fa'l-yaqul' is an imperative form indicating obligation. (4) In a hadith it is said: if you recite tashahhud, your prayer will be valid, which shows that tashahhud is obligatory. The hadith is: 'The Messenger of Allah took hold of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and mentioned similar to the dua hadith of al-A'mash: When you say this, you have completed your prayer, if you want to stand then stand, and if you want to sit then sit.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, p.147, no.970) In this hadith it is said that if you recite tashahhud, your prayer will be complete, so it is obligatory. (5) There is an indication in the verse that tashahhud should be recited because it contains salutation upon the Prophet. The verse is: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet; O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace.' (Surah al-Ahzab, 33:56) In this verse, the phrase 'sallimu taslima' points to reciting tashahhud because in tashahhud there is salutation. (6) An athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: Prayer is not valid except with tashahhud.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on one who forgets tashahhud, vol.2, p.134, no.3085) This athar indicates that prayer is not valid without tashahhud, so tashahhud is obligatory. Translation of (397): [11] To stand for the third rak'ah without delay after tashahhud. Explanation: In a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, in the first sitting one should only recite tashahhud; one should not recite durad or du'a. Therefore, after reciting tashahhud, without reciting anything else, one should stand for the third rak'ah. This is also obligatory. Proof: (1) Hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah taught me the tashahhud in the middle of the prayer and at the end... He said: Then if it is in the middle of the prayer, he stood up when he finished his tashahhud, and if it is at the end, he supplicated after his tashahhud as he wished, then made salam.' (Musnad Ahmad, Musnad Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, vol.2, p.44, no.4369) This hadith shows that in the first sitting one should not recite more than tashahhud. (2) From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Prophet in the two rak'ahs was as if on hot stones.' I said: 'Until he stands?' He said: 'That is intended.' (Nasa'i, chapter on lightening the first tashahhud, p.164, no.717; Abu Dawud, chapter on lightening the sitting, p.151, no.995) This hadith indicates that the Prophet would stand up quickly from the first sitting, showing that one should not recite more than tashahhud. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, in the first sitting one should recite durad after tashahhud. In the encyclopedia, the text is: 'Tashahhud and sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud in every prayer except Fajr: there are two tashahhuds, first tashahhud and last tashahhud. If one omits the first tashahhud and sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud forgetfully, there is no repetition upon him, and upon him are two prostrations of forgetfulness for omitting it.' (Encyclopedia of Imam Shafi'i, chapter on tashahhud and blessing upon the Prophet, vol.2, p.193, no.1456) This passage shows that in the first tashahhud, durad is also obligatory. Their proof: The verse and hadiths in which the virtue of sending blessings after tashahhud is mentioned. (1) The verse: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet; O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace.' (Surah al-Ahzab, 33:56) According to this verse, sending blessings once in one's life is fard, and in prayer it is sunnah. (2) Hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujra: ... We said: We know how to greet you, but how should we send blessings upon you? He said: Say: 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad...' (Muslim, chapter on blessing upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p.173, no.908/406; Abu Dawud, chapter on blessing upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p.149, no.976) This hadith shows that after tashahhud, one should send blessings upon the Prophet. (3) From Sahl ibn Sa'd: The Prophet said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not send blessings upon his Prophet.' (Darqutni, chapter on mentioning the obligation of sending blessings upon the Prophet in tashahhud, p.347, no.1327) This hadith also shows that one should send blessings upon the Prophet. Therefore, according to Imam Shafi'i, it is obligatory to recite durad after the first tashahhud. Note: [1] Some imams and common people have the habit of reciting durad after tashahhud even in the first sitting, so this is a general practice. (2) The hadith about sending blessings after tashahhud is also present, and the school of Imam Shafi'i is also there. [3] Only from the expression of Nur al-Idah does it appear that it is obligatory to stand immediately; however, the clarification of sajda sahw being required is not here, nor is there any hadith for it, so deeming it proper to require sajda sahw for reciting it forgetfully does not seem appropriate.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the Hanafi school regarding one of the wajibat (obligatory acts) of prayer. The specific ruling is that in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, after completing the tashahhud in the first sitting (qada'ah ula), one must stand up immediately for the third rak'ah without reciting anything else (like durad or du'a). This standing is itself wajib according to the Hanafi school. The author then provides the evidence (wajh) from hadith: (1) The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught that in the middle of prayer (i.e., between rak'ahs) one stands after finishing tashahhud, and only in the last sitting does one supplicate. (2) Another hadith describes the Prophet standing so quickly from the first sitting as if on hot stones, indicating he did not delay with additional recitations. Following this, the author includes a note (fa'ida) on the Shafi'i position: Imam Shafi'i considers reciting durad (salawat) after tashahhud in the first sitting to be wajib. The author quotes from an encyclopedia of Shafi'i fiqh to support this. The Shafi'i proofs include the verse of salawat (al-Ahzab 33:56) and hadiths commanding blessings upon the Prophet. The Hanafi response to this is implied in the author's concluding note: While some scholars and laypeople follow the Shafi'i practice, and there is hadith on sending blessings, the Hanafi view is that it is not wajib; moreover, the immediate standing is itself wajib, but requiring sajda sahw for unintentional recitation of durad in the first sitting is not well-justified textually. The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi position and addresses the Shafi'i counterview.

Key Terms
قعدہ اولی (qada'ah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of a specific formula (at-tahiyyatu lillahi...) during sitting in prayer.
سجدہ سہو (sajda sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omissions or additions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on standing immediately after tashahhud in the first sitting?
A) It is fard, and omission invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib, and omission requires sajda sahw.
C) It is sunnah, and omission is makruh but no compensation.
D) It is mubah, and one may recite durad if desired.

Key Takeaway
Standing immediately after tashahhud in the first sitting is wajib; omitting it forgetfully requires sajda sahw.

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Reciting Durad in the First Sitting
Inter-madhhab dispute on reciting durad in the first sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on not reciting durad in the first sitting and evaluate the Shafi'i argument for its obligation.

Core Idea
Reciting durad in the first sitting is wajib according to Shafi'i, but Hanafi school maintains it is not wajib based on prophetic practice.

While the Hanafi school holds that one must stand immediately after tashahhud in the first sitting, Imam al-Shafi'i considers reciting durad (salawat) after tashahhud to be wajib even in the first sitting. This disagreement arises from different interpretations of the same texts. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps us appreciate how usul principles shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Hanafi: After tashahhud in the first sitting, one should stand immediately without reciting durad. Durad is not wajib in the first sitting.
This is based on the hadith where the Prophet stood quickly and the instruction for the middle prayer.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i: Reciting durad after tashahhud in the first sitting is wajib. Omission requires sajda sahw.
The Shafi'i school uses Quran 33:56 and related hadith to support wujub.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proofs
The verse commands sending blessings upon the Prophet. Hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujra teaches the formula. Another hadith says 'There is no prayer for one who does not send blessings upon his Prophet.'
These texts are general and not specific to the first sitting.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the verse and hadith show the virtue and general obligation of sending blessings, but not specifically in the first sitting. The specific practice of the Prophet (immediate standing) restricts the general command.
Hanafi usul: al-amm yufidu al-wujub, but here the amm is restricted by the sunna practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, if one recites durad forgetfully in the first sitting, sajda sahw is required for delaying the wajib. In the Shafi'i school, if one omits durad (even forgetfully), sajda sahw is required. So both require sajda but for opposite actions.
The note in the source mentions that many laypeople follow the Shafi'i practice, but the Hanafi school maintains its position.
