Chapter on the obligatory acts of prayer. The correct recitation in the last sitting (397) and standing for the third without delay after tashahhud. (Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, p.147, no.968) In this hadith, the word 'fa'l-yaqul' is an imperative form indicating obligation. (4) In a hadith it is said: if you recite tashahhud, your prayer will be valid, which shows that tashahhud is obligatory. The hadith is: 'The Messenger of Allah took hold of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and mentioned similar to the dua hadith of al-A'mash: When you say this, you have completed your prayer, if you want to stand then stand, and if you want to sit then sit.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, p.147, no.970) In this hadith it is said that if you recite tashahhud, your prayer will be complete, so it is obligatory. (5) There is an indication in the verse that tashahhud should be recited because it contains salutation upon the Prophet. The verse is: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet; O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace.' (Surah al-Ahzab, 33:56) In this verse, the phrase 'sallimu taslima' points to reciting tashahhud because in tashahhud there is salutation. (6) An athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: Prayer is not valid except with tashahhud.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on one who forgets tashahhud, vol.2, p.134, no.3085) This athar indicates that prayer is not valid without tashahhud, so tashahhud is obligatory. Translation of (397): [11] To stand for the third rak'ah without delay after tashahhud. Explanation: In a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, in the first sitting one should only recite tashahhud; one should not recite durad or du'a. Therefore, after reciting tashahhud, without reciting anything else, one should stand for the third rak'ah. This is also obligatory. Proof: (1) Hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah taught me the tashahhud in the middle of the prayer and at the end... He said: Then if it is in the middle of the prayer, he stood up when he finished his tashahhud, and if it is at the end, he supplicated after his tashahhud as he wished, then made salam.' (Musnad Ahmad, Musnad Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, vol.2, p.44, no.4369) This hadith shows that in the first sitting one should not recite more than tashahhud. (2) From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The Prophet in the two rak'ahs was as if on hot stones.' I said: 'Until he stands?' He said: 'That is intended.' (Nasa'i, chapter on lightening the first tashahhud, p.164, no.717; Abu Dawud, chapter on lightening the sitting, p.151, no.995) This hadith indicates that the Prophet would stand up quickly from the first sitting, showing that one should not recite more than tashahhud. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, in the first sitting one should recite durad after tashahhud. In the encyclopedia, the text is: 'Tashahhud and sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud in every prayer except Fajr: there are two tashahhuds, first tashahhud and last tashahhud. If one omits the first tashahhud and sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud forgetfully, there is no repetition upon him, and upon him are two prostrations of forgetfulness for omitting it.' (Encyclopedia of Imam Shafi'i, chapter on tashahhud and blessing upon the Prophet, vol.2, p.193, no.1456) This passage shows that in the first tashahhud, durad is also obligatory. Their proof: The verse and hadiths in which the virtue of sending blessings after tashahhud is mentioned. (1) The verse: 'Indeed, Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet; O you who have believed, send blessings upon him and greet him with peace.' (Surah al-Ahzab, 33:56) According to this verse, sending blessings once in one's life is fard, and in prayer it is sunnah. (2) Hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujra: ... We said: We know how to greet you, but how should we send blessings upon you? He said: Say: 'O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad...' (Muslim, chapter on blessing upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p.173, no.908/406; Abu Dawud, chapter on blessing upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p.149, no.976) This hadith shows that after tashahhud, one should send blessings upon the Prophet. (3) From Sahl ibn Sa'd: The Prophet said: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not send blessings upon his Prophet.' (Darqutni, chapter on mentioning the obligation of sending blessings upon the Prophet in tashahhud, p.347, no.1327) This hadith also shows that one should send blessings upon the Prophet. Therefore, according to Imam Shafi'i, it is obligatory to recite durad after the first tashahhud. Note: [1] Some imams and common people have the habit of reciting durad after tashahhud even in the first sitting, so this is a general practice. (2) The hadith about sending blessings after tashahhud is also present, and the school of Imam Shafi'i is also there. [3] Only from the expression of Nur al-Idah does it appear that it is obligatory to stand immediately; however, the clarification of sajda sahw being required is not here, nor is there any hadith for it, so deeming it proper to require sajda sahw for reciting it forgetfully does not seem appropriate.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the Hanafi school regarding one of the wajibat (obligatory acts) of prayer. The specific ruling is that in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, after completing the tashahhud in the first sitting (qada'ah ula), one must stand up immediately for the third rak'ah without reciting anything else (like durad or du'a). This standing is itself wajib according to the Hanafi school. The author then provides the evidence (wajh) from hadith: (1) The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught that in the middle of prayer (i.e., between rak'ahs) one stands after finishing tashahhud, and only in the last sitting does one supplicate. (2) Another hadith describes the Prophet standing so quickly from the first sitting as if on hot stones, indicating he did not delay with additional recitations. Following this, the author includes a note (fa'ida) on the Shafi'i position: Imam Shafi'i considers reciting durad (salawat) after tashahhud in the first sitting to be wajib. The author quotes from an encyclopedia of Shafi'i fiqh to support this. The Shafi'i proofs include the verse of salawat (al-Ahzab 33:56) and hadiths commanding blessings upon the Prophet. The Hanafi response to this is implied in the author's concluding note: While some scholars and laypeople follow the Shafi'i practice, and there is hadith on sending blessings, the Hanafi view is that it is not wajib; moreover, the immediate standing is itself wajib, but requiring sajda sahw for unintentional recitation of durad in the first sitting is not well-justified textually. The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi position and addresses the Shafi'i counterview.

Key Terms
قعدہ اولی (qada'ah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of a specific formula (at-tahiyyatu lillahi...) during sitting in prayer.
سجدہ سہو (sajda sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omissions or additions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Shafi'i, what is the ruling on reciting durad after tashahhud in the first sitting?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Mubah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on the status of durad in the first sitting; Hanafi says not wajib, Shafi'i says wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Reciting Durood in First Tashahhud: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Discussion of durood in first tashahhud and sujood as-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting durood in the first tashahhud, explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf regarding sujood as-sahw.

Core Idea
Reciting durood in the first tashahhud is not wajib; forgetting it does not require sujood as-sahw.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether it is obligatory to recite blessings upon the Prophet (durood) in the first sitting of prayer (qa'dah ula). The Shafi'i school holds that it is wajib, citing Quranic and hadith evidence. The Hanafi school disagrees, maintaining that only the final tashahhud requires durood and that the first tashahhud is merely a brief wajib sitting. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the ruling on sujood as-sahw and the practice of Hanafi followers in mixed-madhhab congregations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Reciting durood in the first tashahhud is not wajib. If omitted or recited forgetfully, no sujood as-sahw is required.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that reciting durood in the first tashahhud is wajib; forgetting it would require sujood as-sahw.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites Quran 33:56, the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah teaching durood after tashahhud, and the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not send blessings on his Prophet.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the Quranic verse is general and not specific to prayer; the hadiths refer to the final tashahhud, not the first; and the practice of the Companions does not show obligation in the first sitting.
The text of Nur al-Idah emphasizes that standing up immediately from the first sitting is wajib, implying no extra recitation is required.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: A Hanafi follower behind a Shafi'i imam should remain silent during the first tashahhud; if they forgetfully recite durood, the prayer remains valid without sujood as-sahw.

سجدتا السهو لتركه - ( موسوعة امام شافعی ، باب التشهد والصلوة على النبي ، ج ثانی ص ۱۹۳ نمبر ۱۴۵۶) اس عبارت سے معلوم ہوا کہ پہلے تشہد میں بھی درود شریف واجب ہے۔ وجه : ان کی دلیل وہ آیت اور احادیث ہیں جن میں تشہد کے بعد درود شریف کی فضیلت آئی ہے۔(۱) دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ان الله وملئكته يصلون على النبى يا ايها الذين آمنوا صلوا عليه وسلموا تسليما . آیت ۵۶ ، سورۃ الاحزاب ۳۳) اس آیت سے زندگی میں ایک مرتبہ درود پڑھنا فرض ہے اور نماز میں پڑھنا سنت ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن كعب بن عجرة ..فقلناقدعرفـنـا کیف نسلم علیک فکیف نصلی علیک؟ قال قولوا اللهم صلى على محمد الخ. مسلم شریف، باب الصلوۃ علی النبي بعد التشهد ، ص۱۷۳ نمبر ۹۰۸/۴۰۶ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ علی النبي بعد التشہد ،ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۹۷۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد کے بعد حضور پر درود پڑھنا چاہئے (۳) عن سهل بن سعد ان النبي الله قال لا صــلــة لـم لمن يصل على نبيه الله (دار قطنی ، باب ذکر وجوب الصلوة علی النبی فی التشھد ص ۳۴۷، نمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حضور پر درود پڑھنا چاہئے۔ اسلئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک پہلے تشہد کے بعد بھی درود شریف پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ نوٹ : [1] بعض ائمہ کی اور عوام کی عام عادت یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اولی میں بھی تشہد کے بعد درود شریف پڑھ لیتے ہیں، اس لئے یہ عموم بلوی ہے، (۲) اور تشہد کے بعد درودشریف کی حدیث بھی موجود ہے اور امام شافعی کا مسلک بھی [۳] صرف نور الایضاح کی عبارت سے مترشح ہوتا ہے کہ فورا اٹھنا واجب ہے، لیکن سجدہ سہو لازم ہونے کی تشریح یہاں بھی نہیں ہے، اور نہ اس کے لئے کوئی حدیث ہے اس لئے بھول سے پڑھنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم کرنا مناسب معلوم نہیں ہوتا۔
Sujood as-sahw for leaving it - (Musawwa Imam Shafi'i, chapter of tashahhud and salat upon the Prophet, vol. 2 p. 193 no. 1456) From this phrase it is understood that durood is wajib even in the first tashahhud. Evidence: Their proof is the verse and hadiths that mention the virtue of durood after tashahhud. (1) The proof is the verse: 'Indeed Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet; O you who have believed, ask [Allah to confer] blessing upon him and ask [Allah to grant him] peace.' (Surah al-Ahzab 33:56) From this verse, reciting durood once in a lifetime is fard, and reciting it in prayer is sunnah. (2) There is a hadith from Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah: We said, 'We know how to greet you, but how should we send blessings upon you?' He said, 'Say: O Allah send blessings upon Muhammad etc.' (Muslim, chapter of salat upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p. 173 no. 908/406; Abu Dawud, chapter of salat upon the Prophet after tashahhud, p. 149 no. 976) From this hadith it is understood that durood should be recited after tashahhud. (3) From Sahl ibn Sa'd that the Prophet said, 'There is no prayer for the one who does not send blessings upon his Prophet.' (Dar Qutni, chapter of mentioning obligation of salat upon the Prophet in tashahhud, p. 347 no. 1327) From this hadith also it is understood that durood should be recited. Therefore, according to Imam Shafi'i, reciting durood after the first tashahhud is wajib. Note: [1] Some imams and the common people have the habit of reciting durood after tashahhud in the first sitting, so it is a widespread practice. [2] There is also a hadith about durood after tashahhud, and Imam Shafi'i's madhhab. [3] From the text of Nur al-Idah it is inferred that standing up immediately is wajib, but there is no explanation here of sujood as-sahw becoming necessary, nor is there any hadith for it. Therefore, it does not seem appropriate to require sujood as-sahw for reciting it forgetfully.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding reciting durood (blessings upon the Prophet) in the first tashahhud of prayer. The author first presents the Shafi'i position, which holds that reciting durood in the first tashahhud is wajib. The Shafi'i proofs include the Quranic verse (33:56) commanding blessings on the Prophet, though they interpret it as recommending recitation in prayer rather than obligating it. They also cite hadiths showing the Prophet taught the Companions how to send blessings after tashahhud, and a hadith stating that prayer is incomplete without blessings. The author then provides a note from a Hanafi perspective, clarifying that while some people and even some imams recite durood in the first tashahhud, the Hanafi school does not consider it wajib. The note argues that the text of Nur al-Idah (a Hanafi fiqh work) suggests that standing up immediately after the first tashahhud is wajib, and there is no explicit evidence requiring sujod as-sahw if one forgetfully recites durood. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that reciting durood in the first tashahhud is not wajib, and if recited forgetfully, it does not invalidate the prayer or require sujod as-sahw.

Key Terms
سجدتا السهو (sajdatā al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetful omissions or additions.
قعدہ اولی (qa'dah ūlā): The first sitting in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, after the second rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person forgetfully recites durood (salawat) in the first tashahhud, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) Sujood as-sahw is required
C) The prayer is valid and no sujood as-sahw is required
D) The prayer is valid but one must repeat the durood later

Key Takeaway
Reciting durood in the first tashahhud is not wajib in the Hanafi school, and its forgetful recitation does not require sujood as-sahw.

The Wajib Wording of Salam in Prayer
Determining the obligatory wording of the final salam in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum wajib wording of the final salam in Hanafi prayer and derive the ruling from the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The word 'as-salam' is wajib; the full phrase is sunnah.

The final salam (taslim) is the exit from prayer. But what exactly must be said? The Hanafi school holds that only the word 'as-salam' is obligatory; adding 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' is a confirmed sunnah. This distinction is based on prophetic hadith and has practical implications for every prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the final salam in prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that saying the word 'as-salam' is wajib (obligatory). The prayer is complete with only that word.
The matn explicitly says 'laftz al-salam kahna wajib hai' (saying the word salam is wajib).
2
Locate the first hadith (dalil)
The first proof is the hadith from Abu Sa'id: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its analysis (tahlil) is the taslim.' The word tahlil indicates that the salam is what makes exiting permissible.
Imam al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud report this hadith.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses the term 'taslim', which literally means 'saying salam'. The minimal salam is just the word 'salam'. Therefore, the wajib is the word itself, not the entire greeting.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith but qat'i in dalala for the Hanafis.
4
Consider the second hadith (practice)
The second hadith describes the Prophet saying 'as-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' on both sides. This shows the complete sunnah form, but does not negate that a shorter form is sufficient.
The Hanafis use this to establish the sunnah, not the wajib.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and conclude
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani reportedly considered the full phrase wajib in one narration, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that only 'as-salam' is wajib. This is the position adopted for fatwa.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is and Malikis require the full 'as-salamu alaykum' as wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۹۸) [۱۲] لفظ السلام کہنا نہ علیکم ۔ تشریح : لفظ السلام، کہنا واجب ہے اسی سے نماز پوری ہو جائے گی ، اس کے بعد علیکم ورحمۃ اللہ تک کہنا سنت ہے، یہ کہنا چاہئے لیکن واجب نہیں۔ وجه (ا) عن ابي سعيد قال قال رسول الله الا الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم ۔ (ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوۃ وتحلیلها ص ۶۶ نمبر ۲۳۸ رابوداؤد شریف ، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما رفع رأسه من آخر رکعتہ ، ص ۱۰۰، نمبر ۶۱۸ ) اس حدیث میں صرف سلام کو نماز سے نکلنے کا سبب قرار دیا ہے ، اس لئے صرف سلام واجب ہے۔(۲) دوسری حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله ان النبي عل كان يسلم عن يمينه وعن شماله حتى يرى بياض خده، السلام عليكم ورحمة الله ، السلام علیکم ورحمة الله (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی السلام ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۱۹۹۶) بخاری شریف، باب التسلیم ،ص ۱۱۶، نمبر ۸۳۷/ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی التسليم فى الصلوۃ ص ۶۵ نمبر ۲۹۵) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ سلام پھیرنا چاہئے اس طرح کہ کنارے والوں کو گال نظر آنے لگے۔
Translation: (398) [12] The word 'as-salam' and not 'alaykum. Explanation: Saying the word 'as-salam' is wajib; with it the prayer is completed. After that, saying 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' is sunnah; it should be said but is not wajib. Evidence: (1) From Abu Sa'id that the Messenger of Allah said, 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its analysis is the taslim (salam).' (Tirmidhi, chapter on the prohibition of prayer and its analysis, p. 66 no. 238; Abu Dawud, chapter on the imam who has an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, p. 100 no. 618) In this hadith, only salam is made the cause of exiting prayer, so only salam is wajib. (2) Another hadith: From Abdullah that the Prophet used to say salam to his right and to his left until the whiteness of his cheek could be seen: 'as-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah, as-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on salam, p. 151 no. 1996; Bukhari, chapter on salam, p. 116 no. 837; Tirmidhi, chapter on salam in prayer, p. 65 no. 295) From this hadith it is established that one should turn the salam so that those on the sides can see his cheek.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This ruling from the matn states that the obligatory part of the final salam is the word 'as-salam' (without 'alaykum). The author explains that saying 'as-salam' is wajib, and with it the prayer is concluded. Saying 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' is sunnah and should be done, but if omitted, the prayer is still valid. The first proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet says that the tahlil (opening of prayer) is the takbir, and the tahlil (exiting) is the taslim. This indicates that the essence of the salam is the word 'as-salam'. The second proof is the practice of the Prophet who would say 'as-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to both sides, but the hadith does not specify that the full phrase is obligatory. The Hanafi school thus distinguishes between the wajib (the word 'salam') and the sunnah (the full phrase).

Key Terms
تحلیل (tahlil): The act that makes something permissible; here, the salam that makes exiting prayer permissible
تسلیم (taslim): The greeting of salam at the end of prayer
واجب (wajib): Obligatory according to zanni evidence; omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum wording required for the final salam in prayer?
A) 'as-salamu alaykum'
B) 'as-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'
C) 'as-salam' only
D) 'alaykum' only

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the final salam in prayer is valid with just the word 'as-salam'; the full greeting is sunnah.

Qunut in Witr Prayer is Wajib
Establishing the obligation of qunut in witr prayer through proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in witr and identify the three proofs that establish its obligation.

Core Idea
Qunut in witr is wajib — the Prophet taught it and practiced it.

In this passage, the author clearly states that reciting the qunut supplication in the witr prayer is wajib (obligatory). To support this ruling, three proofs are presented: a hadith where the Prophet specifically taught qunut words, another hadith showing his own practice, and a statement from the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i declaring that witr is incomplete without qunut. Understanding these proofs will strengthen your conviction in this established Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage opens by stating that qunut in witr is wajib. Identify what 'wajib' means in Hanafi fiqh — an act whose omission without excuse is sinful and requires compensation (sujood as-sahw) if forgotten.
Wajib is one step below fard but still binding.
2
Analyze the first proof (hadith of al-Hasan)
The Prophet taught al-Hasan ibn Ali specific words to say in witr. This indicates that qunut is not optional but a taught component of the prayer.
Hadith from Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
3
Analyze the second proof (practice of the Prophet)
Ubayy ibn Ka'b reported that the Prophet recited qunut in witr before ruku. This shows the Prophet's consistent practice, which is a source of obligation.
Hadith from Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah.
4
Analyze the third proof (statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i)
The tabi'i said, 'There is no witr without qunut.' Though not a primary source, this statement reflects the understanding of the early generation and is taken as evidence of obligation by the Hanafi school.
From Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
The passage implicitly contrasts with other schools: Shafi'is consider qunut sunnah, while Hanafis consider it wajib. Note that the practical difference is that a Hanafi must perform sujood as-sahw if qunut is forgotten, whereas a Shafi'i does not.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۳۹۹) [۱۳] وتر میں قنوت پڑھنا۔ تشریح : وتر میں دعاء قنوت پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ وجه (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ قال الحسن بن على علمني رسول الله لا لا ل ل له كلمات اقولهن في الوتر . (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب القنوت فی الوتر ،ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۴۲۵ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی القنوت فی الوتر ،ص ۱۶۵، نمبر ۱۱۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دعاء قنوت خاص طور پر سکھلائی جس سے قنوت کی اہمیت معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ (۲) عن ابي بن كعب ان رسول الله قنت فى الوتر قبل الركوع. (ابوداؤد شریف، باب القنوت فی الوتر ، ص۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۴۲۷ رنسائی شریف، باب ذکر اختلاف الفاظ الناقلين بخير ابی بن کعب فی الوترص ۲۴۳، نمبر ۱۷۰۰ار ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء في القنوت قبل الرکوع و بعدہ ،ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۱۱۸۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وتر میں دعاء قنوت پڑھے ۔ (۳) عن ابراهیم قال لا وتر الا بقنوت ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب من قال لا وتر الا بقوت، ج ثانی، ص ۱۰۲، نمبر ۶۹۵۹) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ قنوت کے بغیر وتر نہیں ہے جس سے وجوب کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔
Translation: (399) [13] Reciting qunut in witr. Explanation: Reciting the qunut supplication in witr is wajib. Evidence: (1) There is a hadith: 'Al-Hasan ibn Ali said: The Messenger of Allah taught me the words I say in witr.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on qunut in witr, p. 213 no. 1425; Ibn Majah, chapter on qunut in witr, p. 165 no. 1178) In this hadith, the qunut supplication was specifically taught, indicating its importance. (2) From Ubayy ibn Ka'b that the Messenger of Allah recited qunut in witr before ruku. (Abu Dawud, chapter on qunut in witr, p. 213 no. 1427; Nasa'i, chapter on differences of narrators regarding Ubayy ibn Ka'b in witr, p. 243 no. 1700; Ibn Majah, chapter on qunut before and after ruku, p. 166 no. 1182) In this hadith, it is recorded that the Prophet recited qunut in witr. (3) From Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i): 'There is no witr without qunut.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who said no witr without qunut, vol. 2, p. 102 no. 6959) This statement of a tabi'i shows that there is no witr without qunut, which indicates obligation.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that reciting qunut (a specific supplication) in the witr prayer is wajib. The author provides three proofs: (1) The Prophet specifically taught Al-Hasan ibn Ali some words to say in witr, implying that qunut is an essential part of the prayer. (2) The Prophet himself is reported to have recited qunut in witr before the ruku. (3) The tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stated that witr is not valid without qunut, which underscores the obligation. The Hanafi school therefore considers qunut a wajib act in witr; if it is omitted intentionally, the prayer is not complete, and if forgotten, sujood as-sahw is required.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer after rising from ruku or before ruku, according to different schools
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayers, consisting of three rak'ahs in the Hanafi school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After the second sujood
B) Before ruku in the last rak'ah
C) After ruku in the last rak'ah
D) Before the takbir of the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Qunut in witr is wajib based on the Prophet's teaching and practice; it must be recited before ruku in the last rak'ah, and if forgotten, sujood as-sahw is required.

The Extra Takbirs of Eid Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah?
Proving the obligation of additional takbirs in the two Eid prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the extra takbirs in the Eid prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The six extra takbirs in the Eid prayer are wajib, not mere sunnah.

The additional takbirs recited during the two Eid prayers are a distinctive feature of the Hanafi school. While all schools agree on the practice, they differ on its legal status and number. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that these takbirs are wajib, supported by the practice of the Prophet as reported by the Companions Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the extra takbirs (takbīr zawā'id) in the two Eid prayers. The ruling is that they are wajib (obligatory).
The term 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh means an obligation that is not as strong as fard but requires compensation if omitted.
2
Understand the disagreement
Note that there is ikhtilaf on the number (Hanafi says six, Shafi'i says seven) but consensus on the existence of extra takbirs.
The disagreement on number does not affect the ruling of wajib.
3
Examine the dalil
The evidence is the hadith where Abu Musa states the Prophet said four takbirs in the Eid prayer (including the opening takbir). Hudhayfah confirms.
The hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and others.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Hanafi usul: the Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l) indicates wujub. The number interpretation: 'four' includes the opening takbir, so three additional in first rak'ah; similar in second.
This interpretation is specific to the Hanafi school.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf considered it sunnah, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is wajib following Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi is wajib; those who follow Abu Yusuf's view are a minority.

Translation: (200) [14] The additional takbirs of the two Eids. Explanation: The additional takbirs of the two Eids are wajib. There is disagreement about the number of additional takbirs, but it is agreed that they are additional takbirs. Evidence: (1) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman asked: 'How did the Messenger of Allah say takbir on the days of Adha and Fitr?' Abu Musa said: 'He would say four takbirs, like the takbirs over the deceased.' Hudhayfah said, 'He spoke the truth.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on takbir in the two Eids, p. 172 no. 153; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the report regarding four takbirs, vol. 3, p. 208 no. 6183; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on takbir in prayer on the day of Eid, vol. 3, p. 167 no. 5704)
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage states that the extra takbirs in the Eid prayers (both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha) are wajib according to the Hanafi school. The author notes that there is a difference of opinion regarding the exact number of additional takbirs (the Hanafi school says six: three in the first rak'ah after the opening takbir and three in the second rak'ah after the takbir of standing), but all agree that there are additional takbirs beyond the standard ones. The evidence provided is the statement of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, who reported that the Prophet said four takbirs in the Eid prayer (including the opening takbir), and Hudhayfah confirmed this. This indicates that the additional takbirs are an established practice. The commentary emphasizes that these takbirs are wajib, meaning their omission requires compensation (sujood as-sahw).

Key Terms
تكبير زوائد (takbīr zawā'id): The extra takbirs recited in the two Eid prayers beyond the standard takbirs of the prayer
عیدین (īdayn): The two Islamic festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha

The Opening Takbir: Specified for Every Prayer
Clarifying that the opening takbir is not exclusive to Eid prayers and explaining the nuanced obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the wajib and sunnah aspects of the opening takbir in the Hanafi school and apply the ruling when a different glorification is used.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is wajib for every prayer, but any word of glorification fulfills the fard; 'Allahu Akbar' is the sunnah.

Many assume that saying 'Allahu Akbar' is absolutely obligatory for starting prayer. The Hanafi school, drawing from Al-Hidayah, teaches a nuanced view: the essential obligation is to begin with any expression that glorifies Allah, while the specific wording 'Allahu Akbar' is the established sunnah. Understanding this distinction safeguards one from unnecessary rigidity while honoring the prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states that the takbir is specified for opening every prayer, not just the Eid prayers. This establishes that the opening takbir is a general requirement.
The matn counters a common misconception that the takbir is only emphasized in Eid.
2
Parse the commentary's core distinction
The commentary explicitly differentiates between fard (any word glorifying Allah) and sunnah (the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar'). This is the key legal nuance.
The commentary cites Al-Hidayah as the source for this distinction.
3
Understand the hierarchical implications
If a person says 'Allah al-Azim' or another glorification, the fard is fulfilled and the prayer is valid, but the sunnah is missed. If one omits any glorification, the prayer is invalid.
This hierarchy (fard vs. sunnah) is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers 'Allahu Akbar' alone as a pillar (rukn); any substitute invalidates the prayer. Recognizing this contrast sharpens the Hanafi position.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for muftis in mixed-madhhab contexts.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a person who begins prayer with 'Allahu al-Azim' due to a slip of the tongue, rule on validity and recommend the optimal practice.
The ruling: prayer is valid but one should strive to say 'Allahu Akbar' as the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۰۱) [۱۵] ہر نماز کو شروع کرنے کے لئے تکبیر متعین کرنا ، خاص عیدین کے لئے ہی ضروری نہیں۔ تشریح : صرف عیدین میں اللہ اکبر، کہہ کر نماز شروع کرے ایسا نہیں ہے، بلکہ تمام نمازوں کو اللہ اکبر، کہہ کر شروع کرے اور تحریمہ باند ھے۔ ہدایہ کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اللہ کی تعظیم کے لئے کسی بھی لفظ سے نماز شروع کرنا فرض ہے، البتہ اللہ اکبر، کہنا سنت ہے۔
Translation: (401) [15] Specifying the takbir for opening every prayer, not only for the two Eids. Explanation: It is not that one should start the prayer only in the two Eids by saying 'Allahu Akbar'; rather, one should start all prayers with 'Allahu Akbar' and tie the tahrimah. From the text of Hidayah, it is understood that starting the prayer with any word of glorification of Allah is fard, but saying 'Allahu Akbar' specifically is sunnah.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the opening takbir (tahrimah) is required for every prayer, not just the Eid prayers. The matn emphasizes that the takbir is specified for opening all prayers. The commentary explains that one should not restrict the awareness of saying 'Allahu Akbar' to Eid; rather, every prayer is initiated with 'Allahu Akbar'. The author then references Al-Hidayah to make a subtle distinction: the actual fard (obligatory) is to start the prayer with any word that glorifies Allah, such as 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allah al-Azim', but the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah. This means that if someone intentionally says 'Allah al-Azim' instead of 'Allahu Akbar', the prayer is valid (obligation fulfilled) but the sunnah is missed. This nuanced view is unique to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer begin and prohibits actions outside prayer
تکبیر افتتاح (takbīr iftitāh): The takbir recited at the beginning of prayer to enter into it

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is invalid
B) The prayer is valid but the sunnah is missed
C) The prayer is valid and it is equally rewardable
D) The prayer is valid but sujood as-sahw is required

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is wajib for every prayer; the essential obligation is any glorification, while 'Allahu Akbar' is the sunnah.

Takbir al-Iftitah for Every Prayer
Ruling that takbir al-iftitah is required for every prayer, not just Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the opening takbir (tahrima) and distinguish between the fard and sunnah components.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is fard in every prayer; any word of glorification suffices; 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah.

This lesson clarifies that the opening takbir is not exclusive to Eid prayers but is required for every salah. It also resolves a common confusion: the obligatory element is the act of glorifying Allah at the start, while the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the prophetic practice (sunnah). The passage draws on the Quran, hadith, and the authority of al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the opening takbir (tahrima) at the start of every prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is fard (obligatory) in every salah, not just the Eid prayers.
The word 'fard' here means the act of consecration is mandatory; without it the prayer is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites two Quranic verses and a hadith. The first verse (Surah al-A'la 87:15) commands mentioning the Lord's name and praying. The second (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:3) commands magnifying the Lord. The hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi describes the Prophet's practice of saying 'Allahu Akbar' when starting prayer.
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah and is considered a sahih report.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'fakabbir' (magnify) in Surah al-Muddaththir is interpreted as a command to say a word of exaltation at the start of prayer. The verse does not specify the wording, indicating that any expression of glorification fulfills the command. The hadith shows the specific sunnah practice.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation), but here the command is general, so the fard is the concept of takbir, not a specific phrase.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the opening takbir must be specifically 'Allahu Akbar'. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that any word of glorification (e.g., 'Allahu Azim', 'Subhan Allah') suffices for the fard, provided it is uttered with the intention of tahrima.
The intra-Hanafi difference (wajib vs fard) is resolved: the relied-upon view is fard.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The passage relies on the text of al-Hidayah, which is a central Hanafi reference. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the fard is the act of takbir, and 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah mu'akkadah.
This position is based on the general command in the Quran and the flexibility of the language.

Translation: (401) [15] Specifying the takbir for opening every prayer, not only for the two Eids. Explanation: It is not that one should start prayer only in Eid with 'Allahu Akbar', rather all prayers should be started with 'Allahu Akbar' (and tie the tahrima). From the expression of Hidayah, it appears that starting prayer with any word of glorification of Allah is fard, but saying 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah. Evidence: (1) In the verse: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray.' (Surah al-A'la, 87:15). (2) In the verse: 'And your Lord magnify.' (Surah al-Muddaththir, 74:3). This verse commands saying 'Allahu Akbar'. (3) I heard Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi say: When the Messenger of Allah stood for prayer, he faced the qibla, raised his hands, and said 'Allahu Akbar'. (Ibn Majah, Bab Iftitah al-Salah, no. 803). This hadith shows that prayer should be started with 'Allahu Akbar'.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs specifying that takbir al-iftitah is required for every prayer, not only for Eid. The author clarifies that the ruling is not limited to Eid prayers. Furthermore, the text from al-Hidayah is referenced to indicate that the actual fard (obligation) is to start the prayer with any word that glorifies Allah, while the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah. Two Quranic verses are presented as proofs: Surah al-A'la (87:15) commands mentioning the Lord's name and praying, and Surah al-Muddaththir (74:3) commands magnifying the Lord. A hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi describes the Prophet's practice of saying 'Allahu Akbar' upon starting prayer. This establishes that the opening takbir is an integral part of the prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the fard of tahrima (the act of consecration) and the sunnah way of performing it with the specific wording.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrima): The opening takbir that marks the commencement of prayer and makes previously permissible actions (like eating, talking) prohibited (haram) during prayer.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir (tahrima) is fard in every prayer; any word of glorification suffices, though 'Allahu Akbar' is the sunnah.

Takbir for Ruku' in the Second Rak'ah of Eid Prayer
Ruling that takbir for ruku' in second rak'ah of Eid is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the takbir for ruku' in the second rak'ah of Eid is wajib and identify the proof from the practice of Ibn Mas'ud.

Core Idea
The takbir for ruku' in Eid is wajib, just like in every prayer, and is separate from the extra takbirs.

In the Eid prayer, there are extra takbirs that some may confuse with the normal takbirs of the prayer. This lesson clarifies that the takbir said when going into ruku' in the second rak'ah is the same wajib takbir as in any other prayer, distinct from the extra takbirs. Understanding this distinction ensures you fulfill the wajib acts of prayer correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Focus on the second rak'ah of Eid prayer. The act in question is saying 'Allahu Akbar' when moving into ruku' (bowing).
This is separate from the extra takbirs of Eid which are said after recitation.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school rules that this takbir is wajib (obligatory) in every prayer, including Eid. Omitting it intentionally or unintentionally requires sajdah al-sahw if not compensated.
Wajib means it is required but not at the level of fard; omission is rectifiable.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The primary evidence is the narration from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) describing the Eid prayer. He said: 'He said takbir four times, then recited, then said takbir and bowed...' This shows the takbir for ruku' is performed after the extra takbirs.
See Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'then said takbir and bowed' indicates a distinct takbir for ruku', separate from the four extra takbirs. This confirms that the ruku' takbir is a regular part of the prayer.
The companion's practice is authoritative (qawl al-sahabi) and constitutes a proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the practical application
In practice, in the second rak'ah of Eid, after recitation, the imam says four extra takbirs (raising hands), then says 'Allahu Akbar' while going into ruku'. Both are wajib, but they are separate acts.
Confusing them could lead to missing the ruku' takbir, necessitating sajdah al-sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۰۲) [۱۲] رکوع کی تکبیر عیدین کی دوسری رکعت میں ۔
تشریح : عید کی تکبیر زوائد کے علاوہ جب رکوع میں جائے تو اللہ اکبر کہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن ابى حميد الساعدى .... فاذا اراد ان يركع رفع يديه حتى يحاذى بهما منكبيه ثم قال الله اكبر . ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی وصف الصلوۃ ، باب منه، ص ۸۲ نمبر ۳۰۴) (۲) سل هذا لعبد الله ابن مسعود ، فسأله فقال ابن مسعود : يكبر اربعا ، ثم يقرأ ، ثم يكبر فيركع ، ثم يقوم في الثانية فيقرأ ، ثم يكبر أربعا بعد القرأة - ( مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التكبير في الصلوة يوم العيد، ج ثالث ص ۱۶۷، نمبر ۵۷۰۵/مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب ۴۲۰، في التكبير في العيدين واختلافهم فیہ، ج اول ص ۴۹۴ نمبر ۵۷۰۴) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ تکبیر زوائد کے علاوہ رکوع کی تکبیر کہ کر رکوع میں جائے۔
Translation: (402) [12] Takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of the two Eids. Explanation: In addition to the extra takbirs of Eid, when going into ruku', one says 'Allahu Akbar'. Evidence: (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: ... when he wanted to bow, he raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then said 'Allahu Akbar'. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Wasf al-Salah, no. 304). (2) Ask this of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, so they asked him, and Ibn Mas'ud said: 'He said takbir four times, then recited, then said takbir and bowed, then stood for the second, recited, then said takbir four times after recitation.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 5705; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 5704). This companion's statement shows that besides extra takbirs, one says the takbir for ruku' and bows.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling clarifying the takbir for ruku' in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer. The author explains that in the second rak'ah, after completing the extra takbirs (which come after recitation), one says 'Allahu Akbar' when going into ruku'. Two proofs are given: first, a general hadith from Abu Humayd describing the Prophet's practice of saying takbir when bowing; second, a specific report from Ibn Mas'ud describing the Eid prayer: he said takbir four times (the extra ones) in the first rak'ah, then recited and bowed; then in the second rak'ah, he recited and then said takbir four times (the extra ones) after recitation, then bowed. The takbir for ruku' is separate from the extra takbirs. The Hanafi school considers this takbir for ruku' as part of the normal prayer, not an extra wajib.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الركوع (takbirat al-ruku'): The takbir said when moving into the bowing position in prayer, distinct from the extra takbirs of Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is only for the imam.

Key Takeaway
The takbir for ruku' in Eid prayer is wajib and is distinct from the extra takbirs; its ruling is the same as in any other prayer.

Jahr (Loud Recitation) in Seven Places
Ruling with proof: seven prayers requiring loud recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven prayers where loud recitation is wajib for the imam and explain the consequence of reciting incorrectly.

Core Idea
Loud recitation in seven specific prayers is wajib; a mistake requires sajdah sahw.

In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's recitation varies between silent and loud in prescribed prayers. This lesson identifies the seven places where jahr (loud recitation) is wajib, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as transmitted by Anas. Missing this wajib or switching recitation type intentionally or forgetfully necessitates sajdah sahw. We'll walk through the list, the ruling, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
Recognize that the author states loud recitation in these seven places is 'wajib'. In Hanafi terminology, wajib is a level between fard and sunnah; omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
Compare to fard: missing a fard invalidates the prayer entirely.
2
List the seven prayers
Memorize the seven: Fajr (both rak'ahs), first two rak'ahs of Maghrib, first two rak'ahs of Isha, Jumu'ah (both rak'ahs), Eid (both rak'ahs), Tarawih (all rak'ahs), and Witr in Ramadan. Note that qada (make-up) of these prayers also requires jahr.
All other prayers are recited silently.
3
Understand the consequence of error
If the imam recites aloud in a silent prayer, or silently in a loud prayer, even by one or two verses, sajdah sahw becomes wajib. This applies whether the error was intentional or forgetful.
Sajdah sahw is performed before the salam.
4
Examine the proof
The author cites the hadith of Anas about Jibril teaching the Prophet the five daily prayers. In this hadith, the Prophet recited silently in Zuhr and Asr, and aloud in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha. This is the basis for the ruling.
The Hanafi school uses this hadith to derive wujub, while other schools consider it sunnah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider jahr in these prayers as sunnah, not wajib. The Hanafi position is based on the principle that the Prophet's consistent practice indicates obligation.
This difference affects whether sajdah sahw is required for omitting jahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۰۳) [۱۷] امام قرآت جہر کر کے کرے فجر میں، مغرب اور عشاء کی پہلی دورکعتوں میں ، چاہے قضا ہو، جمعہ میں، عیدین میں ، تروایح میں ، اور رمضان کی وتر میں ۔
تشریح : ان سات مقامات پر قرآت زور سے پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ [1] فجر کی دونوں رکعتوں میں [۲] مغرب کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں ۔[۳] عشاء کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں [۴] جمعہ کی دونوں رکعتوں میں [۵] عیدین کی دونوں رکعتوں میں [1] تروایح کی تمام رکعتوں میں (۷) رمضان کی وتر میں قرآت زور سے پڑھنا واجب ہے۔۔ ایک دو آیت جہری کو سری پڑھ لے یا سری کو جہری پڑھ لے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہو جائے اس کے لئے کوئی حدیث نہیں ملی۔
وجه (1) عن أنس أن جبرئيل اتى النبى الله بمكة حين زالت الشمس و أمره أن يوذن للناس بالصلوة حين فرضت عليهم ، فقام جبرئيل امام النبي علم و قامو الناس خلف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : فصلى أربع ركعات لا يجهر فيها بقرأة.... ثم امهل حتى اذا دخل وقت العصر ، صلى بهم أربع ركعات لا . بـالـقـرأة .... ثم امهل حتى اذا وجبت الشمس صلى بهم ثلاث ركعات يجهر في ركعتين بالقرأة و لا يجهر فيها
Translation: (403) [17] The imam should recite aloud in Fajr, the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, even if qada, Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Explanation: In these seven places, reciting aloud is wajib. [1] Both rak'ahs of Fajr [2] First two rak'ahs of Maghrib [3] First two rak'ahs of Isha [4] Both rak'ahs of Jumu'ah [5] Both rak'ahs of Eid [6] All rak'ahs of Tarawih [7] Witr in Ramadan: reciting aloud is wajib. If one recites a verse or two aloud that should be silent, or silent that should be aloud, then sajdah sahw becomes necessary. There is no hadith found for this. Evidence: (1) From Anas that Jibril came to the Prophet in Mecca when the sun passed its zenith and commanded him to call the people to prayer... He prayed four rak'ahs without reciting aloud... then waited until Asr time, prayed four rak'ahs without reciting aloud... then waited until sunset, prayed three rak'ahs, reciting aloud in two rak'ahs and not reciting aloud in...
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof enumerating seven prayers where the imam must recite aloud. The author lists them: Fajr (both rak'ahs), first two of Maghrib, first two of Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. The ruling is wajib; if one intentionally or mistakenly changes the recitation type (jahran or sirran), sajdah sahw is required. The proof is a hadith from Anas about Jibril teaching the Prophet the prayers: he prayed Zuhr and Asr silently, and Maghrib and Isha with loud recitation in the first two rak'ahs. The hadith is cut off in the OCR, but the principle is clear. The Hanafi school holds that loud recitation in these places is wajib based on the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud or audible recitation in prayer, as opposed to sirr (silent).
سجدہ سہو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an error in prayer, such as reciting aloud when silent or vice versa.

The Takbir for Bowing in the Second Rak'ah of Eid Prayer
Ruling with proof for takbirat al-rukū' in second rak'ah of Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the takbir for bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer and identify the evidence from hadith and qawl sahabi.

Core Idea
The takbir for bowing in Eid prayer is a separate wajib from the extra takbirs — omission requires sajdah sahw.

In Eid prayer, there are additional takbirs (takbirat zawa'id) said before recitation. But besides those, when moving into bowing (ruku'), one must also say 'Allahu Akbar'. This lesson clarifies that this takbir is an obligatory (wajib) act, distinct from the extra takbirs, and provides evidence from the Prophet's practice and from Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the takbir for bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer. Its ruling is wajib (obligatory).
This is separate from the extra takbirs (takbirat zawa'id).
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is from two sources: a hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi describing the Prophet's practice of saying takbir when bowing, and the qawl sahabi of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud specifically for Eid prayer.
The hadith is general; Ibn Mas'ud's practice applies it to Eid.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's practice establishes that taking for bowing is part of every prayer. Ibn Mas'ud's explicit practice for Eid confirms it is also required there, as a separate wajib beyond the extra takbirs.
Thus, the Hanafi school treats it as wajib.

Chapter on the obligatory acts of the two Eid prayers specifically (402) And the takbir of bowing in the second rak'ah of the two Eids (403) And the imam's audible recitation in Fajr, the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, even if qada, Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Evidence: (1) The verse: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' (Surah al-A'la 87:15) (2) The verse: 'And magnify your Lord' (Surah al-Muddathir 74:3) This verse says: Say Allahu Akbar. (3) I heard Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi say: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he stood for prayer, faced the qibla, raised his hands, and said: Allahu Akbar (Ibn Majah, chapter on opening prayer, p. 114, no. 803). This hadith says to begin prayer with 'Allahu Akbar'. Translation: (402) [12] The takbir of bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid. Commentary: Apart from the additional takbirs of Eid, when going into bowing, one says Allahu Akbar. Evidence: (1) From Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: When he wanted to bow, he raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then said Allahu Akbar (Tirmidhi, chapter on description of prayer, p. 82, no. 304). (2) Ask 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about this. He was asked and said: He says takbir four times, then recites, then says takbir and bows, then stands for the second and recites, then says takbir four times after recitation (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on takbir in Eid prayer, vol. 3, p. 167, no. 5705; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter 420, on takbir in the two Eids and their differences, vol. 1, p. 494, no. 5704). This companion's statement indicates that in addition to the extra takbirs, one says the takbir for bowing and then bows.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of the textbook 'Thamaratun Najah' on the obligatory acts of the two Eid prayers. The first obligatory act discussed is the takbir for bowing in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer. The author clarifies that this takbir is separate from the extra takbirs (takbirat zawa'id) that are said before recitation. The evidence is drawn from two sources: first, the general practice of the Prophet in bowing as reported by Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, where he would raise his hands and say Allahu Akbar when bowing; second, the specific practice of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud in Eid prayer, where he would say takbir four times after recitation in the second rak'ah, which includes the takbir for bowing. The Hanafi position is that this takbir is obligatory (wajib) in the Eid prayer.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الركوع (takbīrat al-rukū'): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' when moving into bowing position in prayer.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbīrāt al-zawā'id): The additional takbirs in Eid prayer before recitation; in the first rak'ah, three takbirs after the opening takbir; in the second, three takbirs after the takbir for standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Audible Recitation (Jahr) in Seven Prayers
Ruling stating wajib of jahr in seven prayers with multiple proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven prayers where jahr is wajib and explain the consequence of mistakenly switching jahr and sirr.

Core Idea
Audible recitation in seven specific prayers is wajib; mistaken silence or audibility requires sajdah sahw.

This passage establishes a key wajib of the imam: audible recitation in seven designated prayers. Understanding these prayers and the ruling helps avoid errors that necessitate prostration of forgetfulness. The author provides multiple proofs from hadith and athar, demonstrating the Hanafi school's reliance on sound evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Seven Prayers
List the seven prayers mentioned: Fajr (both rak'ahs), Maghrib (first two), Isha (first two), Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Note that each has specific rak'ahs for jahr.
For Maghrib and Isha, only the first two rak'ahs are jahr; the last ones are sirr.
2
Understand the Hukm Level
The text explicitly states jahr is 'wajib' in these prayers. Distinguish wajib from fard: omission of a wajib requires sajdah sahw, not repetition of the prayer.
Hanafi usul: a wajib is established by zanni evidence, yet binding.
3
Recognize the Consequence of Mistake
If the imam recites audibly where sirr is required, or silently where jahr is required, sajdah sahw becomes necessary. This compensates for the missed wajib.
Sajdah sahw is performed after the salam with two prostrations.
4
Analyze the Primary Proof (Hadith of Jibril)
The hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in the five prescribed prayers clearly establishes the pattern: jahr in Fajr (both), Maghrib (first two), Isha (first two), and sirr in others. This is the foundational evidence.
The hadith is from Darqutni; its chain is acceptable for zanni thubut.
5
Review Additional Proofs and Qiyas
The author cites specific hadiths for each prayer: Fajr (Ibn Abbas), Maghrib (Jubayr ibn Mut'im), Isha (al-Bara'), Jumu'ah/Eid (Nu'man ibn Bashir). For Eid, qiyas is applied from Jumu'ah based on the common 'illa of large congregation.
The qiyas panel from the analytical toolbox shows the reasoning: Jumu'ah (asl) → Eid (far) via 'illa of gathering.

(بخاری شریف، باب الجهر بقراءة صلوة اصبح ص ۱۲۵ نمبر ۷۷۳ر مسلم شریف ، باب الجهر بالقراءة في الصبح والقراءة على الجن ص ۱۸۹ نمبر ۱۰۰۶/۴۴۹) اس باب میں جنات کے سامنے فجر کی نماز میں جہری قرآت کرنے کی کئی حدیثیں ذکر کی گئی ہیں ۔ جن سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ فجر کی نماز میں جہری قرآت ہے اگر خود امام ہوتو ۔ (۳) مغرب میں جہری قرآت کی دلیل یہ ہے ۔ جبیر بن مطعم عن ابيه قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قرء في المغرب بالطور . ( بخاری شریف، باب الجبر في المغرب ، ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۷۶۵ ) سمعت کے لفظ سے پتہ چلا کہ آپ نے قرآت جہری کی ہے تب ہی تو راوی نے سورہ طور سنی۔ (۴) عشا کی نماز میں جہری قرآت کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ سمعت البراء ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم كان في سفر فقرء في العشاء في احدى الركعتين بالتين والزيتون - ( بخاری شریف، باب الجهر فی العشاء، ص ۱۲۴، نمبر ۷۶۷ مسلم شریف ، باب القراءة في العشاء ، ص ۱۹۳، نمبر ۱۰۳۷٫۴۶۴) یہاں بھی سمعت کے لفظ سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے عشا کی نماز میں قرآت جہری کی ہے۔ (۵) جمعہ اور عیدین میں جہری قرآت کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن النعمان بن بشير قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ في العيدين و في الجمعة وسبح اسم ربک الاعلى و هل أتاك حديث الغاشية (مسلم شریف ، باب ما يقر آفی الجمعۃ ، ص ۱۳۵۱، نمبر ۲۰۲۸/۸۷۸ و ابو داود شریف، باب ما يقر آفی الجمعۃ ، ص ۱۶۹، نمبر۱۱۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور یہ عیدین میں اور جمعہ میں سح اسم ، اور ھل اتاک حدیث الغاشیہ پڑھتے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں قرآت زور سے کرتے تھے تب ہی تو صحابہ نے حضور کی قرآت سنی۔ (۶) قلت لعطاء : ما يجهر به الصوت من القرأة من صلاة الليل والنهار من المكتوبة ؟ قال : الصبح والاوليين العشاء ، و الاوليين المغرب ، و الجمعة اذا كانت في جماعة ، فاما اذا كان المرأ وحده فلا - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ما كجهر من القرآة فيه من الصلوة ، ج ثانى ، ص ۶۵ نمبر ۲۶۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جمعہ میں بھی قرآت زور سے کی جائے گی ، اور اسی پر عیدین کو قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ (۷) تراویح میں اور رمضان کے وتر میں جہری قرآت کرے اس کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلي في المسجد فصلى بصلاته ناس ثم صلى من القابلة فكثر الناس ثم اجتمعوا من الليلة الثالثة فلم
Translation: (403) [17] The imam recites audibly in Fajr, the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, even if qada, Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Commentary: In these seven places, audible recitation is wajib. [1] Both rak'ahs of Fajr; [2] First two rak'ahs of Maghrib; [3] First two rak'ahs of Isha; [4] Both rak'ahs of Jumu'ah; [5] Both rak'ahs of the two Eids; [6] All rak'ahs of Tarawih; [7] Witr in Ramadan. Audible recitation is wajib. If one recites audibly in a silent prayer or silently in an audible prayer, sujūd sahw becomes necessary. No hadith is found [for the last part?]. Evidence: (1) From Anas that Jibril came to the Prophet in Mecca when the sun passed zenith and ordered him to call the people to prayer when it was prescribed for them. Then Jibril led the Prophet and the people prayed behind the Messenger of Allah. He said: He prayed four rak'ahs without audible recitation... then waited until the time of Asr, he prayed four rak'ahs without audible recitation... then waited until sunset, he prayed three rak'ahs, reciting audibly in two rak'ahs and not audibly in the third. Then he waited until a third of the night had passed, he prayed four rak'ahs, reciting audibly in the first two and not in the last two. Then he waited until dawn, he prayed two rak'ahs reciting audibly in both. (Darqutni, chapter on Jibril leading prayer, vol. 1, p. 268, no. 1011) This hadith shows that audible recitation is done in both rak'ahs of Fajr, in the first two of Maghrib and Isha, and silent in the third of Maghrib and last two of Isha. (2) Hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet went out... and was praying Fajr with his companions, and when they heard the Quran they listened to it. (Bukhari, chapter on audible recitation in Fajr prayer, p. 125, no. 773; Muslim, chapter on audible recitation in Fajr and recitation to jinn, p. 189, no. 1006/449) In this chapter, several hadiths about audible recitation in Fajr in front of the jinn are mentioned, showing that Fajr prayer has audible recitation if one is the imam. (3) The evidence for audible recitation in Maghrib is: Jubayr ibn Mut'im from his father: I heard the Messenger of Allah recite Surah al-Tur in Maghrib. (Bukhari, chapter on audible in Maghrib, p. 105, no. 765) The word 'sam'tu' indicates that the Prophet recited audibly so the narrator heard it. (4) The evidence for audible recitation in Isha is: I heard al-Bara' that the Prophet during a journey recited in Isha in one of the two rak'ahs 'Wa al-Tini wa al-Zaytun' (Bukhari, chapter on audible in Isha, p. 124, no. 767; Muslim, chapter on recitation in Isha, p. 193, no. 1037/464) Again the word 'sam'tu' indicates audible recitation. (5) For Jumu'ah and the two Eids, the hadith: Al-Nu'man ibn Bashir said: The Messenger of Allah used to recite in the two Eids and Jumu'ah 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiya' (Muslim, chapter on what is recited in Jumu'ah, p. 1351, no. 2028/878; Abu Dawud, chapter on what is recited in Jumu'ah, p. 169, no. 1122) This hadith shows that the Prophet recited these surahs, indicating audible recitation because the companions heard his recitation. (6) I asked 'Ata': In which prayers is the recitation audible from the night and day obligatory prayers? He said: Fajr, the first two of Isha, the first two of Maghrib, and Jumu'ah when in congregation; if one is alone, then no. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on what is audible in prayer, vol. 2, p. 65, no. 2657) This athar indicates that audible recitation is done in Jumu'ah, and by analogy [qiyas] the two Eids are the same. (7) For Tarawih and Witr in Ramadan, the athar: From 'A'isha, wife of the Prophet, that the Prophet prayed in the mosque and people prayed with him, then he prayed the next night and more people came, then they gathered on the third night but [he did not come out?].
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents the second wajib of the chapter: the imam's audible recitation in seven specific prayers. The author enumerates them: Fajr (both rak'ahs), first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, Jumu'ah, both Eids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. If the imam mistakenly recites audibly where silent is required or vice versa, sujūd sahw becomes wajib. Then seven proofs are given: first, the hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer, which establishes the pattern of jahr in certain prayers; second, the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about Fajr; third, the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im for Maghrib; fourth, the hadith of al-Bara' for Isha; fifth, the hadith of al-Nu'man ibn Bashir for Jumu'ah and Eid; sixth, the athar of 'Ata' which also adds Jumu'ah and analogically extends to Eid; seventh, the athar of 'A'isha about Tarawih (though the text cuts off). The Hanafi position is clear: jahr in these prayers is wajib, and the proofs are from authentic hadith and athar.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer where the imam raises his voice so the congregation can hear.
سجده سهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or mistake in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following prayers is NOT included in the seven where audible recitation is wajib according to this passage?
A) Fajr
B) Maghrib (first two rak'ahs)
C) Dhuhr
D) Tarawih

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, jahr in the seven specified prayers is wajib; unintentionally omitting or adding requires sajdah sahw.

Proofs for Audible Recitation (Jahr) in Specific Prayers
Collects eight hadiths and athar proving jahr in specific prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight hadith and athar proofs for audible recitation (jahr) in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr and explain how each proof supports the Hanafi position that jahr is wajib.

Core Idea
Audible recitation is wajib in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr — proven by the Prophet's practice.

This lesson collects eight key proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions, establishing that audible recitation (jahr) is wajib in specific prayers. Each hadith directly demonstrates the Prophet (peace be upon him) reciting aloud, forming the basis of the Hanafi ruling. Understanding these proofs solidifies the distinction between jahri and sirri prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight prayers covered
From the passage, list the prayers that require jahr: Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr. Note that Maghrib and Isha only require jahr in the first two rak'ahs.
Fajr is fully jahri; Maghrib and Isha are partially jahri.
2
Match each proof to its prayer
For each of the eight proofs, determine which prayer it addresses. For example, proof (1) from the hadith of Jibril shows jahr in Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha. Proofs (2)-(4) specifically address Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha. Proof (5) covers Jumu'ah and Eid, proof (6) is an athar summarizing the rule, proof (7) for Tarawih, and proof (8) for Witr.
3
Extract the key phrase indicating jahr
In each proof, look for words like 'سمعت' (I heard) or explicit statements about reciting aloud. For instance, in proof (3) 'سمعت رسول الله يقرأ في المغرب بالطور' directly implies audible recitation.
The word 'سمعت' is a strong indicator of jahr.
4
Connect the proof to the Hanafi ruling
Explain how each proof obligates jahr. The consistent practice of the Prophet in congregation makes jahr a wajib act for the imam. The athar of 'Ata' explicitly states the rule, and the analogy (qiyas) extends it to Eid and Tarawih.
Hanafis consider this practice as wajib due to its continuity and emphasis.
5
Synthesize the overall evidence
Combine all proofs to conclude that jahr is wajib in these prayers. Note that this is a mukhtalaf fih issue; other schools may consider it sunnah. The Hanafi position is based on strong textual evidence.

Commentary
This passage is a collection of proofs (dalil) for the ruling that certain prayers require audible recitation (jahr). The author lists eight evidences: (1) The hadith of Jibril leading the Prophet in prayer, showing jahr in Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and sirr in the remaining. (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas about the prayer of Fajr with jahr. (3) Jubayr ibn Mut'im heard the Prophet recite Surah al-Tur in Maghrib. (4) Al-Bara' heard Surah al-Tin in Isha. (5) Al-Nu'man ibn Bashir reports the Prophet recited in Jumu'ah and Eid. (6) The athar of 'Ata' summarizing the rule. (7) Hadith of Aisha about Tarawih prayer in congregation. (8) The practice of 'Ali for Witr. These establish that jahr is the established practice in these prayers.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Audible recitation, loud enough for others to hear.
الإسرار (al-israr): Silent recitation, audible only to oneself.
الصلاة الجهرية (al-salat al-jahriyyah): Prayers in which audible recitation is prescribed: Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid, Tarawih, Witr.

Ruling on Silent Recitation in Zuhr, Asr, and Remaining Rak'ahs
States the rule for silent recitation with three proofs from hadith and athar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five places where silent recitation (sirr) is wajib and explain the evidence from the three proofs.

Core Idea
Silent recitation (sirr) is wajib in five prayer segments; the Prophet's practice and Jibril's guidance prove it.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding silent recitation in prayer. The text specifies five contexts where the recitation must be silent (sirr) and not audible. The author then provides three proofs from the Sunnah and the saying of a tabi'i to establish that this is a wajib obligation, not merely a sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify what act is being discussed and what legal ruling (hukm) it carries. The act is silent recitation (al-israr) in prayer. The hukm is wajib (obligatory).
In Hanafi fiqh, wajib means an obligation whose omission is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.
2
List the five places
Enumerate the five locations where silent recitation is required: all rak'ahs of Zuhr, all rak'ahs of Asr, the third rak'ah of Maghrib, the third and fourth rak'ahs of Isha, and all day nafl prayers.
The first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha are recited aloud (jahr).
3
Analyze the first proof
The hadith of Abu Qatada states that the Prophet recited the Fatiha and a sura in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, and would sometimes make them hear an ayah. The occasional audible ayah indicates that the baseline recitation was silent.
This proof is implicit; the occasional loud recitation shows that normally it was silent.
4
Analyze the second proof
The hadith of Anas reports that Jibril led the Prophet in Zuhr and Asr with four rak'ahs each, and he did not recite aloud (la yajharu fiha bi-qira'ah). This is a direct and explicit proof of silent recitation in these prayers.
This hadith is the strongest proof for the Hanafi position.
5
Analyze the third proof
The saying of Hasan al-Basri: 'Day prayers are silent, night prayers are audible.' This is a statement from a prominent tabi'i and serves as supporting evidence.
While not a prophetic statement, it reflects the practice of the early generations.

Source Text

Translation: (404) Silent recitation in all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, and in the remaining rak'ahs after the first two of Maghrib and Isha, and in day nafl prayers. Explanation: Silent recitation is wajib in these five places: all rak'ahs of Zuhr, all rak'ahs of Asr, third rak'ah of Maghrib, third and fourth of Isha, and day nafl. Proofs: (1) Abu Qatada: The Prophet used to recite Fatiha and a sura in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, and would sometimes make us hear an ayah. (2) Anas: Jibril led the Prophet in Zuhr and Asr with silent recitation. (3) Hasan al-Basri: Day prayers are silent, night prayers are audible.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) with its proofs. The author states that silent recitation is wajib in five places: all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, the third of Maghrib, the third and fourth of Isha, and all day nafl prayers. Then three proofs are given: (1) Hadith of Abu Qatada indicating the Prophet recited silently in the first two rak'ahs, with occasional audible verse showing it was not fully jahr. (2) The hadith of Jibril leading prayer shows silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr. (3) The saying of Hasan al-Basri that 'day prayers are silent, night prayers are audible' is used as supportive evidence. Thus, these prayers require sirr.

Key Terms
الإسرار (al-israr): Silent recitation where only the reciter hears himself.
الظهر (al-zuhr): The midday prayer, consisting of four rak'ahs.
العصر (al-asr): The afternoon prayer, consisting of four rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Silent recitation is wajib in Zuhr, Asr, third of Maghrib, third/fourth of Isha, and day nafl, proven by the Prophet's practice and Jibril's guidance.

The Munfarid's Choice in Audible Prayers
Ruling on the munfarid's recitation in audible prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a munfarid in jahr prayers and explain the underlying reason.

Core Idea
The munfarid may choose between jahr and sirr in audible prayers.

This lesson addresses a specific but common scenario: praying alone in a prayer that is normally recited aloud in congregation (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha). Many students assume that if the prayer is jahr, one must recite aloud even when alone. However, the Hanafi school grants full choice. Let's examine the text and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Focus on the phrase 'والمنفرد مخير' – the munfarid has a choice. Determine what exactly he has a choice over.
The choice is in recitation volume during prayers that are normally jahr for an imam.
2
Distinguish the munfarid from the imam
Recall that in congregation, the imam recites aloud in jahr prayers. The munfarid is not bound by this rule.
The text says: 'because there is no congregation to disturb.'
3
Understand the scope of the choice
The choice is between jahr (audible) and sirr (silent). Both are equally valid. The munfarid may even choose mixed recitation.
The text adds an analogy with night nafl prayer, which also permits choice.
4
Apply the ruling to concrete prayers
Identify which prayers are jahr: Fajr, Maghrib, Isha. For these, the munfarid may choose. For silent prayers (Zuhr, Asr), he recites silently by default.
The choice only applies to prayers that are jahr for imam.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools require the munfarid to recite aloud in jahr prayers. The Hanafi position is based on the absence of disturbance.
This ikhtilaf affects practice: a Hanafi praying alone in Fajr can recite silently, which would be invalid in some other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۰۵) اور تنہا نماز پڑھنے والے کو جہری نماز میں اختیار ہے، جیسے کہ رات میں نفل پڑھنے والے کو اختیار ہے۔ تشریح : جو آدمی تنہا نماز پڑھ رہا ہو تو جہری نماز میں اس کو اختیار ہے کہ زور سے قرآت کرے اور اپنے آپ کو سنائے ، اور یہ بھی اختیار ہے کہ آہستہ پڑھے، کیونکہ جماعت نہیں ہے اس لئے کسی کو ستانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (405) And the one praying alone has a choice in audible prayers, just as the one praying night nafl has a choice. Explanation: A person praying alone in a jahr prayer may choose to recite aloud, making himself hear, or to recite silently, because there is no congregation to disturb.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: the munfarid (individual praying alone) has the choice (mukhayyar) in prayers that are normally jahr for the imam. He may recite aloud or silently. The reason given is that there is no congregation to disturb. The analogy with night nafl prayer supports this: in night nafl, one may also recite aloud or silently according to need. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
مخير (mukhayyar): Having a choice between two options, both equally valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No, unless he recites aloud
D) Yes, but only if he intended to pray qada

Key Takeaway
The munfarid in a jahr prayer may freely choose between audible and silent recitation; both are equally valid in the Hanafi school.
