Silent Recitation in Zuhr, Asr, and Other Prayers
Lists five places where silent recitation is wajib with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five places where silent recitation (israr) is wajib according to the Hanafi school and identify the proof for each.

Core Idea
Silent recitation is wajib in five specific prayers: Zuhr, Asr, the last rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and daytime nafl.

This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling on silent recitation (israr) in prayer. The text specifies five categories of prayer where the recitation must be silent, with proofs from the Sunnah. Understanding this distinction is crucial because it determines the validity and obligation of your prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories
List the five places where silent recitation is wajib: all rak'ahs of Zuhr, all rak'ahs of Asr, the third rak'ah of Maghrib, the third and fourth rak'ahs of Isha, and all daytime nafl prayers.
The first two rak'ahs of Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and night nafl require loud recitation.
2
Understand the ruling level
Silent recitation is wajib, not fard. In Hanafi usul, wajib is proven by zanni dalil (ahad hadith), while fard requires qati' dalil (Quran or mutawatir).
This distinction affects the consequence of omission: omitting a wajib requires sajdah al-sahw; omitting a fard invalidates the prayer.
3
Examine the proofs
Three proofs are cited: (1) Hadith of Abu Qatada: the Prophet sometimes made them hear a verse during Zuhr/Asr, indicating normal recitation was silent. (2) Hadith of Anas: Jibril led the Prophet in silent prayers for Zuhr and Asr. (3) Athar of al-Hasan: daytime prayer is silent.
These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut), hence the ruling is wajib.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider silent recitation sunnah in these prayers, not wajib. The Hanafi school insists on wajib due to the strength of the evidence.
The practical difference: in Hanafi, omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw); in Shafi'i, it is merely leaving a sunnah (no compensation).
5
Apply the ruling
Given a specific prayer, determine whether recitation must be silent or loud. For example, in the third rak'ah of Isha, recitation must be silent; in the first rak'ah of Fajr, loud.
Daytime nafl includes prayers like Duha, but not night nafl (like Tahajjud) which require loud recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في واجبات الصلوة (۴۰۴) والاسرار فى الظهر والعصر وفيما بعد اوليى العشاء ونفل النهار وجه : (۱) عن ابي قتادة عن ابيه قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه يقرأ في الركعتين من الظهر والعصر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة سورية ويسمعنا الآية احيانا (٢) عن انس أن جبرئيل اتى النبي عليه بمكة حين زالت الشمس و أمره أن يوذن للناس بالصلوة حين فرضت عليهم ، فقام جبرئيل امام النبي عليه و قاموا الناس خلف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : فصلى أربع ركعات لا يجهر فيها بقرأة.... ثم امهل حتى اذا دخل وقت العصر ، صلى بهم أربع ركعات لا يجهر فيها بالقرأة (٣) عن الحسن قال : صلوة النهار عجماء وصلاة الليل تسمع اذنيك
Chapter on obligatory acts of prayer. (404) And silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr, and after the first two of Isha, and in daytime supererogatory prayers. Proof: (1) From Abu Qatada from his father: The Prophet used to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr Fatiha and a surah and sometimes made us hear a verse. (2) From Anas: Jibril came to the Prophet at Mecca at noon and commanded him to call the people to prayer... He led four rak'ahs without loud recitation... then waited until the time of Asr and led them four rak'ahs without loud recitation. (3) From al-Hasan: The daytime prayer is silent, and the night prayer you make your ears hear.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: silent recitation (sirr) is wajib in five places: all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, the third rak'ah of Maghrib, the third and fourth of Isha, and all daytime nafl prayers. The proofs are ahadith: (1) Abu Qatada reports that the Prophet sometimes made them hear a verse in Zuhr/Asr, showing he was reciting silently. (2) The hadith of Jibril teaching the Prophet the prayers shows he did not recite loudly in Zuhr and Asr. (3) The saying of al-Hasan al-Basri that daytime prayer is 'dumb' (silent) and night prayer is audible. These establish the Hanafi position that sirr is wajib in these prayers.

Key Terms
الاسرار (al-israr): Silent recitation in prayer where only the reciter can hear himself.
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation that is audible to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Zuhr and Asr, plus the last two of Isha and third of Maghrib, and daytime nafl
C) All prayers except Fajr
D) Only in Isha and Maghrib

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, silent recitation (israr) is an wajib act in Zuhr, Asr, the last rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and all daytime nafl prayers, based on ahadith.

The Munfarid's Choice: Volume of Recitation
States that the munfarid can choose to recite loudly or silently in loud prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation volume for the munfarid and identify the proofs that establish choice.

Core Idea
The munfarid may choose: jahr is not wajib when alone.

You may have assumed that a person praying alone must recite loudly in Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, just as the imam does. But the Hanafi school gives the individual a choice. This lesson examines the proofs that support this flexibility, including statements from Companions and the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? It is the recitation volume of a person praying alone (munfarid) in a prayer where the imam normally recites aloud (jahr). The ruling: he has a choice (mukhayyar) between jahr and sirr.
This also applies to the one praying night nafl (mutanaffil bi al-layl).
2
Locate the proofs (adilla)
Four proofs are cited: (1) The statement of the Tabi'i 'Ata that when alone, the prayer is like Zuhr (silent). (2) The practice of Ibn 'Umar reciting loudly when making up missed portions alone. (3) The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas describing the Prophet's recitation as moderate, audible to those nearby. (4) The hadith of 'Aisha that the Prophet sometimes recited loudly and sometimes silently at night.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
These proofs collectively indicate that the Prophet did not always recite loudly when alone – his volume varied. 'Ata's athar directly says the munfarid should not raise his voice; it is like Zuhr. Ibn 'Umar's practice shows he chose jahr when alone, confirming choice. Therefore, the ruling is permissibility of both.
The Hanafi position relies on these evidences being zanni in both transmission and meaning, so they establish a non-binding option.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
The Shafi'i school holds that jahr is wajib on the munfarid in Fajr and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha. Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf is reported to favor jahr, while Imam Muhammad gives full choice. The text supports the latter.
The practical difference: a Hanafi may recite silently without sin; a Shafi'i must recite aloud.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the munfarid may choose, as the proofs for choice are stronger and the requirement of jahr is not established by definitive evidence. Later Hanafi texts often recommend jahr if it aids concentration, but it remains optional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۰۵) والمنفرد مخيَّر و كذلك المتنفل بالليل (۴۰۲) ولو ترك السورة في اوليى العشاء قرأها في الأخريين مع الفاتحة وجه (۱) قلت لعطاء : ما يجهر به الصوت من القرأة من صلاة الليل و النهار من المكتوبة ؟ قال : الصبح والاوليين العشاء ، و الاوليين المغرب ، و الجمعة اذا كانت في جماعة ، فاما اذا كان المرأ وحده فلا ، هي الظهر حينئذ - (مصنف عبدالرزاق) (۲) اس کی دلیل یہ اثر بھی ہے عن نافع ان عبد الله بن عمر كان اذا فاته شيء من الصلوة مع الامام فيما جهر فيه الامام بالقراءة انه اذا سلم الامام قام عبد الله فقرء لنفسه فيما يقضى و جهر (موطا امام مالك) (۳) رات میں نفل پڑھنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ زور سے قرآت پڑھے اور اس کا بھی اختیار ہے کہ آہستہ قرآت پڑھے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔عن ابن عباس قال : كانت قراءة النبي له على قدر ما يسمعه من في الحجرة وهو في البيت . (ابوداود شريف) (۴) اور اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پڑھنے والے کو اختیار ہے۔ قال : سألت عائشة كيف كانت قرأة النبي له بالليل ؟ [أ كان يسر بالقرأة أم يجهر ؟ ] فقالت : كل ذالك قد كان يفعل، ربما اسر بالقرأة و ربما جهر
(405) The one who prays alone has a choice. Likewise the one who prays supererogatory prayers at night (402). And if he leaves the surah in the first two of Isha, he recites it in the later two with the Fatiha. Proof: (1) I asked 'Ata: What recitation is raised loudly in obligatory prayers of night and day? He said: Fajr, the first two of Isha, the first two of Maghrib, and Jumu'ah if in congregation. As for a person alone, no, it is like Zuhr then. (2) Another proof: From Nafi' that Ibn 'Umar, when he missed something of the prayer with the imam in a prayer where the imam recited loudly, when the imam concluded, he stood and recited loudly for himself. (3) The one who prays night nafl has the option to recite loudly or silently. Proof from Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet's recitation was such that one in the room could hear him while he was in the house. (4) And in this hadith: I asked 'Aisha how was the Prophet's night recitation; she said he did both, sometimes silently and sometimes loudly.

Commentary
This passage deals with a ruling: the munfarid (person praying alone) has the option to recite loudly or silently in prayers that normally require jahr in congregation. This also applies to the one praying night nafl (salat al-layl). The proofs include: (1) The statement of 'Ata that when alone, the prayer is like Zuhr (silent). (2) The practice of Ibn 'Umar reciting loudly when making up a missed portion alone. (3-4) The hadith that the Prophet sometimes recited loudly and sometimes silently at night, showing choice. The Hanafi position is that jahr is not required for the munfarid; he may choose based on what helps his concentration.

Key Terms
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying individually, not in congregation.
المتنفل بالليل (al-mutanaffil bi al-layl): One who prays supererogatory prayers at night (like tahajjud).

Key Takeaway
The munfarid is free to choose between loud and silent recitation in prayers that are normally loud in congregation, a uniquely Hanafi flexibility based on multiple proofs.

Making Up Missed Surah in Isha Prayer
Ruling on making up a missed surah in Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for making up a missed surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha and apply it to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
A missed surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha must be made up in the last two rak'ahs with loud recitation.

In the Hanafi school, reciting an additional surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha is wajib. If one forgets to do so in Isha, the prayer is not invalidated, but the omission must be remedied. This lesson explains how to compensate and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the missed wajib
Determine which element was omitted: the additional surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha. This is a wajib, not a rukn.
Missing Fatiha is a rukn and has a different ruling.
2
Apply the compensation rule
The compensation is to recite the missed surah in the last two rak'ahs, along with al-Fatiha, and both must be recited loudly (jahr).
Loud recitation is used because Isha is a jahr prayer; the surah in the first two rak'ahs would have been loud, so the compensation preserves jahr.
3
Consider the dalil
The ruling is based on the statement of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (a companion), which is a valid source in Hanafi fiqh. It commands reciting in the last two rak'ahs when one forgets in the first two.
The athar is narrated in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Distinguish from missing Fatiha
If al-Fatiha itself is missed in the first two rak'ahs, it is not made up in later rak'ahs because it is a rukn that cannot be relocated; the prayer would need to be repeated if intentional.
The text explicitly states 'he should not repeat it in the last ones'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۰۶) اور عشا کی پہلی دورکعت میں سورت چھوڑ دے تو اس کو اخیر میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ جہر سے پڑھے۔اور سورۂ فاتحہ چھوڑ دے تو اخیر میں اس کو مکرر نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : عشاء کی پہلی دو رکعت میں سورت ملانا چھوڑ دیا تو اس کو دوسری دورکعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ پڑھے اور دونوں میں جہری قرآت پڑھے، کیونکہ سورت میں سری کریں تو جہری چھوٹ گئی اس لئے جہری پڑھے، اور سورت فاتحہ کو سری پڑھے تو ایک ہی رکعت میں جہری اور سری جمع کرنا لازم آئے گا اس لئے دونوں ہی کو جہری پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) عـن عـلـى قال اذا نسى الرجل ان يقرأ فى الركعتين الأولين من الظهر و العصر و العشاء فليقرأ في الركعتين الاخريين و قد أجزاعنه - (مصنف عبدالرزاق) (۲) اور جہری قرآت کرنے کا استدلال اس حدیث کے اشارة النص سے کیا۔ عن ابی قتادہ قال : خطبنا رسول الله الله .... فصلی رسول الله ركعتين
Translation: (406) And if he leaves the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, he recites it in the last ones with Fatiha and with loud recitation. And if he leaves Surah al-Fatiha, he should not repeat it in the last ones. Explanation: If one omits adding a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, he should recite it in the later two rak'ahs along with Fatiha and recite both loudly. Because if he recited the surah silently, the loud recitation would be lost, so he recites loudly. And if he recites Fatiha silently, it would necessitate combining loud and silent in one rak'ah, so he recites both loudly. Proof: (1) From 'Ali: When a man forgets to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr, Asr, and Isha, he should recite in the last two rak'ahs and it suffices him. (2) And the deduction for loud recitation is from the textual indication of this hadith: from Abu Qatada: The Messenger of Allah delivered a sermon... then he prayed two rak'ahs...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling for a specific scenario: if a person forgets to recite an additional surah after Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha (which is wajib to do so), he must make it up in the last two rak'ahs by reciting both Fatiha and the surah, and he must recite loudly. The basis is the athar of 'Ali. The reasoning: since the first two rak'ahs are meant for loud recitation (jahr), if he recites the surah silently in the later rak'ahs, the jahr of the surah would be lost; so he recites both Fatiha and surah loudly. If he had missed Fatiha entirely, he does not make it up because the missed Fatiha would have been wajib, but its place is in the first two rak'ahs. The text also mentions that if he misses Fatiha alone, he does not repeat it; this is because Fatiha is a pillar (rukn) that cannot be relocated. The proof from 'Ali's statement is a qawl sahabi, which is a valid source in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
السورة (al-surah): An additional chapter after al-Fatiha in prayer.
فاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, obligatory in every rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He should recite the surah in the last two rak'ahs along with al-Fatiha and recite loudly
D) He should ignore it as it is not required

Key Takeaway
A missed surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha must be made up in the last two rak'ahs with loud recitation of both al-Fatiha and the surah.

Making Up a Missed Surah in the Last Rak'ahs of Isha
Ruling on making up a surah omitted in first two rak'ahs of Isha with jahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on making up a missed surah in the Isha prayer and apply the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
If a surah is omitted in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, it must be recited audibly in the last two rak'ahs.

In the Hanafi school, reciting a surah after Surah Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha is a wajib act. If it is omitted, the prayer does not become invalid, but the surah must be made up in the last two rak'ahs with audible recitation. This lesson explains the ruling and its proof from the practice of the Prophet and the companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns the omission of a surah after Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha. The compensation is to recite that surah in the last two rak'ahs along with Fatiha.
The surah must be recited audibly because the first two rak'ahs are supposed to be audible.
2
Examine the proof from practice
Look at the hadith of Abu Qatada where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs audibly after sunrise, indicating that the requirement of jahr remains even when making up.
The phrase 'as he used to do every day' shows constancy in jahr for Fajr.
3
Distinguish from omission of Fatiha
If Fatiha itself is omitted, it is not repeated in the last two rak'ahs because Fatiha is a rukn that must be performed in the original place; the prayer would be invalid if omitted intentionally.
The surah is wajib, Fatiha is rukn.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not require any surah after Fatiha, so no compensation is needed. This difference affects whether the prayer is considered complete without the surah.
In Hanafi, omission of surah triggers wajib compensation; in Shafi'i, no issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في واجبات الصلوة
فيم يجهر كمتنفل بالليل (۴۰۲) ولو ترك السورة في اوليى العشاء قرأها في الأخريين مع الفاتحة وجه
(۱) قلت لعطاء : ما يجهر به الصوت من القرأة من صلاة الليل و النهار من المكتوبة ؟ قال : الصبح والاوليين العشاء ، و الاوليين المغرب ، و الجمعة اذا كانت في جماعة ، فاما اذا كان المرأ وحده فلا ، هي الظهر حينئذ - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ما تجمهر من القرأة فيه من الصلوة ، ج ثانى ص ۶۵ نمبر ۷ ۲۶۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ آدمی جماعت کے ساتھ ہو تو جہر کرے اور تنہا ہو تو ضروری نہیں ہے
(۲) اس کی دلیل یہ اثر بھی ہے عن نافع ان عبد الله بن عمر كان اذا فاته شيء من الصلوة مع الامام فيما جهر فيه الامام بالقراءة انه اذا سلم الامام قام عبد الله فقرء لنفسه فيما يقضى و جهر (موطا امام مالک، باب العمل فى القراءة ص ۶۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہری نماز کیلئے پڑھتا ہو تو زور سے قرآت پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عبداللہ بن عمر زور سے پڑھتے تھے۔
(۳) رات میں نفل پڑھنے والے کو اختیار ہے کہ زور سے قرآت پڑھے اور اس کا بھی اختیار ہے کہ آہستہ قرآت پڑھے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔عن ابن عباس قال : كانت قراءة النبي له على قدر ما يسمعه من في الحجرة وهو في البيت . (ابوداود شریف ، باب رفع الصوت بالقرأة في صلوۃ اللیل ،ص ۱۹۸، نمبر ۱۳۲۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رات کی نفل میں قرآت زور سے بھی پڑھی جاسکتی ہے۔
(۴) اور اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پڑھنے والے کو اختیار ہے۔ قال : سألت عائشة كيف كانت قرأة النبي له بالليل ؟ [أ كان يسر بالقرأة أم يجهر ؟ ] فقالت : كل ذالك قد كان يفعل ، ربما اسر بالقرأة و ربما جهر فقلت : الحمد لله الذي جعل فی الامر سعة . ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی القرآة بالمیل ص ۱۱۹ نمبر ۴۴۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سری اور جہری دونوں قرآت کرسکتا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۴۰۶) اور عشا کی پہلی دورکعت میں سورت چھوڑ دے تو اس کو اخیر میں فاتحہ کے ساتھ جہر سے پڑھے۔اور سورۂ فاتحہ چھوڑ دے تو اخیر میں اس کو مکر ر نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : عشاء کی پہلی دو رکعت میں سورت ملانا چھوڑ دیا تو اس کو دوسری دور کعتوں میں سورہ فاتحہ کے ساتھ پڑھے اور دونوں میں جہری قرآت پڑھے، کیونکہ سورت میں سری کریں تو جہری چھوٹ گئی اس لئے جہری پڑھے، اور سورت فاتحہ کو سری پڑھے تو ایک ہی رکعت میں جہری اور سری جمع کرنا لازم آئے گا اس لئے دونوں ہی کو جہری پڑھے۔
وجه : (۱) عـن عـلـى قال اذا نسى الرجل ان يقرأفى الركعتين الأولين من الظهر و العصر و العشاء فليقرأ في الركعتين الاخريين و قد أجزاعنه - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من نسى القرآة ، ج ثانی، جس ۸۱ نمبر ۲۷۵۹) اس قول صحابی میں ہے کہ پہلی رکعت میں قرآت بھول گیا تو دوسری رکعت میں قرآت کرے۔
(۲) اور جہری قرآت کرنے کا استدلال اس حدیث کے اشارة النص سے کیا۔ عن ابی قتادہ قال : خطبنا رسول الله الله .... فصلی رسول الله ركعتين صلى الله 
جهرا (۴۰) ولو ترك الفاتحة لا يكررها في الأخريين
، ثم صلى الغداة فصنع كما كان يصنع كل يوم - (مسلم شریف، باب قضاء الصلوة الفائمة واستحباب تعجیل قضائها،ص ۲۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۶۲/۶۸) اس حدیث میں, كما كان يصنع كل يوم ، کے اشارة النص سے استدلال فرمایا ہے کہ ہر دن فجر میں جہری قرآت کرتے تھے تو اس دن بھی سورج طلوع ہونے کے بعد بھی جہری قرآت ہی کی ہے، جس سے ثابت ہوا کہ جہری کو بعد میں ادا کرنا ہو تو جہری ہی ادا کرے۔
Section on obligatory acts of prayer. Regarding what is recited audibly: like one praying nafl at night (402). And if one leaves the surah (after Fatiha) in the first two of Isha, he recites it in the last two with Fatiha. Proof: (1) I asked Ata: 'What is recited audibly from the recitation of the night and day obligatory prayers?' He said: 'Fajr, the first two of Isha, the first two of Maghrib, and Jumu'ah if in congregation. As for a man alone, no; it is like Zuhr then.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). This athar indicates that one recites audibly with the congregation, but not if alone. (2) Another proof: from Nafi that Ibn Umar, when he missed a part of prayer with an imam who recited audibly, would stand after the imam's salam and recite for himself audibly in what he made up. (Muwatta Imam Malik). This shows that for audible prayers one can recite audibly. (3) One praying nafl at night has the choice to recite audibly or softly. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The recitation of the Prophet was such that those in the room could hear it while he was in the house.' (Abu Dawud). (4) And in another hadith: I asked Aisha how the Prophet recited at night, softly or audibly? She said: 'He did both; sometimes softly, sometimes audibly.' I said: 'Praise be to Allah who made the matter flexible.' (Tirmidhi). Translation (406): And if one leaves the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, he recites it in the last two with Fatiha audibly. And if he leaves Surah Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last two. Commentary: If one omits adding a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, he recites it in the last two rak'ahs with Surah Fatiha, and recites both with audible recitation because if he recites the surah softly, he would miss the audible jahr, so he recites audibly. And if he recites Fatiha softly, he would combine jahr and sirr in one rak'ah, so he recites both audibly. Proof (1): Ali said: 'If a man forgets to recite in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr, Asr, and Isha, let him recite in the last two, and that suffices him.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). This companion's statement shows that if recitation is forgotten in the first rak'ah, he recites in the second rak'ah. (2) And the deduction for audible recitation is from the indication of the text of this hadith: Abu Qatada said: 'The Messenger of Allah gave us a sermon... and he prayed two rak'ahs audibly, then he prayed Fajr and did as he used to do every day.' (Muslim). In this hadith, from the indication of the text of 'as he used to do every day', it is deduced that he used to recite audibly in Fajr every day, and even after sunrise he recited audibly, proving that if one has to make up an audible prayer, he recites audibly.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof dealing with the situation when a person omits reciting a surah (after Surah Fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs of the Isha prayer. The author first states the ruling: if one leaves the surah in the first two rak'ahs, he should recite it in the last two rak'ahs along with Surah Fatiha, and he should recite audibly (jahr). The commentary explains that this is because the first two rak'ahs of Isha are supposed to be recited audibly; reciting the surah softly would miss the required jahr. Therefore, both the surah and Fatiha are recited audibly in the last two rak'ahs. The author then provides proofs: (1) from Ata that audible recitation is required in Fajr, the first two of Maghrib and Isha, and Jumu'ah when in congregation (this indicates the general rule of jahr in those prayers). (2) From Ibn Umar that he would recite audibly when making up a missed part of an audible prayer. (3) The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows that the Prophet would recite audibly at night in nafl, which is the basis for choice in nafl. (4) The hadith of Aisha confirms that both options are permissible. For the specific ruling, the author cites a hadith from Abu Qatada where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs audibly after sunrise, implying that the obligation of jahr remains even when making up. The overall ruling is that the missed surah must be made up audibly in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer, where the reciter's voice is loud enough for others nearby to hear.
اخريين (ākhirayn): The last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) or the last rak'ah of Maghrib (the third).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person forgets to recite a surah after Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha, what must he do?
A) He does nothing; the prayer is valid without compensation.
B) He recites the surah in the last two rak'ahs with Fatiha, audibly.
C) He performs sajdah al-sahw only.
D) He repeats the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
An omitted surah after Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha must be made up audibly in the last two rak'ahs, as it is a wajib act that requires compensation.

Omitting Surah Fatiha: No Repetition in Last Rak'ahs
Ruling with proof based on reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when Surah Fatiha is omitted in the first two rak'ahs and explain the reasoning based on the distinction between wajib and rukn.

Core Idea
Surah Fatiha omitted in first two rak'ahs? Do not repeat it; sajdah al-sahw suffices because repetition brings no benefit.

In the previous lesson, we learned that omitting a surah after Fatiha requires making it up in the last two rak'ahs. Now we encounter a different case: what if Surah Fatiha itself is omitted? The Hanafi school rules that it is not repeated, but rather compensated by sajdah al-sahw. This distinction hinges on the nature of Fatiha as a wajib, not a rukn, and on the principle of avoiding useless repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is omitting Surah Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs. The ruling: do not repeat it in the last two rak'ahs; instead, perform sajdah al-sahw after the prayer.
2
Understand the reasoning (proof)
The reasoning is that reciting Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs would serve as the prescribed recitation for those rak'ahs. Repeating it for the first two would be useless duplication because the missed Fatiha would not benefit from being recited in a different rak'ah.
This reasoning is based on the principle of avoiding 'la fa'ida' (no benefit).
3
Note the legal category of Fatiha
In the Hanafi school, reciting Surah Fatiha is a wajib, not a rukn. Omission of a wajib requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw), not full repetition of the act.
This contrasts with omission of a rukn, which invalidates the prayer.
4
Contrast with omission of a surah
Previously, we learned that omitting a surah after Fatiha (which is sunnah) requires making it up in the last two rak'ahs. Why the difference? Because a surah is sunnah and its repetition brings added benefit, whereas Fatiha is wajib and its repetition would be redundant.
The distinction lies in the legal weight of the omitted element.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers Fatiha a rukn (pillar). If omitted, they require repeating the entire rak'ah. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: Hanafis perform sajdah al-sahw; Shafi'is repeat the rak'ah.
This lesson only covers the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك الفاتحة لا يكررها في الأخريين
ترجمه : (۴۰۷) اور اگر پہلی رکعت میں سورت فاتحہ چھوڑ دیا تو دوسری دو رکعت میں مکرر نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : پہلی دورکعتوں میں سورت ملائی لیکن فاتحہ چھوڑ دیا تو دوسری دو رکعتوں میں اس کا اپنا فاتحہ پڑھے گا، اب پہلی دو رکعتوں کا بھی فاتحہ پڑھے گا تو سورہ فاتحہ دو دومرتبہ ہو جائے گا، اس لئے دومرتبہ نہ کرے اس لئے کہ اس سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے، البتہ فاتحہ واجب ہے اس لئے اس کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو کر لے نماز ہو جائے گی۔
And if one leaves the Fatiha, he does not repeat it in the last two. Translation (407): And if one leaves Surah Fatiha in the first rak'ah, he does not repeat it in the last two. Commentary: He recited a surah but left Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, so in the last two rak'ahs he will recite his own Fatiha; now he would have recited Fatiha twice, so he should not repeat it because there is no benefit. However, Fatiha is wajib, so for its omission he performs sajdah al-sahw, and the prayer becomes valid.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for when Surah Fatiha is omitted in the first two rak'ahs. According to the Hanafi school, if a person mistakenly omits Surah Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs (but recited a surah after it), he should not repeat Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. The reasoning is that doing so would result in reciting Fatiha twice (once in the last two rak'ahs for those rak'ahs themselves, and then again to make up for the first two), which is pointless. Instead, since reciting Fatiha is wajib, its omission requires sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness), and the prayer is valid thereafter. This is in contrast to the omission of a surah (after Fatiha), which must be made up in the last two rak'ahs as explained in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
سجده سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, such as omitting a wajib element.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person omits Surah Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of the Isha prayer, what is the proper course of action?
A) Repeat the entire prayer.
B) Recite Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs and also perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) Do not recite Fatiha again in the last two rak'ahs, but perform sajdah al-sahw.
D) Recite Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs and no sajdah al-sahw is needed.

Key Takeaway
Omitting Surah Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs does not require repetition; sajdah al-sahw is sufficient because Fatiha is a wajib and repetition brings no benefit.

Ruling on Not Repeating Fatiha in Last Rak'ahs
Ruling on omitting Fatiha in first two rak'ahs and not repeating it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs and explain the legal consequence (sajdah sahw) and the proof (ishara al-nass from hadith).

Core Idea
Omitting Fatiha requires sajdah sahw, not repetition, and does not invalidate the rak'ah.

In this passage, the author addresses a specific scenario: a worshipper recites a surah but omits Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer. The Hanafi ruling is clear—do not repeat Fatiha in the last two; instead, perform sajdah sahw. This ruling is supported by a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and illustrates the school's distinction between fard and wajib.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
What is the ruling when Fatiha is omitted in the first two rak'ahs? Do not repeat it in the last two; perform sajdah sahw.
2
Identify the proof
The text cites a hadith about the Prophet praying Fajr aloud after sunrise.
Sahih Muslim, Bab Qada' al-Salat
3
Analyze the istidlal
How does the hadith prove the ruling? Via ishara al-nass: the Prophet did what he used to do, indicating that a missed prayer retains its original jahri/sirri quality.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers Fatiha fard; omission invalidates the rak'ah. The Hanafi response: it is wajib only, compensated by sajdah sahw.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the worshipper completes the prayer with sajdah sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في واجبات الصلوة جهرا (۴۰) ولو ترك الفاتحة لا يكررها في الأخريين، ثم صلى الغداة فصنع كما كان يصنع كل يوم - (مسلم شریف، باب قضاء الصلوة الفائمة واستحباب تعجیل قضائها،ص ۲۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۶۲/۶۸) اس حدیث میں, كما كان يصنع كل يوم ، کے اشارة النص سے استدلال فرمایا ہے کہ ہر دن فجر میں جہری قرآت کرتے تھے تو اس دن بھی سورج طلوع ہونے کے بعد بھی جہری قرآت ہی کی ہے، جس سے ثابت ہوا کہ جہری کو بعد میں ادا کرنا ہو تو جہری ہی ادا کرے۔ ترجمه : (۴۰۷) اور اگر پہلی رکعت میں سورت فاتحہ چھوڑ دیا تو دوسری دو رکعت میں مکرر نہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : پہلی دورکعتوں میں سورت ملائی لیکن فاتحہ چھوڑ دیا تو دوسری دو رکعتوں میں اس کا اپنا فاتحہ پڑھے گا، اب پہلی دو رکعتوں کا بھی فاتحہ پڑھے گا تو سورہ فاتحہ دو دومرتبہ ہو جائے گا، اس لئے دومرتبہ نہ کرے اس لئے کہ اس سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے، البتہ فاتحہ واجب ہے اس لئے اس کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو کر لے نماز ہو جائے گی۔
Section on the obligatory acts of prayer: Jahri recitation. (40) And if one leaves the Fatiha (in the first two rak'ahs), he does not repeat it in the last two. Then he prayed Fajr as he used to do every day (Sahih Muslim, chapter on making up missed prayers and desirability of hastening, p. 238, no. 1562/68). From this hadith, the indication of the text (ishara al-nass) is used to deduce that he used to recite aloud every day in Fajr, so on that day after sunrise he also recited aloud, which proves that if one has to perform (a missed prayer) later, he should recite aloud. Translation: (407) And if in the first rak'ah he omitted Surah Fatiha, he should not repeat it in the next two rak'ahs. Explanation: In the first two rak'ahs he recited a surah but omitted Fatiha; then in the last two rak'ahs he will recite his own Fatiha. Now if he also recites Fatiha for the first two rak'ahs, the Fatiha would occur twice, therefore do not repeat it because there is no benefit in that. However, Fatiha is wajib, so for omitting it he should perform sajdah sahw and the prayer will be valid.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the section on the obligatory acts (wajibat) of prayer. It addresses the case where a person omits reciting Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer but recites another surah. According to the Hanafi madhhab, Fatiha is wajib in every rak'ah for the imam and the single worshipper, but not for the follower. If it is omitted in the first two rak'ahs, one should not repeat it in the last two rak'ahs, because that would cause an unnecessary repetition. Instead, the prayer is valid but deficient, and the deficiency is compensated by performing sajdah sahw. The author supports this with a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) after missing Fajr prayed it aloud after sunrise, deducing that the loud recitation of a jahri prayer is not waived when made up. The core ruling is clear: omission of a wajib element like Fatiha does not invalidate the prayer; it only requires sajdah sahw. This is a key distinction between fard and wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayers where the imam recites audibly (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah).
الفاتحة (al-fatiha): Surah al-Fatiha, the first chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person omits Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr prayer, what should he do?
A) Repeat the prayer.
B) Recite Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs as compensation.
C) Perform sajdah sahw and do not repeat Fatiha.
D) Recite Fatiha twice in the last two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Omitting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs does not require repetition; instead, sajdah sahw compensates, and the prayer remains valid.

The Fifty-One Sunnas of Prayer: An Overview
Enumeration of sunnah acts in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state at least ten of the fifty-one sunnas of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on omitting a sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
There are fifty-one sunnas in prayer; omitting them is makruh tanzihi but does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage from a Hanafi primer enumerates the sunnah acts (sunan) of prayer, emphasizing that they are fifty-one in total. Understanding these sunnas is essential for performing prayer with ideal perfection. While omitting a sunnah does not break the prayer, it reduces its reward and is considered makruh tanzihi (disliked). The list includes acts from the opening takbir to the recitation, and memorizing them helps a Muslim refine their prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Category
Recognize that the passage lists sunnah acts (mustahabb/mandub) of prayer, not fard or wajib. These are recommended but not obligatory.
Sunnah muakkadah is emphasized; omitting it is makruh tanzihi.
2
Note the Total Number
The text explicitly states 'وهي احدى و خمسون' (they are fifty-one). Keep this number in mind as a memorization anchor.
The number 51 is a key fact for this lesson.
3
Memorize Key Sunnas
From the partial list, focus on the most prominent sunnas: raising hands for takbir, hand placement (men below navel, women on chest), reciting Thana, Ta'awwudh, Basmalah, Amin, Tahmid, quiet recitation, standing straight, imam's takbir, saying Sami' Allahu liman hamidah, foot spacing, recitation lengths, lengthening first rak'ah in Fajr, takbir for ruku', tasbih thrice, and grasping knees.
The list is not exhaustive; other sunnas exist (e.g., qunut, tashahhud positions).
4
Understand the Ruling
These acts are sunnah muakkadah. Omitting any of them without a valid reason is makruh tanzihi, but the prayer remains valid. No sajdah sahw is required for omission.
This distinguishes sunnah from wajib, where omission requires compensation.

Section: On its sunnas. They are fifty-one. There are fifty-one (51) sunnas in prayer. Section: On explaining the sunnas of prayer. For men and slave women: raising both hands to the level of the ears at the takbir tahrimah. ... Keeping fingers spread. ... The follower's takbir tahrimah should be connected to the imam's. Men place the right hand over the left below the navel. Women place both hands on the chest without forming a circle. ... Reciting Subhanaka Allahumma (etc.). Reciting A'udhu billah for recitation. ... Reciting Bismillah at the beginning of each rak'ah. Saying Amin. ... Saying Rabbana lakal hamd. ... Saying all these quietly. 12. Standing straight without bowing the head at the time of takbir tahrimah. ... The imam's takbir. 16: ... And saying Sami' Allahu liman hamidah loudly. In standing: keeping the feet about four fingers apart. Section on the sunnas of prayer. Reciting from the long surahs of Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, from the medium surahs in Asr and Isha, and from the short surahs in Maghrib. And in Fajr prayer only, lengthen the first rak'ah. ... Takbir for bowing. ... Reciting tasbih three times in it. ... Grasping both knees with both hands.

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the sunnah acts (sunan) of prayer in the Hanafi madhhab. The author states that there are fifty-one sunnas in total, though the list here is partial and includes key sunnas such as raising the hands for takbir, placement of hands, recitations (Thana, Ta'awwudh, Basmalah, Amin, Tahmid), quiet recitation, standing straight, the imam's takbir, saying Sami' Allahu liman hamidah aloud, foot spacing, recitation lengths (Tiw al-Mufassal, Awsat, Qisar), lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr, takbir for ruku', tasbih thrice, and grasping the knees. These sunnas are recommended; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but reduces its perfection. The list is important for students to memorize as it encapsulates the ideal form of prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act in prayer; omission is not sinful but goes against the ideal practice.
مفصل (mufassal): The surahs from Qaf (chapter 50) to the end of the Quran, divided into long (tiwal), medium (awsat), and short (qisar).

Salah — Prayer

The Fifty-One Sunnahs of Prayer
Enumeration of the 51 Sunnah acts of Salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major categories of sunnah acts in Salah and identify the Hanafi position on each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's 51 sunnah acts perfect the prayer; omitting them reduces reward but does not invalidate.

This passage from a Hanafi matn lists the fifty-one sunnah acts (sunan) of Salah. These are recommended practices that the Prophet consistently performed. While not obligatory, they complete the prayer and bring it closer to the prophetic model. The list covers actions from the opening takbir to the final supplication, including recitations, postures, and etiquette. Understanding these sunnan helps a Muslim pray with excellence.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the sunnan by prayer element
Group the listed sunnahs into opening, standing/recitation, bowing, prostrating, sitting, and closing. This helps in systematic memorization and application.
The original list is sequential; categorizing aids retention.
2
Identify gender differences
Note where the text specifies different rulings for men and women, e.g., hand placement, sitting posture, finger positions in sujud.
These differences are based on the prophetic practice for each gender.
3
Distinguish between sunnah mu'akkadah and ghayr mu'akkadah
Although the list does not differentiate, later Hanafi works classify some as emphasized (mu'akkadah) and others as non-emphasized. For example, raising hands in takbir is mu'akkadah; spreading fingers in ruku' is ghayr mu'akkadah.
Omitting a mu'akkadah sunnah is more blameworthy but still not sinful.
4
Connect each sunnah to its evidence
Trace each sunnah to a hadith or practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The Hanafi school relies on authentic reports for these acts.
This deepens understanding and strengthens conviction in following the sunnah.
5
Apply the list to a complete prayer
Mentally rehearse a prayer from takbir to salam, checking off each sunnah as you go. This practical application embeds the knowledge.
Use the list as a checklist during actual prayer to gradually perfect it.

Chapter: (On its Sunnahs) and they are fifty-one. There are fifty-one Sunnahs in prayer. Chapter: On the explanation of the Sunnahs of prayer. For a man and a slave woman: raising both hands up to the ears at the time of the takbir tahrimah. Keeping fingers spread. ... The follower's tahrimah should be connected to the imam's tahrimah. A man places his right hand over his left below the navel. A woman places both hands on her chest without making a circle. ... Reciting Subhanakallahumma (etc.). Reciting A'udhu billah for recitation. ... Reciting Bismillah at the beginning of every rak'ah. Saying Amin. ... Saying Rabbana lakal hamd. ... Saying all these quietly. 12 Standing straight without tilting the head at the time of tahrimah. ... The imam's takbir. 16: ... And saying Sami' Allahu loudly. Keeping the feet four fingers apart while standing. Chapter on the Sunnahs of prayer. Reciting the long chapters of Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, the medium ones in 'Asr and 'Isha', and the short ones in Maghrib. And lengthening the first rak'ah only in Fajr prayer. ... Takbir for ruku'. ... Saying tasbih three times in it. ... Grasping both knees with both hands. ... :M ... Keeping fingers spread, but a woman does not keep them spread. Keeping both shins upright. 23 Keeping the back extended. 24 Keeping the head level with the buttocks. 25 ... Rising from ruku'. ... Then standing calmly after it. 277 27 In sujud, first placing both knees, then both hands, then the face. When rising, doing the reverse. 29 Takbir for sujud. 30 Takbir for rising from sujud. Making sujud between both palms. 32 ... Saying tasbih three times in sujud. 35 ... A man keeps his belly away from his thighs, his elbows away from his sides, and his hands away from the ground. ... A woman bends down and brings her belly to her thighs. ..:MA Performing qawma (standing after ruku'). Performing jalsah (sitting between the two prostrations). In jalsah, placing both hands on the thighs as in qa'dah. Spreading the left foot and standing the right foot upright. 9 A woman sits on her buttocks. 42 At the time of 'la ilaha' in al-Tahiyyat, he raises his finger and at 'illa Allah' he lowers it. ... Reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs. In the final qa'dah, reciting salawat upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Supplicating with words resembling the Qur'an and hadith, not resembling the speech of people. Chapter on the Sunnahs of prayer.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a clear enumeration of the Sunnah acts (sunan) of prayer (Salah) according to the Hanafi school. The author states that there are fifty-one Sunnahs in total, and then lists them in a sequential order corresponding to the actions of the prayer from beginning to end. The list covers the recommended practices for both men and women, noting differences where applicable (e.g., hand placement, sitting posture). The Sunnahs include the raising of hands, recitations, postures, and etiquette. The passage serves as a memorization anchor for students to learn the Sunnah acts that complete the prayer. It is important to note that these are not obligatory; omitting a Sunnah does not invalidate the prayer but is considered less perfect. The Hanafi position on each act is given without proof, as this is a matn text meant for memorization.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed, whose omission is not sinful but is blameworthy.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer and makes prohibited what was permissible.
مفصل (mufassal): The last seventh of the Qur'an, from Surah Qaf or al-Hujurat to the end.
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer.
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing posture in prayer.
سجود (sujud): Prostration posture in prayer.
قعدہ (qa'dah): Sitting posture in prayer.

The Sunnah of Raising Hands for Takbir Tahrimah
Ruling with proof on hand-raising sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands for takbir tahrimah and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Raising hands for takbir tahrimah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, with different heights for men and free women.

This passage from the chapter on the sunan of prayer gives the Hanafi position on how and when to raise the hands at the start of prayer. It covers three key rulings: the timing of the hand raise, the height for men, and the distinct height for free women. The author provides hadith evidence to support the simultaneous raising of hands with the takbir, a sunnah that is emphasized but not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising the hands at the beginning of prayer (takbir tahrimah). The passage lists it under 'sunan al-salah', indicating it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not a wajib or fard.
Omission does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Separate the three rulings
The passage gives three distinct rulings: (1) timing – hands must rise simultaneously with the takbir, (2) height for men and slave women – to the ears, (3) height for free women – to the shoulders.
The author notes that no explicit text is found for slave women; it is analogized from free women.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: the practice of Ibn Umar (ascribed to the Prophet) in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud, and a direct narration in Abu Dawud showing the Prophet raised hands with the takbir. The key legal point is the simultaneity.
The hadith are ahad (zanni in transmission), but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school also considers raising hands sunnah but at additional points (e.g., before and after ruku). The Hanafi distinction of free women raising to shoulders is unique.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

فصل في سنن الصلوة
(۴۰۸) رفع اليدين للتحريمة حذاء الاذنين للرجل والامة وحذاء المنكبين للحرة
ترجمه : (۴۰۸) [۱] مرد اور لونڈی کے لئے تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت کانوں کے برابر دونوں ہاتھ اٹھانا۔ اور آزاد عورت شانوں تک اٹھائے۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت ہاتھ تکبیر سے پہلے نہ اٹھائے ، اور نہ بہت بعد میں اٹھائے ، بلکہ تکبیر کے ساتھ ہی ہاتھ بھی اٹھائے ۔ [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھائے ، یعنی کان کے اوپر حصے تک انگلی ہو اور کان کے نیچے حصے کے مقابل انگوٹھا ہو ۔ اور باندی بھی یہی کرے لیکن باندی کے لئے کوئی حدیث یا قول صحابی نہیں ملا ، البتہ چونکہ وہ عورت ہے اس لئے اس کا تحریمہ آزاد عورت کی طرح ہونا چاہئے، واللہ اعلم ۔ (۳) تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آزاد عورت مونڈھے تک اپنا ہاتھ اٹھائے۔ وجه : (۱) تکبیر کے ساتھ ہاتھ اٹھائے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان ابن عمر كان اذا دخل في الصلوة كبر و رفع يديه .... و رفع ذالك ابن عمر الى النبي الا الله - ( بخاری شریف، باب رفع الیدین اذا قام من الرکعتین ، ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۷۳۹ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب رفع اليدين حذ والمنكبين مع تكبيرة الاحرام ، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۸۶۵/۳۹/ابو داؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین ، ص ۱۱۱ نمبر ۷۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور متکبیر کے ساتھ ہی ہاتھ اٹھاتے تھے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں اسکی صراحت ہے۔ حدثني أهل بيتى عن أبى أنه حدثهم أنه رأى رسول الله الله يرفع يديه مع التكبير (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین ، ص ۱۱، نمبر ۷۲۵ ) اس حدیث میں صراحت ہے کہ ہاتھ اٹھانے کے ساتھ تکبیر کہتے تھے ۔ (۳) مردکان
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Prayer. (408) Raising the hands for takbir tahrimah: level with the ears for a man and a slave woman, and level with the shoulders for a free woman. Translation: (408) [1] For a man and a slave woman, raising both hands level with the ears at the time of takbir tahrimah. And a free woman raises to the shoulders. Explanation: There are three issues here: [1] One is that at the time of takbir tahrimah, one should not raise the hands before the takbir, nor too long after, but raise the hands simultaneously with the takbir. [2] The second issue is that a man should raise his hands to the ears, meaning the fingers are at the upper part of the ear and the thumb is opposite the lower part of the ear. A slave woman does the same, but no hadith or saying of a companion is found for her; however, since she is a woman, her takbir should be like a free woman's, and Allah knows best. (3) The third issue is that a free woman raises her hands to the shoulders. Evidence: (1) For raising hands with the takbir, the proof is this hadith: 'Ibn Umar used to, when entering prayer, say takbir and raise his hands... and he attributed that to the Prophet, peace be upon him.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that the Prophet used to raise his hands with the takbir. (2) Another hadith explicitly states: 'My family narrated to me from my father that he narrated that he saw the Messenger of Allah raising his hands with the takbir.' (Abu Dawud). This hadith explicitly states that he said takbir with raising the hands. (3) A man...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the sunnah of raising the hands at the beginning of prayer (takbir tahrimah). The author lists three key rulings: first, hands must be raised simultaneously with the takbir, not before or after. Second, a man raises his hands to the level of his ears, with fingertips at the upper part and thumb opposite the lower part. A slave woman follows the same ruling, though no direct evidence is cited; the author reasons that since she is a woman, she should emulate a free woman. Third, a free woman raises her hands only to the shoulders. The author then provides hadith evidence: the famous narration of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands with the takbir, recorded in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. Another narration from Abu Dawud explicitly states the simultaneity. This passage clarifies that the sunnah is not just the height but also the timing. The Hanafi school follows this as a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not a wajib, so omitting it does not require sujud al-sahw. The difference between a free woman and a slave woman in hand height is a specifically Hanafi ruling; other schools often treat women the same as men in this aspect.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir tahrimah): The opening takbir of the prayer which makes what was permissible (like speech) prohibited (haram) during salah.
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising both hands during the prayer at specific points, here at the takbir tahrimah.
سنن الصلوة (sunan al-salah): Recommended but non-obligatory acts in prayer; omitting them does not invalidate prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To the ears, like a man.
B) To the shoulders.
C) To the chest.
D) She does not raise her hands at all.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands for takbir tahrimah is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, with men raising to ears and free women to shoulders, based on authentic hadith.

Sunan of the Salām in Prayer
Lists recommended practices for the salām

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan (recommended acts) of the closing salām and identify the correct intentions and timing for the imam, follower, one praying alone, and the latecomer.

Core Idea
The salām's sunan are recommended enhancements; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage enumerates the sunan (recommended practices) of the closing salām in prayer. These sunan are derived from the Prophet's ﷺ practice and elevate the quality of the prayer, but they are not obligatory. Understanding these sunan helps the believer perfect their prayer while knowing that missing them does not require any compensation or repetition. The list covers face turning, intention, volume, synchronisation with the imam, and considerations for different roles.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the status of the salām
First, understand that the salām itself is a wajib act in the Hanafi school. The actions listed in this passage are sunan (mustahabb) that enhance the salām. Omitting them does not require sajdah sahw or invalidate the prayer.
This is crucial to avoid conflating sunan with obligations.
2
Memorize the face-turning sequence
Note that the salām is given twice: first to the right, then to the left. The face should be turned enough that the cheek is visible from behind.
3
Learn the intentions for the imam, follower, and lone worshipper
The imam intends both the praying followers and the guardian angels. The follower intends himself, the guardian angels, and the righteous people on that side. The one praying alone intends only the guardian angels.
These intentions are sunan, not obligations.
4
Observe the volume distinction
The second salām should be said more softly than the first. For the follower, the salām should coincide with the imam's salām.
5
Apply the rules for the latecomer
A masbūq (latecomer) should wait for the imam to complete his own salām before giving his own salām. This is because he needs to complete his missed rak'ahs after the imam's salām.

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sunan (recommended practices) of the salam in prayer. It begins with turning the face to the right and then left. For the imam, he should intend both the human worshippers and the guardian angels when giving salam. The follower intends himself, the angels, and the righteous people on that side. The one praying alone intends only the angels. The second salam is said more softly than the first. The follower should give salam at the same time as the imam, and start from the right side. A latecomer (masbuq) should wait for the imam to finish before giving his own salam. These are all sunnah; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer or require sajdah sahw. The Hanafi school considers these as mustahabb (recommended) practices derived from the Prophet's ﷺ practice.

مقتدی (muqtadī): The follower who prays behind an imam.
مسبوق (masbūq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has begun.

Raising Hands for the Opening Takbir: Rulings and Proofs
Ruling with proof: three sub-rulings and their dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on raising hands for the opening takbir for men, free women, and slave women, and identify the key hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Raising hands for the opening takbir is sunnah, not wajib; the height differs by gender and status.

The opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) is a pillar of the prayer, but the act of raising the hands simultaneously is a confirmed sunnah. The Hanafi school has detailed the method: men and slave women raise their hands to the ears, while free women raise them only to the shoulders. This lesson unpacks the three rulings and the authentic hadith evidence that supports them, clarifying common misconceptions about obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the Arabic text and translation. Note the three distinct rulings: timing (simultaneous with takbir), hand position for men/slave women (to ears), and hand position for free women (to shoulders).
The slave woman's ruling is deduced by analogy; no direct hadith is mentioned.
2
Understand the legal category
The text explicitly says it is sunnah, not wajib or fard. Memorize the consequence: if omitted, the prayer is valid and no sajdah sahw is required.
Knowing the difference between sunnah and wajib is critical in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the proofs for timing
Examine the hadith of Ibn Umar and the narration from Wa'il ibn Hujr. They show that the Prophet ﷺ raised his hands with the takbir, not before or after.
This refutes practices of raising hands before or after the takbir.
4
Analyze the proofs for hand height (men)
Combine the hadith of 'Abd al-Jabbar (palms at shoulders, thumbs at ears) and Malik ibn al-Huwayrith (hands level with ears). The Hanafis reconcile them: palms opposite shoulders, thumbs near ears.
This explains why men raise to ears but not full stretch.
5
Examine the proof for women
The athar from al-Zuhri and Hammad indicate women raise to shoulders or chest. The author chooses shoulders, based on the stronger narration.
This differs from the Shafi'i position, which raises to shoulders for both genders.

ضروری نوٹ : سنت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کرنا بہتر ہے، ثواب ملے گا، اور نہ کرے تو سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا، نماز ہو جائے گی
ترجمه : (۴۰۸) [۱] مرد اور لونڈی کے لئے تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت کانوں کے برابر دونوں ہاتھ اٹھانا۔ اور آزاد عورت شانوں تک اٹھائے۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت ہاتھ تکبیر سے پہلے نہ اٹھائے ، اور نہ بہت بعد میں اٹھائے ، بلکہ تکبیر کے ساتھ ہی ہاتھ بھی اٹھائے ۔ [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھائے ، یعنی کان کے اوپر حصے تک انگلی ہو اور کان کے نیچے حصے کے مقابل انگوٹھا ہو ۔ اور باندی بھی یہی کرے لیکن باندی کے لئے کوئی حدیث یا قول صحابی نہیں ملا ، البتہ چونکہ وہ عورت ہے اس لئے اس کا تحریمہ آزاد عورت کی طرح ہونا چاہئے، واللہ اعلم ۔ (۳) تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آزاد عورت مونڈھے تک اپنا ہاتھ اٹھائے۔
وجه : (۱) تکبیر کے ساتھ ہاتھ اٹھائے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ ان ابن عمر كان اذا دخل في الصلوة كبر و رفع يديه .... و رفع ذالك ابن عمر الى النبي الا الله - ( بخاری شریف، باب رفع الیدین اذا قام من الرکعتین ، ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۷۳۹ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب رفع اليدين حذ والمنكبين مع تكبيرة الاحرام ، ص ۱۶۶، نمبر ۸۶۵/۳۹/ابو داؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین ، ص ۱۱۱ نمبر ۷۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور متکبیر کے ساتھ ہی ہاتھ اٹھاتے تھے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں اسکی صراحت ہے۔ حدثني أهل بيتى عن أبى أنه حدثهم أنه رأى رسول الله الله يرفع يديه مع التكبير (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب رفع الیدین ، ص ۱۱، نمبر ۷۲۵ ) اس حدیث میں صراحت ہے کہ ہاتھ اٹھانے کے ساتھ تکبیر کہتے تھے ۔ (۳) مردکان تک ہاتھ اٹھائے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الجبار بن وائل عن ابيه : أنه أبصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حين قام الى الصلاة رفع يديه حتى كانتا بحيال منكبيه و حاذى بابهاميه أذنيه ثم كبر . (ابوداود شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۱۳، نمبر ۷۳۴ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہتھیلی مونڈھے کے پاس ہو اور انگوٹھے کان کے پاس ہو اس طرح ہاتھ اٹھائے ، اسی پر حنفیہ عمل کرتے ہیں تا کہ تمام احادیث پر عمل ہو جائے۔ (۴) کان کی لو تک انگلیاں رکھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔عـــــــن مالک بن الحوريث ان رسول الله له الا الله كان اذا كبر رفع يديه حتى يحاذى بهما اذنيه - (مسلم شریف ، باب استخباب رفع الیدین حد والمنکین، ص ۱۶۸ نمبر ۸۶۵/۳۹۱)(۵) عورت اپنے ہاتھ کو مونڈھے تک اٹھائے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن الزهري قال ترفع يديها حذو منكبيها - دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن حماد انه كان يقول في المرأة اذا استفتحت الصلاة ترفع يديها الى ثدييها - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في المرأة اذا افتخحت الصلاة الى اين ترفع یدیھا ، ج اول، ص ۱۲۱۶، نمبر ۲۴۷۳/۲۴۷۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ مونڈھے اور پستان تک اٹھائے۔
(408) Raising the hands for the opening takbir: to the level of the ears for the man and the slave woman, and to the level of the shoulders for the free woman.
Necessary note: The meaning of sunnah is that doing it is better, reward will be received, and if one does not do it, sajdah sahw is not necessary, and the prayer will still be valid.
Translation: (408) [1] For the man and the slave woman, raising both hands to the level of the ears at the time of the opening takbir. And the free woman raises them to the shoulders.
Explanation: Here there are three issues. [1] One is that at the time of the opening takbir, do not raise the hands before the takbir nor much after, but raise the hands simultaneously with the takbir. [2] The second issue is that the man raises his hands to the ears, meaning the fingers are at the upper part of the ear and the thumb is opposite the lower part of the ear. And the slave woman does the same, but no hadith or saying of a Companion was found for the slave woman; however, since she is a woman, her opening takbir should be like that of a free woman, and Allah knows best. (3) The third issue is that the free woman raises her hands to the shoulders.
Proof: (1) For raising hands with the takbir, the proof is this hadith: 'Ibn Umar used to, when entering the prayer, say the takbir and raise his hands...' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that the Prophet ﷺ would raise his hands at the same time as the takbir. (2) The clarity of this is in the hadith: 'My family narrated to me from my father that he saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ raising his hands with the takbir' (Abu Dawud). (3) For the man raising his hands to the ears, the proof is the hadith: 'Abd al-Jabbar ibn Wa'il from his father: that he saw the Prophet ﷺ when he stood for prayer, he raised his hands until they were at the level of his shoulders and his thumbs were at the level of his ears, then he said the takbir.' (Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates placing the palms at the shoulders and thumbs at the ears; the Hanafis act upon this to combine all the ahadith. (4) For placing the fingers at the earlobes, the proof is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'When he made takbir, he raised his hands until they were level with his ears' (Muslim). (5) For the woman raising her hands to the shoulders, the proof is the athar of al-Zuhri: 'She raises her hands to the level of her shoulders.' And in another narration from Hammad: 'When a woman begins the prayer, she raises her hands to her chest.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah).
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah of raising the hands during the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah). The text breaks it down into three rulings: (1) Timing: the hands must be raised simultaneously with the takbir, not before or after. (2) For men (and slave women, by extension), the hands are raised until the fingers reach the tops of the ears and the thumbs are opposite the earlobes, with palms facing forward. (3) For free women, the hands are raised only to the shoulders, as a matter of modesty. The text also provides extensive proofs from authentic hadith and athar, showing that the Hanafis reconcile various narrations by having the palms opposite the shoulders and the thumbs near the ears. The note at the beginning clarifies that these are sunnah, not wajib or fard; leaving them does not invalidate the prayer nor require sajdah sahw.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (taḥrīma): The opening takbir of the prayer, saying 'Allahu Akbar' while raising the hands.
حذاء (ḥidhā'): Meaning 'opposite' or 'level with' – the hands are raised to be opposite the ears (men) or shoulders (women).
منکبین (mankibain): The shoulders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Spreading the Fingers When Raising Hands for Takbir
States the sunnah of spreading fingers during takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on finger position during the opening takbir and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Slightly spreading the fingers when raising the hands for takbir is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ.

This lesson addresses the proper form of the hands during the opening takbir. While the obligation of raising the hands is established, the specific manner of the fingers is a sunnah supported by explicit hadith. We will examine the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon. The act is spreading the fingers (nashr al-aṣābi') while raising the hands for the opening takbir. The ruling is sunnah (recommended).
Sunnah acts are those the Prophet consistently did; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah (ra) recorded by al-Tirmidhi. The Prophet ﷺ would spread his fingers when saying the takbir.
This is a sunnah ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni, but it is accepted for establishing a sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit verb 'spread' (nashara) indicates the action. Since the hadith describes a constant practice, it is taken as a recommended act.
The proof is direct and clear.
4
Note cross-madhhab agreement
The Maliki and Shafi'i schools also consider this sunnah. There is no dispute among the four major schools on this point.
This is a muttafaq alayh issue.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
When raising the hands for takbir, the fingers should be slightly spread, not tightly clenched. This is the operative ruling for practice.
The prayer remains valid even if one forgets to spread the fingers.

This passage covers the sunnah of spreading the fingers (nashr al-asabi') while raising the hands for the opening takbir. The hands should be raised with the fingers naturally apart, not pressed together. The proof is a hadith from Abu Hurairah (ra) reported by Imam al-Tirmidhi, which explicitly states that the Prophet ﷺ would spread his fingers. This is a recommended practice; omitting it does not affect the validity of the prayer.

Key Terms
نشر الاصابع (nashr al-aṣābi'): Spreading the fingers apart, not clenching them together.

Follower's Takbir: Timing and Ruling
Explains sunnah of follower's takbir immediately after imam's.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the follower's takbir timing and apply the condition that it must be immediately after the imam's takbir.

Core Idea
The follower's takbir must be right after the imam's—not before, not too late—this is sunnah.

This passage clarifies the proper timing for a follower (muqtadi) to say his opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) in congregational prayer. The key is muqārana—coinciding the follower's takbir with the imam's. The ruling is sunnah, meaning it is recommended but not obligatory; however, delaying excessively is makruh. Let us walk through the legal details and proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower's opening takbir in congregational prayer. Its ruling is sunnah—not fard or wajib. The passage explicitly states 'this is sunnah'.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, but the text simply says 'sunnah'.
2
Understand the timing condition
The follower's takbir must be immediately after the imam's—not before, not so delayed that the connection (ittisal) is lost. If excessively delayed, the follower may lose the reward but the prayer remains valid.
The condition of 'immediately after' (muqārana) is the core requirement.
3
Examine the first proof (hadith)
The hadith of Anas ibn Malik (Bukhari and Muslim) states: 'When the imam says takbir, say takbir.' This indicates following the imam in the takbir.
The command 'fakabbiru' is in the imperative, but it is understood as sunnah due to other evidence.
4
Examine the second proof (athar)
The athar from 'Ata' (in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) instructs to say takbir with the imam, confirming the immediate timing.
This athar reinforces the same point.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a follower says takbir before the imam, his takbir is not valid as a follower's takbir—he must wait and repeat it after the imam. If he delays too much, his prayer is valid but he has committed makruh tanzihi.
The mufta bihi is the immediate following.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۱۰) ومقارنة احرام المقتدى احرام امامه
ترجمه : (۴۱۰) [۳] مقتدی کا تحریمہ امام کے تحریمہ سے ملا ہوا ہو۔
تشریح : مقتدی کا تحریمہ امام سے پہلے نہ ہو اور نہ بہت بعد میں ہوتا کہ تکبیر افتتاح فوت نہ ہو جائے بلکہ امام کی تکبیر کے فورا بعد میں ہو، اور مقتدی کی نماز امام کے ساتھ جڑی ہوئی ہو یہ سنت ہے۔
وجه : (ا) عن انس بن مالك ...... و قال انما جعل الامام ليؤتم به فاذا كبر فكبروا و اذا ركع فاركعوا و اذا رفع فارفعوا ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب صلاة القاعد، ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۱۱۱۴ر مسلم شریف، باب ائتمام الماً موم بالا مام، ص۱۷۴، نمبر ۴۱۱ ۹۲۱ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب امام تکبیر کہے تو تم تکبیر کہو، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کے ساتھ تکبیر کہے۔ (۲) عن عطاء قال قلت له لو خيل الى ان الامام قد كبر تكبيرة الافتاح فكبرت ثم كبرت بعد ؟ قال تكبر معه_(مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب الرجل یکبر قبل الامام، ج ثانی، ص ۴۷ نمبر ۲۵۵۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ امام کے ساتھ تکبیر تحریمہ کہو۔
(410) And the follower's ihram coinciding with the imam's ihram.
Translation: (410) [3] The follower's opening takbir should be attached to the imam's opening takbir.
Explanation: The follower's opening takbir should not be before the imam's, nor so much after that the opening takbir is lost, but rather immediately after the imam's takbir, and the follower's prayer should be connected with the imam's; this is sunnah.
Proof: (1) From Anas ibn Malik (رضي الله عنه) that he said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so when he says the takbir, say the takbir; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise.' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith indicates that when the imam says takbir, you should say takbir, which shows that one says takbir with the imam. (2) From 'Ata' who said: 'I said to him: If I think that the imam has said the opening takbir, and I say takbir, and then he says takbir later? He said: Say takbir with him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). This athar indicates saying the opening takbir with the imam.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah of the follower (muqtadi) saying his opening takbir immediately after the imam's takbir. It should not be before the imam, nor should it be excessively delayed. The goal is to ensure that the follower's prayer is connected (ittisal) to the imam's. The proofs are from the well-known hadith of Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet ﷺ instructs to say takbir when the imam says takbir, and from the athar of 'Ata' that confirms the timing. This is a sunnah; if the follower delays too much, his takbir may still be valid but he loses the reward of performing it in the ideal manner.

Key Terms
مقارنة (muqārana): Making the follower's takbir coincide with the imam's, i.e., immediately after.
ائتمام (i'timām): The act of following the imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the follower say his opening takbir?
A) Before the imam says takbir
B) Simultaneously with the imam
C) Immediately after the imam's takbir
D) After the imam finishes the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
The follower's opening takbir is sunnah and must be said immediately after the imam's takbir to maintain proper following (i'timam).

Placing the Right Hand on the Left Below the Navel
States the sunnah method for men to place hands below the navel in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of hand placement for men in Hanafi prayer and distinguish it from other schools.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sunnah: men place right hand on left below the navel, forming a ring around the wrist.

In this lesson, we learn the specific method for men to place their hands during the standing portion of prayer. The Hanafi school follows the practice of placing the right hand on the left below the navel, with a ring formed around the wrist using the little finger and thumb. This is considered sunnah, not obligatory, but it is the recommended way to follow the Prophet's practice (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the ruling level
Understand that this act is sunnah (recommended) and not fard or wajib. Omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Identify the placement
The hands are placed below the navel. This is specific to men; women place hands on the chest.
Based on narrations from 'Ali (ra) and others.
3
Note the hand positioning
The right palm is placed on the back of the left hand, with the little finger and thumb forming a ring around the left wrist.
This is the described sunnah method.
4
Contrast with other schools
Shafi'is place hands on the chest, Malikis let them hang freely, Hanbalis also below the navel but with slight differences.
Ikhtilaf is recognized.

Source Text

(۴۱) ووضع الرجل يده صلى الله عليه وسلم
ترجمه : (۴۱) [۴] مرد اپنا دائیں ہاتھ بائیں ہاتھ پر اپنے ناف کے نیچے رکھے۔ اور رکھنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کا باطن حصہ بائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کی پشت پر رکھے چھنگلی اور انگوٹھے سے پہونچے کا حلقہ بنالے۔
(411) And the man places his hand (ﷺ).
Translation: (411) [4] The man places his right hand on his left hand below his navel. And the method is that he places the inner part of the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand's palm, and makes a ring around the wrist with the little finger and thumb.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah of how a man places his hands in the standing posture (qiyam) of prayer. The right hand is placed on the left hand, with the palm of the right on the back of the left, and the little finger and thumb encircling the wrist, and the hands are placed below the navel. This is the Hanafi position. Note that this applies specifically to men; women have a different placement (on the chest). This ruling is a sunnah; it is not obligatory but recommended. The text does not provide proof, but it is based on narrations from 'Ali (ra) and others.

Key Terms
تحت السرة (taḥta al-surra): Below the navel, the recommended placement for a man's hands in prayer.
وضع اليدين (waḍ' al-yadayn): The placement of the hands during qiyam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) On the chest
B) Below the navel
C) Above the navel
D) At the sides

Key Takeaway
For men, the Hanafi sunnah is to place the right hand on the left below the navel, forming a ring around the wrist; this is recommended but not obligatory.

Spreading Fingers During Takbir: A Sunnah Act
Ruling on spreading fingers when raising hands for takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on spreading fingers during takbir and explain the hadith evidence that establishes it as sunna.

Core Idea
Spreading fingers during takbir is sunna, not fard, based on the Prophet's explicit action.

Many worshippers are uncertain whether to keep their fingers tightly closed or slightly apart when raising their hands for takbir. This lesson clarifies that spreading the fingers is a confirmed sunna, drawing directly from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is spreading fingers (nashr al-asabi') when raising hands for takbir in prayer. The author states it is a sunna, meaning recommended but not obligatory.
In Hanafi fiqh, sunna acts are meritorious; omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith from Abu Huraira recorded in Sunan al-Tirmidhi: when the Prophet said takbir, he spread his fingers.
Hadith reference: Tirmidhi, no. 239.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith describes a consistent action of the Prophet. According to Hanafi usul, the Prophet's habitual actions (fi'l) indicate recommendation (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation.
The imperative form is absent; thus the action is at the level of sunna, not wajib.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
While all major schools agree on the sunna nature, some early Hanbali or Shafi'i opinions may treat it as merely permissible (mubah). The Hanafi school explicitly upholds it as sunna.
The practical difference is minimal: the act is highly recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سنن الصلوة (۴۰۹) ونشر الاصابع (۴۱۰) ومقارنة احرام المقتدى الاحرام امامه (41) ووضع الرجل يده اليمنى على اليسرى تحت سرته . وصفة الوضع ان يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلّقا بالخنصر والابهام على الرسغ (۴۱۲) ووضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحلّيق. تشريح : ہاتھ اٹھاتے وقت انگلی ملی ہوئی نہ ہو بلکہ قدرے کشادہ ہو، یہ سنت ہے۔ وجه : عن ابي هريرة قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا كبر للصلاة نشر اصابعه - ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی نشر الاصابع عند التگیر ،ص۶۶، ۲۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہاتھ اٹھاتے وقت انگلیاں کھلی ہو تیں تھیں۔
Chapter on the Sunnas of Prayer. (409) Spreading the fingers. (410) The follower's takbir coinciding with the imam's takbir. (41) The man placing his right hand on his left below his navel. The manner of placement is that he places the inner palm of his right hand on the back of his left hand, forming a ring with his little finger and thumb around the wrist. (412) The woman placing her hands on her chest without forming a ring. Explanation: When raising the hands, the fingers should not be closed but slightly spread; this is sunna. Evidence: From Abu Huraira who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when he said the takbir for prayer, he spread his fingers. (Tirmidhi, chapter on spreading fingers at takbir, p. 66, no. 239) This hadith indicates that when raising the hands, the fingers were open.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage states the ruling (hukm) regarding the position of the fingers during the takbir for prayer. The author explains that it is sunna to have the fingers slightly spread, not closed together. The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira which explicitly states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) spread his fingers when he said the takbir. This is the Hanafi position, and it is considered a recommended act (sunnah), meaning it is praiseworthy to do so, but omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
نشر الاصابع (nashr al-asabi‘): Spreading the fingers apart when raising the hands for takbir in prayer.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act whose omission does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Spreading fingers during the opening takbir is a sunna act; it is recommended but not obligatory, and omitting it does not affect the prayer's validity.
