Hand Placement Below the Navel in Prayer
Ruling on hand placement below navel with three hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi sunna method of hand placement for men in salah, cite the three hadith proofs, and explain why it is sunna (not wajib).

Core Idea
Men place right hand over left below the navel; this is sunna, not wajib, based on clear action and mursal hadith.

This lesson focuses on a specific sunna action in salah: how a man should place his hands after the opening takbir. The Hanafi method is detailed: right palm on back of left hand, with thumb and little finger forming a ring around the wrist, all below the navel. We will examine the three hadith proofs that support this practice and understand why it is considered sunna rather than wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing right hand on left below navel; ruling is sunna (recommended), not wajib. It is not a pillar or condition of prayer.
Sunna means the Prophet often did it; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Examine the three hadith proofs
First hadith from Wa'il ibn Hujr shows the Prophet placed right on left. Second from Qabisah shows the left is grasped with the right. Third from 'Ali specifies below the navel.
The Hanafis act on all three hadiths together.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Hanafis combine these proofs; they consider the mursal hadith of 'Ali as valid evidence for below navel (mursal is accepted in Hanafi usul).
Mursal is a hadith missing a companion link; Hanafis accept it with conditions.
4
Note the flexibility
Imam Tirmidhi noted that both above and below navel are permissible. The Hanafi school adopts below navel as the preferred sunna.
This flexibility shows legitimate ikhtilaf among schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (41) [۴] مرد اپنا دائیں ہاتھ بائیں ہاتھ پر اپنے ناف کے نیچے رکھے۔ اور رکھنے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کا باطن حصہ بائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کی پشت پر رکھے چھنگلی اور انگوٹھے سے پہونچے کا حلقہ بنالے۔ تشریح : مرد کے لئے تحریمہ باندھنے کا سنت طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ ناف کے نیچے باندھے، اور اس کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ کے اندرونی حصے سے بائیں ہاتھ کے گئے کے اوپر حصے کو پکڑے، اور چھنگلی سے اور انگوٹھے سے بائیں ہاتھ کے گئے پر حلقہ بنالے۔ وجه : (۱) دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں پر رکھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن وائل بن حجر انه رأى النبي عل ... ثم وضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى. (مسلم شریف، باب وضع یدہ الیمنی علی الیسری ، ص ۱۷۰ نمبر ۱/۸۹۶/۴۰۱ بوداؤد شریف، باب وضع الیمنی علی الیسری ص ۱۱۷ نمبر ۷۵۵ / بخاری شریف ، باب وضع الیمنی علی الیسری فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۷۴۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھے (۲) قبيضة بـن هـلـب عـن ابيه قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يؤمنا فيأخذ شماله بیمینه - ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء في وضع الیمین علی الشمال في الصلوۃ ص ۷۰، نمبر ۲ ۲۵ رنسائی شریف، باب وضع الیمین على الشمال في الصلوۃ ص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۸۰۹ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دائیں ہاتھ سے بائیں ہاتھ کو پکڑ نا چاہئے ۔ اس لئے حنفیہ نے دونوں حدیثوں پر عمل کیا ۔ (۳) اور ناف کے نیچے ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علي قال ان من السنة في الصلوة وضع الكف على الكف في الصلوة تحت السرة. (ابوداؤد شریف باب وضع الیمنی علی الیسری فی الصلوۃ ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۷۵۶ دار قطنی ، باب فی اخذ الشمال باليمين في الصلوة ، ج اول ص ۲۸۹، نمبر ۱۰۸۹ارسفن للبیھقی ، باب وضع الیدین علی الصدر في الصلوة من السنته ج ثانی ص ۴۸ نمبر (۲۳۴) اس حدیث مرسل سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہاتھ ناف کے نیچے رکھنا چاہئے۔ نوٹ: امام تزندگی نے بہترین فیصلہ فرمایا ہے کہ دونوں کی گنجائش ہے۔ ورأى بعضهم ان يضعها فوق السرة ورأى بعضهم ان يضعها تحت السرة وكل ذلك واسع عندهم . ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء في وضع اليمين على الشمال في الصلوۃ ص ۵۹ نمبر (۲۵۲) لغت : سیری: بائیں ہاتھ ۔ سرۃ : ناف۔ باطن الکف ہتھیلی کے اندر کا حصہ محلقا : حلقہ بنائے ہوئے ۔ الخصر : ہاتھ کی چھوٹی انگلی ، چھنگلی۔ ابہام : انگوٹھا۔الرسغ : پہونچا، گٹا۔
Translation: (41) [4] The man places his right hand on his left hand below his navel. The manner of placement is that he places the inner part of the palm of his right hand on the back of the palm of his left hand, forming a ring with the little finger and thumb around the wrist. Explanation: The sunna way for a man to tie the takbir is to place his hands below the navel, and the manner is that he grips the back of the left hand with the inside of the right hand, and forms a ring around the left wrist with the little finger and thumb. Evidence: (1) Placing the right on the left: the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr that he saw the Prophet place his right hand on his left. (Muslim, chapter on placing right hand on left, p. 170, no. 1/896/401; Abu Dawud, p. 117, no. 755; Bukhari, p. 120, no. 740) This shows the right hand is placed on the left. (2) Hadith of Qabisah ibn Hulb from his father: 'The Messenger of Allah used to lead us in prayer and would take his left with his right.' (Tirmidhi, p. 70, no. 225; Nasa'i, p. 123, no. 809) This shows that the left hand should be grasped with the right. Therefore, the Hanafis act on both hadiths. (3) Below the navel: the hadith of 'Ali: 'It is from the sunna in prayer to place palms on palms below the navel.' (Abu Dawud, p. 118, no. 756; Dar Qutni, vol. 1, p. 289, no. 1089; Bayhaqi, vol. 2, p. 48, no. 234) This mursal hadith indicates that hands should be placed below the navel. Note: Imam Tirmidhi gave an excellent judgment that both are permissible: some scholars hold they should be above the navel, some below, and all are considered flexible. (Tirmidhi, p. 59, no. 252) Vocabulary: shimal: left hand; surra: navel; batin al-kaff: inner palm; muhalliqan: forming a ring; khinsar: little finger; ibham: thumb; rusrigh: wrist.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on the placement of hands for men during prayer. The author first describes the sunna method: the right hand is placed on the left below the navel, with the right palm on the back of the left hand, and the little finger and thumb form a ring around the wrist. Three proofs are given: (1) the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr showing the Prophet placed right on left, (2) the hadith of Qabisah indicating the left is grasped with the right, and (3) the mursal hadith of 'Ali specifying below the navel. The author also notes Imam Tirmidhi's view that both above and below the navel are acceptable, indicating flexibility. The Hanafi school relies on the mursal hadith of 'Ali as evidence for below the navel, which is considered a sunna (recommended) not a wajib. The vocabulary clarifies the terms used in the description.

Key Terms
سرۃ (surrah): Navel; the point below which men place their hands.
محلقا (muhalliqan): Forming a ring (with the thumb and little finger around the opposite wrist).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a man place his hands during prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) On the chest
B) Above the navel
C) Below the navel
D) At the sides

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunna for men is to place the right hand on the left below the navel, forming a ring; missing this does not invalidate the prayer.

Women's Hand Placement in Prayer: On Chest, No Ring
Ruling on hand placement for women: on chest without forming a ring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for women's hand placement in prayer and identify the evidence used.

Core Idea
Women place right palm on left on chest without a ring; it is sunna, not wajib.

In the Hanafi school, women are instructed to place their hands on their chest during prayer without forming a ring between the thumb and little finger. This practice is based on a hadith describing the Prophet's own hand placement. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish the sunna for women from that for men and reinforces the role of modesty in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a woman's hand placement in prayer. The ruling is sunna: it is recommended but not obligatory.
2
Locate the evidence
The evidence is a hadith from Tawus, a tabi'i, who narrated that the Prophet placed his right hand on his left on his chest during prayer.
Hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Understand the application to women
The Hanafi school applies this general practice to women due to the principle of modesty (sitr). Placing hands on the chest is more concealing than below the navel.
4
Note the madhhab distinction
Men place hands below the navel and form a ring; women place on the chest without a ring. This differentiation is unique to the Hanafi school.
Other schools may have both genders place hands on the chest.

ترجمه : (۴۱۲) [۵] عورت اپنے دونوں ہاتھوں کو بغیر حلقہ کئے سینہ پر رکھے۔ تشریح : عورت اپنے دونوں ہاتھوں کو سینہ پر رکھے اور حلقہ بنائے بغیر رکھے بلکہ دائیں ہتھیلی کو بائیں ہتھیلی پر رکھے ۔ وجه : عن طاوس قال كان رسول الله الا الله يضع يده اليمنى على يده اليسرى ثم يشد بينهما على صدره و هو في الصلاة - ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب وضع الیمنی علی الیسری بس ۱۸ نمبر ۷۵۹ سفن البیھقی ، باب وضع اليدين على الصدر في الصلوة )
Translation: (412) [5] The woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring. Explanation: The woman places her hands on her chest without forming a ring; rather, she places the right palm on the left palm. Evidence: From Tawus who said: 'The Messenger of Allah used to place his right hand on his left hand, then clasp them together on his chest while in prayer.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on placing right on left, p. 118, no. 759; Bayhaqi, chapter on placing hands on the chest in prayer)
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling for women's hand placement in prayer. Unlike men who place hands below the navel and form a ring, women place their hands on the chest without forming a ring. The proof is a hadith from Tawus (a tabi‘i) describing the Prophet's own practice of placing his right hand on his left and clasping them on his chest. The Hanafi school applies this to women as it conceals their figure better and is more modest. The ruling is sunna; omission does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms
تحليق (tahliq): Forming a ring with thumb and little finger; women do not do this.

Salah — Prayer

The Sunnah Acts of Thana', Ta'awwudh, and Tasmiyah in Prayer
Three sunan of prayer with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan acts of prayer (thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah) and identify their proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Thana', ta'awwudh, and tasmiyah are sunnah mu'akkadah, proven by ahad hadith and the Quran.

In the opening of prayer, after the takbir tahrimah, the Hanafi school prescribes three specific recitations: thana' (the opening supplication), ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), and tasmiyah (saying bismillah). While these acts are not obligatory, they are highly recommended and based on the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) as recorded in authentic hadith. This lesson will guide you through the evidence and the correct order of these sunan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan acts
Recognize that thana', ta'awwudh, and tasmiyah are independent sunan recited at the start of prayer. Understand their place: thana' after takbir, then ta'awwudh, then tasmiyah before Fatihah.
The thana' text is: 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk'.
2
Locate the proof for each act
For thana' and ta'awwudh, the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). For ta'awwudh additionally, Quran 16:98. For tasmiyah, the hadith from Ibn Abbas (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i).
All proofs are ahad (non-mutawatir), which is why these acts are considered sunnah, not wajib.
3
Analyze the strength of the evidence
Recognize that the hadith are classified as zanni al-thubut (speculative in transmission) and zanni al-dalalah (speculative in meaning). The Hanafi usul principle holds that such evidence yields a ruling of sunnah, not obligation.
Compare with Quranic verse 16:98 which has an imperative form, but it is interpreted as recommended (nadb) due to other evidence.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools, like the Shafi'i, consider tasmiyah as part of Fatihah and recite it aloud. The Hanafi school recites it silently and considers it a separate sunnah before Fatihah.
The ikhtilaf stems from different interpretations of the hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۱۳) [۲] سبحانک اللهم (الخ) پڑھنا۔ [۷] قرآت کے لئے اعوذ باللہ پڑھنا۔ [۸] ہر رکعت کے شروع میں بسم اللہ پڑھنا۔ تشریح : تحریمہ باندھنے کے بعد ثنا، یعنی سبحانک اللهم و بحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالی جدک ولا اله غیرک ۔ پڑھے، اور جنکو قرآت پڑھنی ہے اس کیلئے یہ ہے کہ اعوذ باللہ من الشیطان الرجیم پڑھے، اور اس کے بعد بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ، پڑھے۔ کیونکہ یہ قرآت کے تابع ہیں۔ وجه : (۱) ثنا اور تعوذ کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عـن ابـی سـعـيـد الـخـدرى قال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة بالليل كبر ثم يقول سبحانك اللهم وبحمدک و تبارک اسمک و تعالى جدك ولا اله غیرک. ثم يقول الله اكبر كبيرا ثم يقول اعوذ بالله السميع العليم من الشيطان الرجيم من همزه و نفخه و نفثه ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما یقول عند افتتاح الصلوۃ ،ص ۶۷ نمبر ۲۴۲ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب من رأی الاستفتاح بسبجا نک ،ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۷۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سبحانک اللھم الخ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ (۲) اعوذ باللہ کے لئے یہ آیت بھی ہے۔ فاذا قرأت القرآن فاستعذ بالله من الشيطان الرجيم - ( آیت ۹۸، سورۃ النحل (۱۶) اس آیت میں بھی ہے کہ قرآن پڑھتے وقت اعوذ باللہ، پڑھے ۔ (۳) بسم اللہ پڑھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يفتتح صلواته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم. (ترندی شریف، باب من رأی الجهر بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۲۴۵ رنسائی شریف، باب قرآت ( بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ، ص ۱۲۶ نمبر ۹۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔
Translation: (413) [2] Reciting 'Subhanakallahumma...' etc. [7] Reciting 'A'udhu billah' for the recitation. [8] Reciting 'Bismillah' at the beginning of every rak'ah. Explanation: After the takbir tahrimah, recite the thana', i.e., 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka wa la ilaha ghayruk'. And for whoever is to recite (Quran), he should recite 'A'udhu billahi min ash-shaytan ir-rajim', and after it 'Bismillah ir-rahman ir-rahim', because these are subordinate to the recitation. Proof: (1) For thana' and ta'awwudh, there is this hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) when he stood for prayer at night, he would say the takbir, then say 'Subhanakallahumma...' then say 'Allahu akbar kabira', then say 'A'udhu billah as-sami' al-'alim min ash-shaytan ir-rajim, from his urging, his pride, and his poetry.' [Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud] This hadith shows that one should recite 'Subhanakallahumma...' etc. (2) For a'udhu billah, there is also this verse: 'So when you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from Satan, the cursed one.' (Surah al-Nahl, 98) This verse also says that when reciting the Quran, one should recite a'udhu billah. (3) The proof for reciting bismillah is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas, he said: The Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) used to begin his prayers with 'Bismillah ir-rahman ir-rahim'. [Tirmidhi, Nasa'i] This hadith shows that one should recite bismillah before the recitation.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof passage from the Hanafi fiqh work Thamaratun Najah. It states three sunan acts of prayer: reciting thana' (the opening supplication), ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), and tasmiyah (saying bismillah) at the beginning of each rak'ah. The commentary explains that after the takbir tahrimah, one recites thana', then a'udhu billah, then bismillah. The author provides proof from hadith for each: for thana' and ta'awwudh, a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri; for ta'awwudh additionally the Quranic verse 16:98; for tasmiyah, a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi school considers these as sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib, because the evidence for them is ahad hadith. The order given is standard in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ثناء (thanā'): The opening supplication recited after takbir tahrimah, specifically 'Subhanakallahumma...'
تعوذ (taʿawwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah from Satan before recitation, i.e., 'A'udhu billah...'
تسمية (tasmiyah): Reciting 'Bismillah ir-rahman ir-rahim' before each rak'ah's recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Thana', ta'awwudh, and tasmiyah are sunnah mu'akkadah acts in prayer, proven by ahad hadith and Quranic verse, and their omission does not invalidate the prayer.

The Sunnah of Saying Āmīn and Rabbanā Lak al-Ḥamd
Ruling on two sunan of prayer with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying Āmīn and Rabbanā lak al-ḥamd in prayer and explain the proof from authentic hadith.

Core Idea
Āmīn and Rabbanā lak al-ḥamd are sunnah acts recited quietly; their proof lies in the Prophet's command.

In the prayer, after reciting Sūrat al-Fātiḥah and after rising from rukūʿ, certain phrases are recommended. This lesson examines two such phrases—Āmīn and Rabbanā lak al-ḥamd—and clarifies the rulings for the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone, based on authentic hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Saying Āmīn after Sūrat al-Fātiḥah and saying 'Rabbana lak al-ḥamd' after rising from rukūʿ are both sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the Hanafi school. They are performed quietly.
The passage explicitly states 'quietly' (آہستہ).
2
Locate the dalīl
For Āmīn: Hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'When the imam says Āmīn, then say Āmīn, for whoever's Āmīn coincides with the Āmīn of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' For tahmid: Hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah, then say Allāhumma Rabbanā lak al-ḥamd.' Both are recorded in Bukhari and Muslim/Tirmidhi.
These are ahad (single-narrator) hadith, hence zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The command 'say' (فأمنوا, فقولوا) in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation, because the default command is for obligation only if no counter-indication; here the context of sunnah acts in prayer shows it is recommended.
This is a key Hanafi usul principle applied to the ahad hadith.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
The Shāfiʿī school holds that Āmīn should be said aloud in audible (jahr) prayers, based on other narrations and their usul reading. The Hanafi school sticks to quiet recitation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools rely on authentic hadith.
5
Determine the practical application
The imam says 'Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah' aloud; the follower says 'Rabbana lak al-ḥamd' quietly. One praying alone says both: after rukūʿ, he says 'Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah' and then 'Rabbana lak al-ḥamd'.
The passage explicitly clarifies the split roles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۴۱۴) [۹] آمین کہنا۔ (۱۰) ربنا لک الحمد کہنا۔ تشریح : یہاں دو مسئلے ہیں [1] ایک یہ ہے کہ سورہ فاتحہ ختم ہونے کے بعد آہستہ سے آمین کہے۔ [۲] دوسرا یہ کہ رکوع سے اٹھتے وقت سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ، کے بعد ربنا لک الحمد، آہستہ سے کہے۔ وجه : (۱) آمین کہنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابي هريرة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : اذا امن الامام فأمنوا فانه من وافق تأمينه تأمين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ، وقال ابن شهاب وكان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول آمين ( بخاری شریف، باب جهر الامام بالتأمين ،ص ۱۲۷، نمبر ۷۸۰ مسلم شریف، باب السمیع والتحميد والتأمين ، ص ۱۷۴، نمبر ۹۱۵/۴۱۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا امام اور مقتدی دونوں آمین کہے۔ (۲) اور ربنا لک الحمد، کہنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله الله قال اذا قال الامام سمع الله لمن حمده فقولوا اللهم ربنا لک الحمد (بخاری شریف، باب فضل اللهم ربنا لک الحمد، ص ۱۲۹، نمبر ۷۹۶ رترندی شریف ، باب آخر و باب ما یقول الرجل اذا رفع راسہ، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۲۶۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام سمع الله من حمدہ کہے اور مقتدی ربنا لک الحمد کہے۔ البتہ منفرد ہو تو چونکہ وہ امام اور مقتدی دونوں ہے اس لئے وہ دونوں کہے گا۔
Translation: (414) [9] Saying Amin. (10) Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. Explanation: There are two issues here: [1] One is that after completing Surah al-Fatihah, one should say Amin quietly. [2] The second is that when rising from bowing, after saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', one should say 'Rabbana lakal hamd' quietly. Proof: (1) The proof for saying Amin is this hadith: from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins will be forgiven.' And Ibn Shihab said: The Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) used to say Amin. [Bukhari, Muslim] This hadith shows that both the imam and the follower should say Amin. (2) The proof for saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' is this hadith: from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) said: 'When the imam says "Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah", then say "Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd".' [Bukhari, Tirmidhi] This shows that the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. However, if one is praying alone, since he is both imam and follower, he will say both.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof passage on two sunan of prayer: saying Amin after Fatihah and saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' after rising from ruku. The author explains that both are recited quietly. The proof for Amin is a Sahih hadith where the Prophet instructed to say Amin when the imam does. The proof for tahmid is another hadith specifying that the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd' when the imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. The Hanafi school considers these acts as sunnah, performed quietly. The passage also notes that a person praying alone says both phrases.

Key Terms
آمین (āmīn): A word said after Fatihah, meaning 'O Allah, respond'.
تحمید (taḥmīd): Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' after rising from ruku.
سمع اللہ لمن حمدہ (Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah): Phrase said by the imam when rising from ruku, meaning 'Allah hears the one who praises Him'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Rabbana lakal hamd only

Key Takeaway
Saying Āmīn and Rabbanā lak al-ḥamd quietly is a confirmed sunnah in the Hanafi school, supported by authentic hadith.

Sunnah of Reciting Silently
Rules for reciting certain dhikr silently in prayer with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four dhikr recited silently in Hanafi salah and identify the Hanafi proofs for silent recitation.

Core Idea
Thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and tahmid are sunnah to recite silently; aloud is makruh.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that certain supplications in prayer are to be recited silently. The passage presents clear proofs from the Quran, Hadith, and the practice of the Companions and early scholars. Understanding these proofs strengthens one's appreciation of the Hanafi method of istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four dhikr and their rulings
List the four things: thana' (subhanaka allahumma...), ta'awwudh (a'udhu billah...), tasmiyah (bismillah...), and tahmid (rabbana lakal hamd). The Hanafi ruling is that reciting them silently is sunnah muakkadah; reciting aloud is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the proofs for each ruling
For tasmiyah: hadith from Anas and Abdullah ibn Mughaffal show the Companions did not recite it aloud, leading to the conclusion of silent recitation. For amin: Quran 7:55 and hadith from Alqamah. For all four: athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
The proofs are a mix of athar, hadith, and Quran.
3
Understand how the proofs indicate silent recitation
The Quranic verse commands secret supplication; the hadith show omission of loud recitation; the athar explicitly state the imam should conceal. Combining evidence yields the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi method uses multiple evidences to derive the ruling.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is recite basmalah aloud in jahr prayers and amin aloud. Hanafis differ based on the same or different proofs. This ikhtilaf is legitimate.
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in congregational prayer.

ترجمه : (۴۱۵) [۱۱] ان سکھوں کو آہستہ پڑھے۔ تشریح : [۱] ثناء [۲] اعوذ بالله [۳] بسم الله [۴] ربنا لک الحمد۔ان چاروں کو آہستہ پڑھے۔ وجه : (۱) چاروں کو آہستہ پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال : يخفى الامام: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، والاستعاذة ، و آمين ، و ربنا لک الحمد - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۹۳ من كان لا جهر بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ج اول ،ص۱۳۶۰، نمبر ۴۱۳۶ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ما یخشی الامام، ج ثانی، ص ۵۷ نمبر ۲۵۹۸ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعوذ باللہ اور بسم اللہ، آمین، اور تحمید آہستہ پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ (۲) بسم اللہ آہستہ کہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس بن مالك أنه حدثه قال : صليت خلف النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم و ابي بكر ، وعمر ، وعثمان ، فكانوا يستفتحون بالحمد لله رب العالمين ، لا يذكرون بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، في اول قراءة ، ولا في آخرہ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب حجة من قال لا تجهر بالبسملة ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۹۲۳/۳۹۹ بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التكبیر، ص۱۰۳، نمبر۷۴۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور اور صحابہ بسم اللہ پڑھتے ہی نہیں تھے نہ شروع میں نہ آخر میں۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن مغفل قال سمعنی ابی وانا في الصلوة اقول بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحيم فقال لى اى بنی محدث ایاک و الحدث ... وقال وقد صليت مع النبي الله و مع ابي بكر وعمر ومع عثمان فلم اسمع احدا منهم يقولها فلا تقلها ،اذا انت صليت فقل الحمد لله رب العالمین ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ترک الجھر بسم اللہ الرحمان الرحیم ص ۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۴ / بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التگیر ص۱۰۳نمبر ۷۴۳ مسلم شریف، باب حجته من قال لا جهر بالبسملة ص۱۷۲ نمبر ۸۹۰٫۳۹۹ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھتے تھے، اور اوپر کی حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پڑھتے تھے تو دونوں حدیثوں کو ملانے کے بعد یہ نتیجہ نکلتا ہے کہ آہستہ پڑھتے تھے۔ (۴) آمین آہستہ کہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ادعوا ربكم تضرعا و خفية انه لا يحب المعتدين. ( آیت ۵۵ سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) آمین دعا ہے اور آیت میں ہے کہ دعا آہستہ کیا کرو اس لئے آمین آہستہ کہنا بہتر ہے۔ (۵) حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن علقمة بن وائل عن ابيه ان النبى الله قرء غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين فقال آمین و خفض بها صوته - ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الامین، ص ۶۹ نمبر ۲۴۸ / دار قطنی ، باب الله مین فی الصلوۃ بعد فاتحته الكتاب والجهر بها، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۸ نمبر ۶ ۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین آہستہ کہنا چاہئے ۔ بخاری مسلم وغیرہ میں
Translation: (415) [11] Recite these things quietly. Explanation: [1] Thana' [2] A'udhu billah [3] Bismillah [4] Rabbana lakal hamd. Recite all four quietly. Proof: (1) The proof for reciting all four quietly is the saying of a tabi'i: from Ibrahim, he said: 'The imam should conceal (recite quietly): Bismillah ir-rahman ir-rahim, and the isti'adhah, and Amin, and Rabbana lakal hamd.' [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abdurrazzaq] This athar shows that a'udhu billah, bismillah, amin, and tahmid should be recited quietly. (2) The proof for reciting bismillah quietly is this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik that he said: 'I prayed behind the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they would begin with 'Alhamdulillahi rabbil alamin', not mentioning 'Bismillah ir-rahman ir-rahim' at the beginning or the end of the recitation.' [Muslim, Bukhari] This hadith indicates that the Prophet and the Companions did not recite bismillah aloud. (3) From Abdullah ibn Mughaffal: he heard his father say... and he said: I prayed with the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and I did not hear any of them say it, so do not say it. When you pray, say 'Alhamdulillahi rabbil alamin'. [Tirmidhi, Bukhari, Muslim] This hadith shows that the Companions did not recite bismillah, and the previous hadith showed that they did recite it, so combining the two hadiths results in the conclusion that they recited it quietly. (4) The proof for saying amin quietly is this verse: 'Call upon your Lord humbly and secretly; indeed, He does not love transgressors.' (Surah al-A'raf, 55) Amin is a supplication, and the verse says to make supplication quietly, so saying amin quietly is better. (5) Also in a hadith: from Alqamah ibn Wail from his father that the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) recited 'not those who have incurred wrath, nor those who have gone astray' and said 'Amin', lowering his voice. [Tirmidhi, Dar Qutni] This hadith shows that amin should be said quietly. [Bukhari, Muslim, etc.]
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof passage about reciting four things quietly in prayer: thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd). The author provides multiple proofs: a saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i) that the imam should recite them quietly; hadith from Anas and Abdullah ibn Mughaffal indicating that the Companions did not recite bismillah aloud, leading to the Hanafi position that it is recited silently; for amin, the Quranic verse 7:55 encouraging quiet supplication, and a hadith where the Prophet lowered his voice when saying amin. The Hanafi school emphasizes reciting these silently, unlike the Shafi'i school which recites bismillah and amin aloud in certain prayers.

Key Terms
الإسرار (al-isrār): Reciting quietly, moving the lips but not audible to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT among the four dhikr to be recited silently?
A) Thana'
B) Ta'awwudh
C) Tasmiyah
D) Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah

Key Takeaway
Reciting thana', ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid silently is a confirmed sunnah in Hanafi prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Silent Recitations in Prayer: Hanafi Position and the Amin Dispute
Rulings and proofs for silent recitations and the Amin dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on silently reciting thana, ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid in prayer, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki argument for reciting Amin aloud.

Core Idea
Thana, ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid are recited silently; Amin is also silent in the Hanafi school, but the dispute is over istihbab, not wujub.

In this lesson, we explore the silent recitations that are part of the sunnah actions of prayer according to the Hanafi school. The passage presents the proofs for reciting thana, ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid silently, and then engages in the well-known dispute over whether Amin should be said silently or aloud. Understanding the reasoning and evidence will help you appreciate the Hanafi methodology and the etiquette of ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four silent recitations
From the passage, list the four recitations that the author says should be recited silently: thana, ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid. Note that the author also includes Amin in the same list, but the dispute is specifically about Amin.
The key terms are defined at the end of the passage.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs for silent recitation
For each of the four, trace the dalil: (1) the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, (2) the hadith of Anas that the Prophet and caliphs did not recite basmalah aloud, (3) the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mughaffal prohibiting basmalah aloud, and (4) the Quranic verse 7:55 and the hadith of Alqamah for Amin. Understand how each proof supports silent recitation.
Note the reconciliation of the two basmalah hadiths: one indicates they recited, the other indicates they did not; the conclusion is they recited silently.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument for Amin
The passage presents their proofs: the hadith of Abu Hurayrah (the Prophet said Amin), the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr (the Prophet extended his voice), and the practice of the Prophet being audible. Notice that the opponents use 'isharat al-nass' (implication) to argue for loud recitation.
The opposing school does not claim a direct explicit text for loudness, but infers it from narrations.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response notes that Abu Hurayrah himself reported that the people later left off saying Amin loudly, and that the Quranic verse instructs secret supplication. The hadith of lowering the voice is more explicit. The dispute is over istihbab, not obligation, so both practices are permissible.
The author's teacher adopted a middle path: intermediate volume.

فصل في سنن الصلوة
فضل اللهم ربنا لک الحمد، ص ۱۲۹، نمبر ۷۹۶ رترندی شریف ، باب آخر و باب ما یقول الرجل اذا رفع راسہ، ص ۷۴ نمبر ۲۶۷) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام مع اللہ من حمدہ کہے اور مقتدی ربنا لک الحمد کہے۔ البتہ منفرد ہو تو چونکہ وہ امام اور مقتدی دونوں ہے اس لئے وہ دونوں کہے گا۔ ترجمه : (۴۱۵) [۱۱] ان سکھوں کو آہستہ پڑھے۔
تشریح : [۱] ثناء [۲] اعوذ بالله [۳] بسم الله [۴] ربنا لک الحمد۔ان چاروں کو آہستہ پڑھے۔

صلى الله
أنه حدثه قال : صليت خلف النبی ا ، و ابي بكر ، وعمر ، وعثمان ، فكانوا يستفتحون بالحمد لله رب العالمين ، لا يذكرون بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، في اول قراءة ، ولا في آخرہ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب حجة من قال لا تجهر بالبسملة ص ۱۶۹، نمبر ۸۹۲۳/۳۹۹ بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التكبیر، ص۱۰۳، نمبر۷۴۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور اور صحابہ بسم اللہ پڑھتے ہی نہیں تھے نہ شروع میں نہ آخر میں۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن مغفل قال سمعنی ابی وانا في الصلوة اقول بسم ا الله الرحمن الرحيم فقال لى اى بنی محدث ایاک و الحدث ... وقال وقد صليت مع النبي الله و مع ابي بكر وعمر ومع عثمان فلم اسمع احدا منهم يقولها فلا تقلها ،اذا انت صليت فقل الحمد لله رب العالمین ۔(ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ترک الجھر بسم اللہ الرحمان الرحیم ص ۵۷، نمبر ۲۴۴ / بخاری شریف، باب ما یقول بعد التگیر ص۱۰۳نمبر ۷۴۳ مسلم شریف، باب حجته من قال لا جهر بالبسملة ص۱۷۲ نمبر ۸۹۰٫۳۹۹ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ بسم اللہ نہیں پڑھتے تھے، اور اوپر کی حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پڑھتے تھے تو دونوں حدیثوں کو ملانے کے بعد یہ نتیجہ نکلتا ہے کہ آہستہ پڑھتے تھے۔ (۴) آمین آہستہ کہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ادعوا ربكم تضرعا و خفية انه لا يحب المعتدين. ( آیت ۵۵ سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) آمین دعا ہے اور آیت میں ہے کہ دعا آہستہ کیا کرو اس لئے آمین آہستہ کہنا بہتر ہے۔ (۵) حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن علقمة بن وائل عن ابيه ان النبى الله قرء غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين فقال آمین و خفض بها صوته - ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الامین، ص ۶۹ نمبر ۲۴۸ / دار قطنی ، باب الله مین فی الصلوۃ بعد فاتحته الكتاب والجهر بها، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۸ نمبر ۶ ۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین آہستہ کہنا چاہئے ۔ بخاری مسلم وغیرہ میں زور سے آمین کہنے کی باضابطہ کوئی حدیث نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ : امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک آمین زور سے کہنا بہتر ہے۔ وہ اس حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں (اگر چہ اس میں زور کا لفظ نہیں ہے ) حدیث یہ ہے۔ (۱) عن ابي هريرة ان النبى الله قال : اذا امن الامام فأمنوا فانه من وافق تأميـنـه تـأمين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه وقال ابن شهاب وكان رسول الله الله يقول آمين (بخاری شریف، باب جبر الامام بالتا مین بص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۷۸۰ مسلم شریف ، باب التسميع والتحميد والتاه مین ص۱۷۴، نمبر ۹۱۵/۴۱۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور آمین کہتے تھے، زور سے کہتے ہو نگے تب ہی تو راوی نے سنا ہوگا ، اسلئے اس حدیث کے اشارۃ النص سے زور سے آمین کہنا ثابت ہوا۔ (۲) عن وائل بن حجر قال سمعت النبي الله قرأ غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين وقال آمین و مد بها صوته - ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی التأمین ، ص ۶۹ نمبر ۲۴۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آمین زور سے کہا۔ (۳) اس حدیث میں زور سے آمین کہنے کی صراحت ہے۔ لیکن یہ بھی ساتھ ہی ہے کہ صحابہ نے زور سے آمین کہنا چھوڑ دیا تھا۔ عن ابي هريرة قال ترك الناس التأمين ، وكان رسول الله اذا قال غير المغضوب عليهم ولا الضالين قال آمين حتى يسمعها اهل الصف الاول فيرتج بها المسجد. (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب انھر بآمین، ج ۱۲۱، نمبر ۸۵۳/دار قطنی ، باب الامین فی الصلوۃ، ج اول ص ۱۳۲۸، نمبر ۱۲۵۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آمین زور سے کہنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن خود ابو ہریرہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صحابہ نے زور سے آمین کہنا چھوڑ دیا تھا۔ اسی حدیث میں اوپر آیا عن ابي هريرة قال ترک الناس التأمين
نوٹ : یہ استحباب کا اختلاف ہے۔ کوئی زور سے آمین کہتا ہو تو اس پر نکیر نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ میرے استاذ حضرت مولانا انظر شاہ صاحب کشمیری کو دیکھا کہ وہ زور اور آہستہ کے درمیان میں آمین کہتے ، جس سے صرف بغل والے سن لیتے تھے ۔ تا کہ دونوں حدیثوں پر عمل ہو جائے۔ ناچیز بھی یہی کرتا ہے۔
لغت ثاء: سبحانک اللھم ، الخ کو نا کہتے ہیں۔ تعوذ: اعوذ بالله م الشیطان الرجیم تسمیۃ : بسم الله ارحمن الرحيم تحمید: ربنا لک الحمد
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Prayer. Virtue: 'O Allah, our Lord, to You is all praise' (reference: Tirmidhi, page 129, number 796, another chapter and chapter on what a man says when he raises his head, page 74, number 267). From this it is understood that the Imam says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'. However, if one is praying alone, since he is both Imam and follower, he will say both. Translation: (415) [11] He should recite these silently. Explanation: [1] Thana [2] Ta'awwudh [3] Basmalah [4] Tahmid. He should recite all four silently. Proof: (1) The proof for reciting all four silently is this saying of a Tabi'i: From Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i) who said: The Imam should recite silently: Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, al-Isti'adha, Amin, and Rabbana lakal hamd. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ... / Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, ...) From this athar it is understood that Ta'awwudh, Basmalah, Amin, and Tahmid should be recited silently. (2) Recite Basmalah silently: The proof is this hadith: From Anas ibn Malik ... that he prayed behind the Prophet, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they would begin with 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabb al-'Alamin', not mentioning Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim at the beginning or end of the recitation. (Muslim, ... / Bukhari, ...) This hadith indicates that the Prophet and the Companions did not recite Basmalah at all, neither at the beginning nor the end. (3) From Abdullah ibn Mughaffal: He said my father heard me while I was in prayer saying Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim and he said to me: O my son, it is an innovation, beware of innovation... and he said: I prayed with the Prophet, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and I did not hear any of them say it, so do not say it. When you pray, say 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabb al-'Alamin'. (Tirmidhi, ... / Bukhari, ... / Muslim, ...) From this hadith it is understood that the Companions did not recite Basmalah. And from the previous hadith it is understood that they did recite, so combining the two hadiths leads to the conclusion that they recited it silently. (4) Recite Amin silently: The proof is this verse: 'Call upon your Lord humbly and secretly; indeed, He does not love transgressors.' (Surah al-A'raf, verse 55) Amin is a supplication, and the verse says to make supplication secretly, so reciting Amin silently is better. (5) There is also a hadith: From Alqamah ibn Wa'il from his father that the Prophet recited 'Ghayri al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin' and said Amin, lowering his voice. (Tirmidhi, ... / Dar Qutni, ...) This hadith indicates that Amin should be recited silently. There is no explicit hadith in Bukhari or Muslim about reciting Amin loudly. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik consider reciting Amin loudly better. They argue with this hadith (although it does not contain the word 'loudly'): (1) From Abu Hurayrah that the Prophet said: 'When the Imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins are forgiven.' Ibn Shihab said: The Messenger of Allah used to say Amin. (Bukhari, ... / Muslim, ...) This hadith indicates that the Prophet used to say Amin; had it not been loud, the narrator would not have heard it, so by 'isharat al-nass' (implication of the text) reciting Amin loudly is proven. (2) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I heard the Prophet recite 'Ghayri al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin' and say Amin, extending his voice. (Tirmidhi, ...) This hadith indicates that Amin was said loudly. (3) This hadith explicitly states reciting Amin loudly. But there is also the fact that the Companions stopped reciting Amin loudly. From Abu Hurayrah: The people left off saying Amin, and the Messenger of Allah, when he said 'Ghayri al-maghdubi 'alayhim wa la al-dallin', would say Amin so that those in the first row could hear him, and the mosque would reverberate. (Ibn Majah, ... / Dar Qutni, ...) This hadith indicates that Amin should be recited loudly. But Abu Hurayrah himself says that the Companions left off saying Amin loudly. In the same hadith it comes: From Abu Hurayrah: The people left off saying Amin. Note: This is a difference of istihbab (recommendation). One should not criticize someone who says Amin loudly. I saw my teacher, Hadrat Mawlana Anzar Shah Kashmiri, that he would say Amin between loud and silent, so that only those next to him could hear, in order to act upon both hadiths. This humble one also does the same. Vocabulary: Thana: 'Subhanakallahumma...' etc. is called 'thana'. Ta'awwudh: 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Tasmiyah: 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. Tahmid: 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute presented in the context of explaining the sunnah actions of prayer. The author, Shaykh Ahmad Ya'qub, begins by listing four silent recitations: thana (the opening supplication), ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), basmalah (Bismillah), and tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd). He provides multiple proofs from the sayings of the Tabi'un and hadith to establish that these are recited silently in the Hanafi school. The proofs include an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, hadith from Anas ibn Malik and Abdullah ibn Mughaffal, and the Quranic verse on supplicating secretly. For Basmalah, the author reconciles apparently contradictory hadith by concluding that the Companions recited it silently. For Amin, he presents the Hanafi position (silent) with Quran and hadith evidence, then presents the Shafi'i/Maliki position (loud) with their proofs, including the hadith of Abu Hurayrah and the practice of the Prophet as heard by the companions. The author notes that the dispute is over istihbab (recommendation) and not obligation, and he relates the practice of his teacher Mawlana Anzar Shah Kashmiri, who said Amin at an intermediate volume to act on both sets of hadith. The author adopts this middle course. The passage concludes with a vocabulary list defining the key terms. This exemplifies the Hanafi methodology of preferring silent recitations while acknowledging valid scholarly difference on Amin.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication in prayer, specifically 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika...'
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited before Quran recitation.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'
تحمید (tahmid): The phrase 'Rabbana lakal hamd' said after rising from ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Only Basmalah and Tahmid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers silent recitation of thana, ta'awwudh, basmalah, and tahmid in prayer, and the dispute over Amin is a legitimate difference of istihbab, not wujub, so mutual respect is mandatory.

Standing Straight During Takbir Tahrimah
Ruling and proof for standing upright during opening takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on posture during the takbir tahrimah and identify the proof from the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi.

Core Idea
Standing straight during the opening takbir is a sunnah muakkadah; the Prophet's practice shows no head-lowering.

In this lesson, we examine the twelfth sunnah of prayer: standing upright without lowering the head when beginning salah. The source passage provides both the ruling and its proof from a well-known hadith. Understanding this clarifies the recommended posture and distinguishes it from obligatory actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the posture of the body when saying the opening takbir (tahrimah). The ruling is that it is a sunnah muakkadah to stand completely upright without lowering the head.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi from Tirmidhi and Nasa'i. The hadith describes the Prophet's posture when starting prayer.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), but it is widely accepted.
3
Derive the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'i'tadal qa'iman' (stood upright) implies an erect stance without bowing. Raising hands to shoulder level further suggests no head-lowering.
4
Note the Hanafi position
Hanafis classify this as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. Omitting it does not invalidate the prayer, but it is a loss of reward.
All schools agree on its desirability.
5
Apply the lesson
When performing takbir tahrimah, ensure the spine is straight and the head is not bent forward. This applies to both imam and follower.

Source Text

تشریح : تحریمہ کے وقت بالکل سیدھا کھڑا ہواور تکبیر کہے،سر جھکا ہوا نہ ہو۔

Translation: (416) (12) To stand straight without lowering the head at the time of tahrimah (opening takbir). Explanation: At the time of tahrimah, one should stand completely straight and say the takbir, not with the head lowered. Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling with proof. It states the twelfth sunnah of prayer (according to the author's numbering): that one should stand up straight without bowing the head when saying the opening takbir (tahrimah). The explanation clarifies that the posture should be erect. The proof is a hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, a companion known for describing the Prophet's prayer before a group of companions. The hadith states that when the Prophet stood for prayer, he would stand upright (i'tidal qa'iman) and raise his hands to shoulder level. This indicates that the head is not lowered because lowering the head would contradict uprightness. The hadith is used as evidence for both the straight posture and the hand-raising. The Hanafi school considers this sunnah (recommended) rather than obligatory; one who omits it does not need to repeat the prayer. The text cuts off at 'In this hadith...' likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer.
اعتدال (i'tidal): Upright posture, standing straight without leaning or bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Standing upright without lowering the head during takbir tahrimah is a confirmed sunnah from the Prophet's practice.

Salah — Prayer

Sunnah of Standing Straight at Takbir and the Dispute on Audible Ameen
First sunnah of prayer with an excursus on saying Ameen aloud in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah regarding posture at takbirat al-ihram, explain the proof from the hadith of Abu Humaid, and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i/Maliki positions on saying Ameen aloud, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Stand straight at takbir; say Ameen quietly — the difference is one of recommendation, not obligation.

This lesson examines two aspects of prayer mechanics. First, we learn the sunnah of standing upright at the opening takbir, supported by a clear hadith. Then, we explore a long-standing inter-madhhab dispute: should the imam say Ameen aloud or quietly? The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Companions, recommends the quiet recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah and its ruling
The passage begins by stating that standing straight without bowing the head is from the sunnah of prayer. Determine the hukm level (e.g., sunnah muakkadah, not fard) based on the author's classification.
The matn from Nur al-Idah uses 'al-i'tidal' which implies uprightness.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi. Find the exact wording in the passage and note that it describes the Prophet standing straight when rising for prayer.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The key term 'i'tadala' means to be straight and upright. How does this prove that bowing the head at takbir is contrary to the sunnah?
If head bowing were allowed, the hadith would not emphasize uprightness; its absence implies prohibition of head bowing.
4
Identify the inter-madhhab dispute on Ameen
The author presents the view of Shafi'i and Maliki who say loud Ameen is better, citing three hadiths. Then he shows the Hanafi proof: the Companions abandoned loud Ameen as reported by Abu Huraira. Contrast the evidence.
Note that the author categorizes this as a difference of istihbab (recommendation), not obligation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school considers the quiet practice as the established sunnah, based on the Companions' consistency. The author records his teacher's moderate voice as a compromise. Determine the mufta bihi position.
Mufta bihi: quiet Ameen. The author warns against criticizing those who say it aloud.

وجه : عن ابي حميد الساعدى قال سمعت و هو في عشرة من أصحاب النبي علم .... فقال كان رسول الله الله اذا قام الى الصلوة اعتدل قائماو رفع يديه حتى يحاذى بهما منكبيه ( ترمذی شریف، باب منه،( ای ماجاء فی وصف الصلوة ) ص۸۲، نمبر ۳۰۴ رنسائی شریف، باب الاعتدال فی الرکوع ،ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۱۰۴۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سر جھکا کر نہ کھڑے ہو۔
Section on the Sunnahs of Prayer. (41) And standing straight at the time of the takbirat al-ihram without bowing the head. There is no well-established hadith for saying Ameen loudly. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, saying Ameen loudly is better. They argue from this hadith (although the word 'loudly' is not in it): (1) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: 'When the imam says Ameen, then say Ameen, for whoever's Ameen coincides with the Ameen of the angels will have his previous sins forgiven.' Ibn Shihab said: 'The Messenger of Allah used to say Ameen.' This hadith indicates that the Prophet said Ameen, and the narrator heard it, so it proves saying Ameen loudly by textual indication. (2) From Wa'il ibn Hujr: I heard the Prophet recite 'Ghair al-maghdubi alayhim wa la al-dallin' and say Ameen, lengthening his voice. This hadith explicitly mentions loud Ameen. (3) This hadith clearly states loud Ameen. But along with this, it also says that the Companions abandoned loud Ameen. From Abu Huraira: The people abandoned the Ameen, while the Prophet, when he said 'Ghair al-maghdubi alayhim wa la al-dallin', used to say Ameen loud enough for the people in the first row to hear, and the mosque would reverberate with it. This hadith shows that loud Ameen should be said. But Abu Huraira himself says the Companions abandoned loud Ameen. Note: This is a difference of recommendation. One should not criticize someone who says Ameen loudly. I saw my teacher Maulana Anzar Shah Kashmiri saying Ameen in a moderate voice such that only those beside him could hear, so as to act upon both hadiths. I also do the same. Lexicon: Tha': 'Subhanaka Allahumma' etc. are said softly. Ta'awwudh: 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'. Tasmiyah: 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'. Tahmid: 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'. Translation: (416) (12) Standing straight without bowing the head at the time of takbirat al-ihram. Explanation: At the time of takbir, stand completely straight and say the takbir, not with head bowed. Proof: From Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi: He said, while in the company of ten of the Prophet's companions, they said: The Messenger of Allah, when he stood for prayer, stood straight and raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders. (Tirmidhi, chapter from that, p.82, no.304; Nasa'i, chapter on moderation in bowing, p.118, no.1040). This hadith indicates that he did not stand with head bowed.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a composite lesson: it first states the sunnah of standing straight during takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir) without bowing the head, then tangentially discusses the ruling of saying Ameen aloud in prayer, before returning to the proof for standing straight. The author begins by citing the matn from Nur al-Idah: 'al-I'tidal 'inda al-tahrimah min ghayri tat'ati al-ra's' – standing upright at the takbir without lowering the head. He then immediately diverges into a benefit (fa'idah) about saying Ameen loudly. He notes that the Shafi'i and Maliki schools prefer saying Ameen aloud and cite three hadiths: (1) the command to say Ameen with the imam, (2) the report that the Prophet lengthened his voice with Ameen, and (3) the report that the mosque reverberated with Ameen. The author notes that the first hadith does not mention volume; the second and third do. However, he also reports that Abu Huraira said 'the people abandoned the Ameen,' indicating that after the Prophet's time the practice of loud Ameen was discontinued. The author then categorizes this as a difference of istihbab (recommendation), not obligation, and records his teacher's practice of a moderate voice to harmonize the positions. After this excursus, he returns to the main topic with the translation and explanation of the sunnah of standing straight. He provides proof from the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi, which explicitly states that the Prophet would stand straight when starting prayer. The passage thus serves both as a ruling with proof and as a documentation of an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that saying Ameen softly is preferred, but the author does not assert this forcefully; he merely reports the difference and advocates tolerance.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer (takbirat al-ihram) which makes certain things prohibited (haram) during prayer.
طأطأة الرأس (tat'at al-ra's): Bowing or lowering the head; here it means not looking down or bending the neck at the start of prayer.
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'Ameen' after the recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the imam saying Ameen aloud during prayer?
A) It is wajib to say it loudly.
B) It is sunnah to say it loudly.
C) It is sunnah to say it quietly.
D) It is haram to say it aloud.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of prayer includes standing upright at takbir and saying Ameen quietly, with the dispute on Ameen volume being a matter of recommendation, not obligation.
